## 第一部分

*（Being a reprint from the Reminiscences of JOHN H. WATSON, M.D., Late of the Army Medical Department.）*

*（节选自约翰·H·华生医学博士的回忆录，前陆军军医处军医。）*

---

### 第一章 歇洛克·福尔摩斯先生
### CHAPTER I. MR. SHERLOCK HOLMES.

---

**In the year 1878** 一八七八年，

**I took my degree of Doctor of Medicine** 我拿到了医学博士学位。

**of the University of London,** 什么的学位？→ 伦敦大学的。

**and proceeded to Netley** → 然后前往内特利，

**to go through the course** 去干什么？→ 去完成一门课程。

**prescribed for surgeons in the army.** 什么样的课程？→ 为陆军外科军医规定的那种课程。

**Having completed my studies there,** [分词-句首状语] 在那里完成学业之后 → 这是在说背景状态，接下来我怎么样了？→

**I was duly attached to the Fifth Northumberland Fusiliers** 我被正式编入了诺森伯兰第五燧发枪团，

**as Assistant Surgeon.** 作为什么身份？→ 担任助理军医。

**The regiment was stationed in India at the time,** 当时团队驻扎在印度，

**and before I could join it,** 而在我能赶到之前，

**the second Afghan war had broken out.** 第二次阿富汗战争已经爆发了。

**On landing at Bombay,** 在孟买登陆时，

**I learned** 我得知——

**that my corps had advanced through the passes,** 我的部队已经穿过了山口，

**and was already deep in the enemy's country.** 而且已经深入了敌人的腹地。

**I followed, however,** 不过我还是跟了上去，

**with many other officers** 和许多其他军官一起。

**who were in the same situation as myself,** [定从-句尾补充] 所谓这些军官，就是跟我处境相同的那些。

**and succeeded in reaching Candahar in safety,** → 成功地平安到达了坎大哈，

**where I found my regiment,** [定从-句尾补充] 在那里我找到了我的团队，

**and at once entered upon my new duties.** → 然后立刻投入了新的职责。

---

**The campaign brought honours and promotion to many,** 这场战役给许多人带来了荣誉和晋升，

**but for me** 【转折】但是对我来说，

**it had nothing but misfortune and disaster.** 除了厄运和灾难，什么也没有。

**I was removed from my brigade** 我被调离了原来的旅，

**and attached to the Berkshires,** → 编入了伯克郡团。

**with whom I served at the fatal battle of Maiwand.** [定从-句尾补充] 我随他们参加了迈旺德那场惨烈的战役。

**There I was struck on the shoulder** 在那里，我的肩膀被击中了。

**by a Jezail bullet,** 被什么击中？→ 被一颗杰扎尔枪子弹。

**which shattered the bone** [定从-句尾补充] 所谓这颗子弹，打碎了骨头，

**and grazed the subclavian artery.** → 还擦伤了锁骨下动脉。

**I should have fallen** 【假设情况】我本来就会落入——

**into the hands** → 落入手中——

**of the murderous Ghazis** → 那些凶残的加齐人的手中——

**had it not been for the devotion and courage** 【实际情况】要不是那份忠诚和勇气。

**shown by Murray, my orderly,** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的忠诚和勇气？→ 由默里表现出来的。所谓默里，就是我的勤务兵。

**who threw me across a pack-horse,** [定从-句尾补充] 他把我扔上了一匹驮马，

**and succeeded in bringing me safely to the British lines.** → 成功地把我安全带回了英军阵线。

---

**Worn with pain,** [分词-句首状语] 被疼痛折磨着，→ 这是在说我的状态，

**and weak from the prolonged hardships** 又因为长期的苦难而虚弱不堪。

**which I had undergone,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的苦难？→ 我所经历的那些。

← 在这种状态下，我怎么样了？→

**I was removed,** 我被转移了。

**with a great train of wounded sufferers,** 和一大批伤员一起。

**to the base hospital at Peshawar.** 转移到哪？→ 到白沙瓦的后方医院。

**Here I rallied,** 在这里我渐渐恢复了，

**and had already improved so far** → 而且已经好到了这种程度——

**as to be able to walk about the wards,** 好到什么程度？→ 好到能在病房里走动了，

**and even to bask a little upon the verandah,** → 甚至能在走廊上晒晒太阳了，

**when I was struck down by enteric fever,** 【情境】落地，进入【转折】→ 这时候，我又被肠热症击倒了。

**that curse of our Indian possessions.** [同位语] 所谓肠热症，就是我们在印度属地的一大祸害。

**For months my life was despaired of,** 好几个月，人们都觉得我活不成了。

**and when at last I came to myself** 【情境】等到我终于清醒过来，

**and became convalescent,** → 开始恢复时，

**I was so weak and emaciated** 【情境】落地 → 我已经虚弱憔悴到——

**that a medical board determined** 到什么程度？→ 以至于一个医疗委员会判定——

**that not a day should be lost** 判定什么？→ 一天也不能耽搁，

**in sending me back to England.** 在做什么上不能耽搁？→ 在把我送回英格兰这件事上。

**I was dispatched, accordingly,** 于是我就被派遣出发了，

**in the troopship "Orontes,"** 在哪？→ 在运兵船"奥隆提斯号"上，

**and landed a month later** → 一个月后登陆了，

**on Portsmouth jetty,** 在哪登陆？→ 在朴茨茅斯码头。

**with my health irretrievably ruined,** [with-描述状态] 带着什么状态？→ 我的健康已经无可挽回地毁了，

**but with permission from a paternal government** 【转折】但是还带着什么？→ 带着政府的一份体恤的许可，

**to spend the next nine months** 许可做什么？→ 花接下来九个月的时间，

**in attempting to improve it.** 花在什么上？→ 试图恢复健康。

---

**I had neither kith nor kin in England,** 在英格兰，我既没有亲人也没有朋友，

**and was therefore as free as air** 因此就像空气一样自由——

**—or as free as an income** 或者说，自由程度相当于一份收入——

**of eleven shillings and sixpence a day** → 每天十一先令六便士那样微薄——

**will permit a man to be.** 所能允许一个人那样自由。

**Under such circumstances,** 在这种情况下，

**I naturally gravitated to London,** 我自然而然地被吸引到了伦敦。

**that great cesspool** [同位语] 所谓伦敦，就是那个巨大的污水池，

**into which all the loungers and idlers of the Empire** 帝国所有的闲人和游荡者，

**are irresistibly drained.** 都被不可抗拒地冲进这里。

**There I stayed for some time** 我在那里住了一段时间，

**at a private hotel in the Strand,** 在哪住？→ 在河滨大道的一家私人旅馆，

**leading a comfortless, meaningless existence,** [分词-句末伴随] 过着怎样的生活？→ 既不舒适也毫无意义，

**and spending such money as I had,** → 花着我仅有的钱，

**considerably more freely than I ought.** 花得怎么样？→ 比应该的要大手大脚得多。

**So alarming did the state of my finances become,** 我的财务状况变得如此令人担忧，

**that I soon realized** 以至于我很快就意识到了——

**that I must either leave the metropolis** 意识到什么？→ 我要么必须离开这座大都市，

**and rusticate somewhere in the country,** → 去乡下找个地方隐居，

**or that I must make** → 要么就必须做出——

**a complete alteration** → 彻底的改变，

**in my style of living.** → 改变我整个生活方式。

**Choosing the latter alternative,** [分词-句首状语] 选择了后者之后 →

**I began by making up my mind** → 我先是下定了决心——

**to leave the hotel,** → 离开旅馆，

**and to take up my quarters** → 然后找个住处，

**in some less pretentious and less expensive domicile.** 什么样的住处？→ 不那么讲究、也不那么贵的地方。

---

**On the very day** 【情境】就在那一天，

**that I had come to this conclusion,** → 就在我做出这个决定的那一天，

**I was standing at the Criterion Bar,** 【情境】我正站在克莱特里恩酒吧，

**when some one tapped me on the shoulder,** 【情境】落地，进入【转折】→ 这时候有人拍了拍我的肩膀，

**and turning round** → 我转过身来，

**I recognized young Stamford,** 认出了年轻的斯坦福德。

**who had been a dresser under me at Barts.** [定从-句尾补充] 所谓斯坦福德，就是以前在巴茨医院时在我手下当过实习生的那个人。

**The sight of a friendly face** 看到一张友好的面孔，

**in the great wilderness of London** 在哪？→ 在伦敦这片偌大的荒野中，

**is a pleasant thing indeed** 确实是一件愉快的事，

**to a lonely man.** 对谁来说？→ 对于一个孤身一人的人。

**In old days** 从前，

**Stamford had never been** 斯坦福德从来算不上——

**a particular crony of mine,** → 我的密友，

**but now I hailed him with enthusiasm,** 【转折】但现在我热情地招呼他，

**and he,** → 而他呢，

**in his turn,** [插入修饰-逗号隔开] 换到他，

**appeared to be delighted to see me.** → 看起来见到我也很高兴。

**In the exuberance of my joy,** 在我满溢的喜悦之中，

**I asked him to lunch with me at the Holborn,** 我邀请他到霍尔本餐厅跟我一起吃午饭，

**and we started off together in a hansom.** → 于是我们一起坐上一辆双轮马车出发了。

---

**"Whatever have you been doing with yourself, Watson?"** "华生，你这些日子到底经历了什么？"

**he asked in undisguised wonder,** 他带着毫不掩饰的惊讶问道，

**as we rattled through the crowded London streets.** 【情境】当我们的马车颠簸着驶过拥挤的伦敦街头时。

**"You are as thin as a lath** "你瘦得跟木板条似的，

**and as brown as a nut."** → 黑得跟个核桃一样。"

---

**I gave him a short sketch of my adventures,** 我简单地给他讲了讲我的经历，

**and had hardly concluded it** → 还没怎么说完，

**by the time that we reached our destination.** 我们就到了目的地。

---

**"Poor devil!" he said, commiseratingly,** "可怜的家伙！"他同情地说，

**after he had listened to my misfortunes.** 在听完我的遭遇之后。

**"What are you up to now?"** "你现在打算干什么？"

---

**"Looking for lodgings," I answered.** "找住处，"我回答。

**"Trying to solve the problem** "想解决一个问题：

**as to whether it is possible** 什么问题？→ 关于是否可能——

**to get comfortable rooms at a reasonable price."** 用合理的价钱找到舒适的房间。"

---

**"That's a strange thing," remarked my companion;** "这可真巧了，"我的同伴说，

**"you are the second man to-day** "你是今天第二个人，

**that has used that expression to me."** [定从-句尾补充] 第二个跟我说这话的人。"

---

**"And who was the first?" I asked.** "第一个是谁？"我问。

---

**"A fellow** "一个家伙，

**who is working at the chemical laboratory** [定从-句尾补充] 所谓这个家伙，就是在化学实验室工作的那个。

**up at the hospital.** 在哪？→ 在医院那边。

**He was bemoaning himself this morning** 他今天早上还在抱怨，

**because he could not get someone** 【原因】因为什么？→ 因为他找不到一个人，

**to go halves with him** 找人干什么？→ 来跟他合租分摊，

**in some nice rooms** 分摊什么？→ 一些不错的房间。

**which he had found,** [定从-句尾补充] 所谓这些房间，就是他找到的那种。

**and which were too much for his purse."** [并列 which] 而且这些房间还怎么样？→ 对他的钱包来说太贵了。"

---

**"By Jove!" I cried,** "天哪！"我叫道，

**"if he really wants someone** "如果他真的想找个人，

**to share the rooms and the expense,** 来分享房间和费用，

**I am the very man for him.** 那我就是最合适的人选。

**I should prefer having a partner to being alone."** 比起一个人住，我更愿意有个室友。"

---

**Young Stamford looked rather strangely at me** 年轻的斯坦福德有些奇怪地看着我，

**over his wine-glass.** 隔着他的酒杯。

**"You don't know Sherlock Holmes yet," he said;** "你还不了解歇洛克·福尔摩斯，"他说，

**"perhaps you would not care for him** "也许你不会愿意要他——

**as a constant companion."** → 做你的长期伴侣。"

---

**"Why, what is there against him?"** "怎么了，他有什么不好？"

---

**"Oh, I didn't say there was anything against him.** "哦，我并没说他有什么不好。

**He is a little queer in his ideas** 他的想法有些古怪——

**—an enthusiast in some branches of science.** [同位语] 在某些科学分支上算是个狂热分子。

**As far as I know** 据我所知，

**he is a decent fellow enough."** 他人还是相当不错的。"

---

**"A medical student, I suppose?" said I.** "我猜是个医学生？"我说。

---

**"No—I have no idea** "不——我根本不知道

**what he intends to go in for.** 他想从事什么行业。

**I believe he is well up in anatomy,** 我知道他精通解剖学，

**and he is a first-class chemist;** → 化学也是一流的；

**but, as far as I know,** 【转折】但据我所知，

**he has never taken out any systematic medical classes.** 他从来没有系统地上过什么医学课程。

**His studies are very desultory and eccentric,** 他的研究非常零散、非常古怪，

**but he has amassed a lot of out-of-the-way knowledge** 【转折】但他积累了大量冷门知识，

**which would astonish his professors."** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的知识？→ 足以让教授们大吃一惊的那种。"

---

**"Did you never ask him** "你从来没问过他——

**what he was going in for?"** → 他想往哪个方向发展吗？"

**I asked.** 我问。

---

**"No; he is not a man** "没有。他这个人

**that it is easy to draw out,** [定从-句尾补充] 不是容易套出话来的那种人，

**though he can be communicative enough** 【让步】虽然他也能侃侃而谈——

**when the fancy seizes him."** 【情境】当他兴致来了的时候。"

---

**"I should like to meet him," I said.** "我倒想见见他，"我说。

**"If I am to lodge with anyone,** 【条件】如果我要跟人合住的话，

**I should prefer a man of studious and quiet habits.** 【结果】我更希望对方是个爱学习、性格安静的人。

**I am not strong enough yet** 我现在身体还不够结实，

**to stand much noise or excitement.** 不够结实到什么程度？→ 受不了太多的吵闹和刺激。

**I had enough of both in Afghanistan** 在阿富汗我经历的那些，

**to last me for the remainder of my natural existence.** 够我这辈子受的了。

**How could I meet this friend of yours?"** 你的这位朋友，我怎么才能见到他？"

---

**"He is sure to be at the laboratory,"** "他肯定在实验室，"

**returned my companion.** 我的同伴回答。

**"He either avoids the place for weeks,** "他要么一连好几个星期不去那儿，

**or else he works there from morning to night.** 【选项B】要么就从早到晚泡在那里。

**If you like,** 【条件】如果你愿意的话，

**we shall drive round together after luncheon."** 【结果】我们吃完午饭一起过去。"

---

**"Certainly," I answered,** "当然好，"我答道，

**and the conversation drifted away into other channels.** → 话题随即转向了其他方面。

---

**As we made our way to the hospital** 【情境】当我们朝医院走去时，

**after leaving the Holborn,** 在什么之后？→ 离开霍尔本餐厅之后，

**Stamford gave me a few more particulars** 斯坦福德又跟我多介绍了一些细节，

**about the gentleman** 关于谁的？→ 关于那位先生的，

**whom I proposed to take as a fellow-lodger.** [定从-句尾补充] 所谓那位先生，就是我打算合租的那个人。

---

**"You mustn't blame me** "如果你跟他合不来，可别怪我，"

**if you don't get on with him," he said;** 他说，

**"I know nothing more of him** "我对他所知的，

**than I have learned** → 也不比这多——

**from meeting him occasionally** → 不过是偶尔碰到时知道的那点——

**in the laboratory.** → 在实验室里碰到时。

**You proposed this arrangement,** 是你提出这个安排的，

**so you must not hold me responsible."** 所以你不能让我负责。"

---

**"If we don't get on** 【条件】如果我们合不来的话，

**it will be easy to part company," I answered.** 【结果】分开就是了，"我回答。

**"It seems to me, Stamford," I added,** "斯坦福德，我觉得，"我补充道，

**looking hard at my companion,** [分词-句末伴随] 紧盯着我的同伴，

**"that you have some reason** "你好像有什么理由，

**for washing your hands of the matter.** 什么理由？→ 想撇清此事的理由。

**Is this fellow's temper so formidable, or what is it?** 这位仁兄的脾气很可怕吗？还是怎么回事？

**Don't be mealy-mouthed about it."** 别吞吞吐吐的。"

---

**"It is not easy** "这不容易——

**to express the inexpressible,"** → 没法表达的东西就是没法表达，"

**he answered with a laugh.** 他笑着回答。

**"Holmes is a little too scientific for my tastes** "福尔摩斯在科学上有点太较真了，超出了我的口味——

**—it approaches to cold-bloodedness.** → 简直有点冷血。

**I could imagine his giving a friend a little pinch** 我能想象他会给朋友来一小撮——

**of the latest vegetable alkaloid,** 一小撮什么？→ 最新的植物生物碱，

**not out of malevolence, you understand,** 别误会，不是出于恶意，

**but simply out of a spirit of inquiry** 【转折】而纯粹是出于探究精神，

**in order to have an accurate idea of the effects.** 【目的】为了什么？→ 为了准确了解一下效果。

**To do him justice,** 公平地说，

**I think that he would take it himself** → 我觉得他自己也会吞下去的——

**with the same readiness.** → 同样干脆利落地。

**He appears to have a passion** 他似乎有一种热情——

**for definite and exact knowledge."** 对什么的热情？→ 对精确而确定的知识。"

---

**"Very right too."** "这也没什么不对。"

---

**"Yes, but it may be pushed to excess.** "没错，【转折】但凡事过度就不好了。

**When it comes to beating the subjects** 【情境】当他去敲打实验体时——

**in the dissecting-rooms with a stick,** → 在解剖室里，用棍子，

**it is certainly taking rather a bizarre shape."** 事情就变得相当古怪了。"

---

**"Beating the subjects!"** "敲打尸体！"

---

**"Yes, to verify** "是的，为了验证

**how far bruises may be produced after death.** 验证什么？→ 人死后还能产生多少淤青。

**I saw him at it with my own eyes."** 我亲眼看见过。"

---

**"And yet you say he is not a medical student?"** "可你又说他不是医学生？"

---

**"No. Heaven knows** "不是。天知道

**what the objects of his studies are.** 他研究的目的是什么。

**But here we are,** 不过我们到了，

**and you must form your own impressions about him."** → 你自己去了解他吧。"

**As he spoke,** 他说着，

**we turned down a narrow lane** 我们拐进一条窄巷，

**and passed through a small side-door,** → 穿过一扇小侧门，

**which opened into a wing of the great hospital.** [定从-句尾补充] 这扇门通往这所大医院的一个侧翼。

**It was familiar ground to me,** 这地方我很熟悉，

**and I needed no guiding** → 不用人领路。

**as we ascended the bleak stone staircase** 【情境】我们沿着阴冷的石阶拾级而上，

**and made our way down the long corridor** → 走过长长的走廊，

**with its vista of whitewashed wall and dun-coloured doors.** [with-描述特点] 走廊两侧是什么样的？→ 刷白的墙壁和灰褐色的门。

**Near the further end** 在走廊尽头附近，

**a low arched passage branched away from it** 一条低矮的拱形通道从走廊岔开，

**and led to the chemical laboratory.** → 通往化学实验室。

---

**This was a lofty chamber,** 这是一间高大的房间，

**lined and littered with countless bottles.** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的房间？→ 四壁排满了、到处散落着无数瓶瓶罐罐。

**Broad, low tables were scattered about,** 宽大的矮桌散布其间，

**which bristled with retorts, test-tubes, and little Bunsen lamps,** [定从-句尾补充] 这些桌子上怎么样？→ 竖着密密麻麻的蒸馏瓶、试管和小小的本生灯，

**with their blue flickering flames.** [with-描述特点] 本生灯什么样？→ 蓝色的火苗闪烁跳动。

**There was only one student in the room,** 房间里只有一个人，

**who was bending over a distant table** [定从-句尾补充] 正俯身在远处的桌子上，

**absorbed in his work.** [分词-后置修饰] 全神贯注地工作着。

**At the sound of our steps** 听到我们的脚步声，

**he glanced round** 他抬头看了一眼，

**and sprang to his feet with a cry of pleasure.** → 随即跳了起来，发出一声欢呼。

**"I've found it! I've found it,"** "我找到了！我找到了！"

**he shouted to my companion,** 他朝着我的同伴喊道，

**running towards us with a test-tube in his hand.** [分词-句末伴随] 一边跑向我们，手里拿着一根试管。

**"I have found a re-agent** "我发现了一种试剂，

**which is precipitated by hæmoglobin,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的试剂？→ 能被血红蛋白沉淀的，

**and by nothing else."** → 而且只有血红蛋白能让它沉淀。"

**Had he discovered a gold mine,** 【假设情况】就算他发现了一座金矿，

**greater delight could not have shone upon his features.** 【实际情况】脸上也不会比现在更光彩照人。

---

**"Dr. Watson, Mr. Sherlock Holmes," said Stamford, introducing us.** "华生医生，这位是歇洛克·福尔摩斯先生，"斯坦福德为我们做了介绍。

---

**"How are you?" he said cordially,** "你好，"他热情地说，

**gripping my hand with a strength** [分词-句末伴随] 紧紧握住我的手，力道——

**for which I should hardly have given him credit.** 什么样的力道？→ 我简直想不到他会有那么大的力气。

**"You have been in Afghanistan, I perceive."** "你从阿富汗回来的吧。"

---

**"How on earth did you know that?"** "你到底怎么知道的？"

**I asked in astonishment.** 我大为吃惊地问。

---

**"Never mind," said he, chuckling to himself.** "别在意，"他咯咯笑着自言自语。

**"The question now is about hæmoglobin.** "现在的问题是血红蛋白。

**No doubt you see the significance** 你一定看出了其中的重要性——

**of this discovery of mine?"** → 我这个发现的重要性吧？"

---

**"It is interesting, chemically, no doubt," I answered,** "从化学角度来说，当然很有意思，"我回答，

**"but practically——"** 【转折】"但从实用角度——"

---

**"Why, man, it is the most practical** "天哪，这是最实用的——

**medico-legal discovery for years.** → 多少年来最实用的法医学发现。

**Don't you see** 你难道没看出来，

**that it gives us an infallible test for blood stains.** 这给了我们一种检验血迹的万无一失的方法吗？

**Come over here now!"** 过来这边！"

**He seized me by the coat-sleeve in his eagerness,** 他急切地一把抓住我的衣袖，

**and drew me over to the table** → 把我拽到那张桌子旁，

**at which he had been working.** [定从-句尾补充] 就是他刚才工作的那张桌子。

**"Let us have some fresh blood," he said,** "我们来弄点新鲜血液，"他说，

**digging a long bodkin into his finger,** [分词-句末伴随] 一边把一根长针刺进自己的手指，

**and drawing off the resulting drop of blood** → 吸取流出的那滴血——

**in a chemical pipette.** → 用化学移液管。

**"Now, I add this small quantity of blood** "现在，我把这一丁点血——

**to a litre of water.** → 加到一升水里。

**You perceive** 你看，

**that the resulting mixture has the appearance of pure water.** 得到的混合液看起来跟纯净水一样。

**The proportion of blood** 血的比例——

**cannot be more than one in a million.** → 不会超过百万分之一。

**I have no doubt, however,** 不过我毫不怀疑，

**that we shall be able to obtain the characteristic reaction."** 我们仍然能得到那个特征反应。"

**As he spoke,** 说着，

**he threw into the vessel a few white crystals,** 他往容器里丢了几粒白色晶体，

**and then added some drops of a transparent fluid.** → 然后加了几滴透明的液体。

**In an instant** 一瞬间，

**the contents assumed a dull mahogany colour,** 溶液变成了暗红褐色，

**and a brownish dust was precipitated** → 一些棕色的沉淀物沉降下来——

**to the bottom of the glass jar.** → 沉到玻璃罐底部。

---

**"Ha! ha!" he cried,** "哈！哈！"他叫道，

**clapping his hands,** [分词-句末伴随] 拍着手，

**and looking as delighted as a child** → 高兴得像个孩子——

**with a new toy.** → 拿到新玩具的孩子。

**"What do you think of that?"** "你觉得怎么样？"

---

**"It seems to be a very delicate test," I remarked.** "看起来是个非常灵敏的测试，"我说。

---

**"Beautiful! beautiful!** "太好了！太好了！

**The old Guiacum test was very clumsy and uncertain.** 旧的愈创木酯测试又笨又不可靠。

**So is the microscopic examination for blood corpuscles.** 用显微镜检查血球也是一样。

**The latter is valueless** 后者毫无用处，

**if the stains are a few hours old.** 【条件】如果血迹过了几个小时的话。

**Now, this appears to act as well** 而现在这种方法看起来一样有效，

**whether the blood is old or new.** 不管血是新的还是旧的。

**Had this test been invented,** 【假设情况】如果这个测试早发明出来的话，

**there are hundreds of men now walking the earth** 现在这世上有好几百个人，

**who would long ago have paid** [定从-句尾补充] 早就该付出代价——

**the penalty of their crimes."** → 为他们的罪行付出代价的那些人。"

---

**"Indeed!" I murmured.** "真的！"我低声说。

---

**"Criminal cases are continually hinging upon that one point.** "刑事案件不断地系于这一个关键点上。

**A man is suspected of a crime** 一个人被怀疑犯了罪——

**months perhaps after it has been committed.** 也许是好几个月之后。

**His linen or clothes are examined,** 检查他的衬衫或衣服，

**and brownish stains discovered upon them.** → 发现上面有棕色的斑点。

**Are they blood stains, or mud stains,** 那是血迹还是泥迹，

**or rust stains, or fruit stains,** → 是锈迹还是果汁痕迹，

**or what are they?** → 还是别的什么？

**That is a question** 这个问题

**which has puzzled many an expert,** [定从-句尾补充] 难倒了许多专家。

**and why?** 为什么？

**Because there was no reliable test.** 【原因】因为没有可靠的检测方法。

**Now we have the Sherlock Holmes' test,** 现在我们有了歇洛克·福尔摩斯测试法，

**and there will no longer be any difficulty."** → 以后就再也不会有困难了。"

---

**His eyes fairly glittered as he spoke,** 他说这话时，眼睛闪闪发光，

**and he put his hand over his heart** → 他把手放在胸前，

**and bowed** → 鞠了一躬，

**as if to some applauding crowd** 仿佛面前有一群喝彩的观众，

**conjured up by his imagination.** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的观众？→ 由他的想象力召唤出来的。

---

**"You are to be congratulated," I remarked,** "恭喜你了，"我说，

**considerably surprised at his enthusiasm.** [分词-后置修饰] 对他的热情颇为惊讶。

---

**"There was the case of Von Bischoff** "有冯·毕肖夫那个案子——

**at Frankfort last year.** → 去年在法兰克福的那件。

**He would certainly have been hung** 他肯定会被绞死的，

**had this test been in existence.** 【假设情况】如果当时有这个测试的话。

**Then there was Mason of Bradford,** 还有布拉德福德的梅森案，

**and the notorious Muller,** → 臭名昭著的穆勒案，

**and Lefevre of Montpellier,** → 蒙彼利埃的勒费弗尔案，

**and Samson of New Orleans.** → 新奥尔良的萨姆森案。

**I could name a score of cases** 我能说出几十个案子，

**in which it would have been decisive."** [介词-后置修饰] 什么样的案子？→ 有了这个测试就能一锤定音的那种。"

---

**"You seem to be a walking calendar of crime,"** "你简直就是一部行走的犯罪年鉴，"

**said Stamford with a laugh.** 斯坦福德笑道。

**"You might start a paper on those lines.** "你可以照这个路子办一份报纸。

**Call it the 'Police News of the Past.'"** 就叫'往日警讯'好了。"

---

**"Very interesting reading it might be made, too,"** "读起来肯定也挺有意思，"

**remarked Sherlock Holmes,** 歇洛克·福尔摩斯说道，

**sticking a small piece of plaster** [分词-句末伴随] 一边贴了一小块膏药——

**over the prick on his finger.** → 贴在手指的刺破处上。

**"I have to be careful," he continued,** "我得小心点，"他继续说道，

**turning to me with a smile,** [分词-句末伴随] 转向我，笑着，

**"for I dabble with poisons a good deal."** 【原因】"因为我常常跟毒药打交道。"

**He held out his hand as he spoke,** 他一边说一边伸出手来，

**and I noticed** → 我注意到

**that it was all mottled over** → 他的手上斑斑点点——

**with similar pieces of plaster,** → 到处贴着同样的膏药，

**and discoloured with strong acids.** → 还被强酸腐蚀得斑驳变色。

---

**"We came here on business," said Stamford,** "我们可是来办正事的，"斯坦福德说，

**sitting down on a high three-legged stool,** [分词-句末伴随] 坐到一张高高的三脚凳上，

**and pushing another one in my direction with his foot.** → 用脚把另一张推到我跟前。

**"My friend here wants to take diggings,** "我这位朋友想找个住处，

**and as you were complaining** 【原因】而你又在抱怨

**that you could get no one** → 找不到一个人——

**to go halves with you,** → 愿意跟你合租，

**I thought that I had better bring you together."** 我想不如把你们撮合到一起。"

---

**Sherlock Holmes seemed delighted** 歇洛克·福尔摩斯显得很高兴

**at the idea of sharing his rooms with me.** 对什么感到高兴？→ 对跟我合住的提议。

**"I have my eye on a suite** "我看中了一套房子——

**in Baker Street," he said,** → 贝克街上的，"他说，

**"which would suit us down to the ground.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的房子？→ 对我们来说再合适不过的那种。

**You don't mind the smell of strong tobacco, I hope?"** 你不介意浓烟草的味道吧？"

---

**"I always smoke 'ship's' myself," I answered.** "我自己也抽'水手烟'，"我回答。

---

**"That's good enough.** "那就行。

**I generally have chemicals about,** 我身边通常都是化学药品，

**and occasionally do experiments.** → 偶尔做做实验。

**Would that annoy you?"** 你会反感吗？"

---

**"By no means."** "完全不会。"

---

**"Let me see—what are my other shortcomings.** "让我想想——我还有什么别的缺点。

**I get in the dumps at times,** 我有时会心情低落，

**and don't open my mouth for days on end.** → 一连好几天不开口。

**You must not think I am sulky** 你别以为我在闹脾气——

**when I do that.** → 遇到这种情况的时候。

**Just let me alone, and I'll soon be right.** 让我一个人待着就好，很快就没事了。

**What have you to confess now?** 你有什么要坦白的？

**It's just as well** 这倒是好的——

**for two fellows to know the worst** → 让两个人摸清各自最糟糕的一面，

**of one another** → 彼此的那面。

**before they begin to live together."** 在开始一起生活之前。"

---

**I laughed at this cross-examination.** 我笑了笑，觉得这简直像是一场面试。

**"I keep a bull pup," I said,** "我养了一只牛头犬，"我说，

**"and I object to rows** "我受不了吵闹，

**because my nerves are shaken,** 【原因】因为我的神经不太好，

**and I get up at all sorts of ungodly hours,** → 我还总是在各种不像话的时间起床，

**and I am extremely lazy.** → 而且我极其懒散。

**I have another set of vices when I'm well,** 等我身体好了还有另一套毛病，

**but those are the principal ones at present."** 不过目前主要就是这些。"

---

**"Do you include violin-playing** "你觉得拉小提琴——

**in your category of rows?"** → 算在你说的吵闹里吗？"

**he asked, anxiously.** 他焦虑地问。

---

**"It depends on the player," I answered.** "那要看是谁拉的，"我回答。

**"A well-played violin is a treat for the gods** "拉得好的小提琴简直是天赐的享受——

**—a badly-played one——"** 拉得差的嘛——"

---

**"Oh, that's all right," he cried, with a merry laugh.** "哦，那就没问题了，"他开心地笑着说。

**"I think we may consider the thing as settled** "我想我们可以认为这事就这么定了——

**—that is, if the rooms are agreeable to you."** 当然，前提是你对房子也满意。"

---

**"When shall we see them?"** "什么时候去看？"

---

**"Call for me here at noon to-morrow,** "明天中午来这儿找我，

**and we'll go together and settle everything," he answered.** 我们一起去把一切敲定，"他说。

---

**"All right—noon exactly," said I, shaking his hand.** "好的——明天中午整，"我握着他的手说。

---

**We left him working among his chemicals,** 我们告别了他，留他继续在化学药品中忙活。

**and we walked together towards my hotel.** → 我们一起朝我住的旅馆走去。

---

**"By the way," I asked suddenly,** "对了，"我突然问道，

**stopping and turning upon Stamford,** [分词-句末伴随] 停下脚步，转向斯坦福德，

**"how the deuce did he know** "他到底怎么知道——

**that I had come from Afghanistan?"** → 我是从阿富汗回来的？"

---

**My companion smiled an enigmatical smile.** 我的同伴露出一个神秘的微笑。

**"That's just his little peculiarity," he said.** "这就是他的小怪癖，"他说。

**"A good many people have wanted to know** "很多人都想知道

**how he finds things out."** 他是怎么看出这些事的。"

---

**"Oh! a mystery is it?" I cried, rubbing my hands.** "哦！原来是个谜？"我搓着双手叫道。

**"This is very piquant.** "这可太有意思了。

**I am much obliged to you for bringing us together.** 非常感谢你把我们凑到一起。

**'The proper study of mankind is man,' you know."** '对人类最恰当的研究对象就是人本身'嘛。"

---

**"You must study him, then," Stamford said,** "那你可得好好研究研究他了，"斯坦福德说道，

**as he bade me good-bye.** 跟我告别时。

**"You'll find him a knotty problem, though.** "不过你会发现他是个不容易解开的难题。

**I'll wager he learns more about you** 我敢打赌，他了解你——

**than you about him.** → 会比你了解他更多、更快。

**Good-bye."** 再见。"

---

**"Good-bye," I answered,** "再见，"我回答，

**and strolled on to my hotel,** → 然后悠然朝旅馆走去，

**considerably interested in my new acquaintance.** [分词-后置修饰] 对我的这位新相识颇为好奇。

---

### 第二章 演绎法
### CHAPTER II. THE SCIENCE OF DEDUCTION.

---

**We met next day as he had arranged,** 第二天我们按他约定的碰了面，

**and inspected the rooms at No. 221B, Baker Street,** → 去看了贝克街221B的那套房子。

**of which he had spoken at our meeting.** [介词-后置修饰] 什么样的房子？→ 就是他在我们碰面时提到的那套。

**They consisted of a couple of comfortable bed-rooms** 它由两间舒适的卧室组成，

**and a single large airy sitting-room,** → 还有一间宽敞明亮的大起居室，

**cheerfully furnished,** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的起居室？→ 布置得很愉快的，

**and illuminated by two broad windows.** → 还有两扇大窗户透进光来。

**So desirable in every way were the apartments,** 这套房子各方面都十分令人满意，

**and so moderate did the terms seem** → 而且租金看起来也很合理——

**when divided between us,** 【情境】当两人分摊的时候，

**that the bargain was concluded upon the spot,** → 以至于我们当场就成交了，

**and we at once entered into possession.** → 立刻搬了进去。

**That very evening I moved my things round** 当天晚上我就把东西从旅馆搬了过来，
**from the hotel,** →

**and on the following morning** → 第二天早上，

**Sherlock Holmes followed me** 歇洛克·福尔摩斯也跟了过来，

**with several boxes and portmanteaus.** 带着什么？→ 几只箱子和旅行包。

**For a day or two** 我们忙了一两天，

**we were busily employed in unpacking** 忙着拆箱，

**and laying out our property to the best advantage.** → 把东西摆放到最合适的位置。

**That done,** 布置完毕之后，

**we gradually began to settle down** 我们渐渐安顿下来，

**and to accommodate ourselves to our new surroundings.** → 适应了新的环境。

---

**Holmes was certainly not a difficult man to live with.** 福尔摩斯确实是个不难相处的人。

**He was quiet in his ways,** 他做事安安静静，

**and his habits were regular.** → 作息也很有规律。

**It was rare** →
**for him to be up** →
**after ten at night,** → 他很少在晚上十点以后还不睡觉，

**and he had invariably breakfasted and gone out** → 早上在我起床之前，

**before I rose in the morning.** 他总是已经吃过早餐出门了。

**Sometimes he spent his day at the chemical laboratory,** 有时他整天泡在化学实验室，

**sometimes in the dissecting-rooms,** 有时在解剖室，

**and occasionally in long walks,** → 偶尔出去长时间散步，

**which appeared to take him into the lowest** [定从-句尾补充] 这些散步似乎把他带到了伦敦城最底层的地方。
**portions of the City.** →

**Nothing could exceed his energy** 没有什么能比得上他的精力，

**when the working fit was upon him;** 【情境】当他进入工作状态时；

**but now and again a reaction would seize him,** 【转折】但不时地，一种反应期会抓住他，

**and for days on end** → 一连好几天，

**he would lie upon the sofa in the sitting-room,** 他会躺在起居室的沙发上，

**hardly uttering a word or moving a muscle** 几乎一言不发、一动不动，

**from morning to night.** 从早到晚。

**On these occasions** 在这种时候，

**I have noticed such a dreamy,** 我注意到他眼中带着一种恍惚而空洞的神情，
**vacant expression in his eyes,** →

**that I might have suspected him** 到什么程度？→ 我几乎要怀疑他了——

**of being addicted to the use of some narcotic,** 怀疑什么？→ 怀疑他在用什么麻醉品，

**had not the temperance and cleanliness of his whole life** 【实际情况】要不是他整个人的生活方式如此节制和干净，

**forbidden such a notion.** 不允许我有这样的想法。

---

**As the weeks went by,** 【情境】随着时间一周一周过去，

**my interest in him** 我对他的兴趣，

**and my curiosity as to his aims in life,** → 以及对他人生目标的好奇心，

**gradually deepened and increased.** 越来越深、越来越强。

**His very person and appearance were such** 他的外貌和体态就是那种——

**as to strike the attention of the most casual observer.** 足以吸引最漫不经心的观察者的注意的那种。

**In height he was rather over six feet,** 他身高六英尺多一点，

**and so excessively lean** → 又极其瘦削，

**that he seemed to be considerably taller.** 以至于显得比实际还要高许多。

**His eyes were sharp and piercing,** 他的眼睛锐利而有穿透力，

**save during those intervals of torpor** 除了什么时候？→ 除了我提到过的那些恍惚的间歇期。

**to which I have alluded;** [定从-句尾补充] 就是我之前提到过的那种。

**and his thin, hawk-like nose** → 他那又瘦又像鹰钩的鼻子，

**gave his whole expression an air of alertness and decision.** 使得他整个人散发出一种警觉而果断的气质。

**His chin, too, had the prominence and squareness** 他的下巴也棱角分明、突出有力，

**which mark the man of determination.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的突出和方正？→ 标志着一个果断之人的那种。

**His hands were invariably blotted with ink** 他的手上总是沾着墨水，

**and stained with chemicals,** → 染着化学药品的痕迹，

**yet he was possessed of extraordinary delicacy of touch,** 【转折】然而他的手指却灵巧得出奇，

**as I frequently had occasion to observe** 这一点我有过无数次机会观察到——

**when I watched him manipulating his fragile philosophical instruments.** 【情境】当我看他操弄那些精密的科学仪器时。

---

**The reader may set me down as a hopeless busybody,** 读者大概会觉得我是个无可救药的多管闲事的人，

**when I confess** 【情境】当我坦承——

**how much this man stimulated my curiosity,** 这个人在多大程度上激起了我的好奇心，

**and how often I endeavoured to break through the reticence** → 以及我曾多少次试图突破那种沉默——

**which he showed on all that concerned himself.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的沉默？→ 他在涉及自身时表现出来的那种。

**Before pronouncing judgment, however, be it remembered,** 【让步】不过在下判断之前，请记住——

**how objectless was my life,** 我的生活是多么百无聊赖，

**and how little there was to engage my attention.** → 又有多么少的事情能吸引我的注意力。

**My health forbade me from venturing out** 我的健康状况不允许我外出，

**unless the weather was exceptionally genial,** 【条件】除非天气特别好，

**and I had no friends** → 【结果（反面）】也没有什么朋友

**who would call upon me** [定从-句尾补充] 会来看望我的，

**and break the monotony of my daily existence.** → 打破我日常生活的单调的。

**Under these circumstances,** 在这种情况下，

**I eagerly hailed the little mystery** 我热切地抓住了那个小小的谜团，

**which hung around my companion,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的谜团？→ 萦绕在我这位同伴身上的。

**and spent much of my time in endeavouring** → 花了大量时间去试图解开它。
**to unravel it.** →

---

**He was not studying medicine.** 他不在学医。

**He had himself, in reply to a question,** 在回答我的一个问题时，

**confirmed Stamford's opinion upon that point.** 他本人证实了斯坦福德在这一点上的说法。

**Neither did he appear to have pursued any** 他似乎也没有修过任何课程，
**course of reading** →

**which might fit him for a degree in science** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的课程？→ 能让他获得理科学位的那种，

**or any other recognized portal** → 或任何其他公认的入口，

**which would give him an entrance into the learned world.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么入口？→ 能让他进入学术界的那种。

**Yet his zeal for certain studies was remarkable,** 【转折】然而他对某些学科的热情是惊人的，

**and within eccentric limits** → 在他那些古怪的领域范围内，

**his knowledge was so extraordinarily ample and minute** 他的知识如此广博而精细，

**that his observations have fairly astounded me.** 以至于他的见解着实让我大吃一惊。

**Surely no man would work so hard** 一个人不可能如此勤奋地工作，

**or attain such precise information** → 或掌握如此精确的信息，

**unless he had some definite end in view.** 【条件】除非他心中有一个明确的目标。→ 有了目标，才会如此。

**Desultory readers are seldom remarkable** 漫无目的的读者很少出众，

**for the exactness of their learning.** 在什么方面出众？→ 在学识的精确度方面。

**No man burdens his mind with small matters** 没有人会让自己的头脑去承载那些细枝末节的事情，

**unless he has some very good reason for doing so.** 【条件】除非他有一个非常充分的理由。

---

**His ignorance was as remarkable as his knowledge.** 他的无知和他的知识一样令人惊讶。

**Of contemporary literature, philosophy and politics** 对于当代文学、哲学和政治，

**he appeared to know next to nothing.** 他似乎一无所知。

**Upon my quoting Thomas Carlyle,** 我引用了一句托马斯·卡莱尔的话，

**he inquired in the naivest way** 他竟然天真地问——

**who he might be and what he had done.** 此人是谁、做了什么。

**My surprise reached a climax, however,** 然而，我的惊讶达到了顶点——

**when I found incidentally** 【情境】当我无意中发现——

**that he was ignorant of the Copernican Theory** 他竟然不知道哥白尼理论，

**and of the composition of the Solar System.** → 也不知道太阳系的构成。

**That any civilized human being in this nineteenth century** 在这十九世纪，一个文明人——

**should not be aware** 居然不知道——

**that the earth travelled round the sun** 不知道地球绕着太阳转——

**appeared to be to me such an extraordinary fact** 这件事在我看来太不可思议了，

**that I could hardly realize it.** 我简直难以相信。

---

**"You appear to be astonished," he said,** "你好像很吃惊，"他说，

**smiling at my expression of surprise.** [分词-句末伴随] 笑着看我惊讶的表情。

**"Now that I do know it** "既然我现在知道了，

**I shall do my best to forget it."** 我会尽力把它忘掉的。"

---

**"To forget it!"** "忘掉它！"

---

**"You see," he explained,** "你看，"他解释道，

**"I consider that a man's brain originally is** "我认为人的大脑本来就像一间小小的空阁楼，
**like a little empty attic,** →

**and you have to stock it with such** → 你得按自己的选择往里面放家具。
**furniture as you choose.** →

**A fool takes in all the lumber of every sort** 蠢人什么破烂都往里塞，

**that he comes across,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的破烂？→ 不管碰到什么都收进来，

**so that the knowledge which might be useful to him** → 结果那些可能对他有用的知识

**gets crowded out,** 反而被挤出去了，

**or at best is jumbled up with a** → 就算没挤出去，
**lot of other things** → 也跟一堆别的东西混在一起，

**so that he has a difficulty in laying** → 以至于根本找不着了。
**his hands upon it.** →

**Now the skilful workman is very careful indeed** 而聪明的工匠是非常非常小心的，

**as to what he takes into his brain-attic.** 小心什么？→ 小心他往脑子阁楼里放什么。

**He will have nothing but the tools** 他只放那些工具，

**which may help him in doing his work,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的工具？→ 有助于他工作的那些，

**but of these he has a large assortment,** 【转折】但这些工具他备得很全，

**and all in the most perfect order.** → 而且井井有条。

**It is a mistake to think** 以为那间小房子——

**that that little room has elastic walls** 以为它的墙壁有弹性，

**and can distend to any extent.** → 可以无限扩张——那是错误的。

**Depend upon it** 放心好了，

**there comes a time** 总有一天，

**when for every addition of knowledge** 你每多学一点知识，

**you forget something that you knew before.** 就能忘掉一点你以前知道的东西。

**It is of the highest importance, therefore,** 因此，最最要紧的是——

**not to have useless facts elbowing out the useful ones."** 不要让那些没用的知识把有用的知识挤出去。"

---

**"But the Solar System!" I protested.** "可是太阳系啊！"我抗议道。

---

**"What the deuce is it to me?" he interrupted impatiently;** "这关我什么事？"他不耐烦地打断我；

**"you say that we go round the sun.** "你说我们绕着太阳转。

**If we went round the moon** 【假设情况】就算我们绕着月亮转，

**it would not make a pennyworth of difference** 也不会有一分钱的差别，

**to me or to my work."** 对谁来说？→ 对我和我的工作来说。"

---

**I was on the point of asking him** 我正想问他

**what that work might be,** 那工作到底是什么，

**but something in his manner showed me** 【转折】但他神态中的某些东西告诉我，

**that the question would be an unwelcome one.** 这个问题不会受欢迎。

**I pondered over our short conversation, however,** 【转折】不过我反复回味了我们那段简短的对话，

**and endeavoured to draw my deductions from it.** → 试图从中推断出些什么。

**He said that he would acquire no knowledge** 他说他不会去获取知识——

**which did not bear upon his object.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的知识？→ 与自己目标无关的那种。

**Therefore all the knowledge which he possessed** 因此他所拥有的知识，

**was such as would be useful to him.** 一定都是对他有用的。

**I enumerated in my own mind** 我在脑子里逐一列举了

**all the various points** 所有那些方面，

**upon which he had shown me** [介词-后置修饰] 什么方面？→

**that he was exceptionally well-informed.** 他在哪些方面显示出非凡的精通。

**I even took a pencil and jotted them down.** 我甚至拿出铅笔记了下来。

**I could not help smiling at the document** 写完之后我忍不住看着那份清单笑了。

**when I had completed it.** 【情境】当我写完之后。

**It ran in this way—** 它是这样的——

---

**SHERLOCK HOLMES—his limits.** **歇洛克·福尔摩斯——其知识的边界。**

1. **Knowledge of Literature.—Nil.** 文学知识——零。
2. **Philosophy.—Nil.** 哲学——零。
3. **Astronomy.—Nil.** 天文学——零。
4. **Politics.—Feeble.** 政治——薄弱。
5. **Botany.—Variable.** 植物学——参差不齐。**Well up in belladonna, opium, and poisons generally.** 精通颠茄、鸦片和各种毒药。**Knows nothing of practical gardening.** 对实用园艺一无所知。
6. **Geology.—Practical, but limited.** 地质学——实用但有限。**Tells at a glance different soils from each other.** 一眼就能分辨不同的土壤。**After walks has shown me splashes upon his trousers,** → 散步回来后给我看他裤子上的泥点——**and told me by their colour and consistence** → 并根据颜色和质地——**in what part of London he had received them.** → 告诉我是在伦敦哪个地方沾上的。
7. **Chemistry.—Profound.** 化学——精深。
8. **Anatomy.—Accurate, but unsystematic.** 解剖学——准确，但不成体系。
9. **Sensational Literature.—Immense.** 耸人听闻的文献——渊博无比。**He appears to know every detail** → 他似乎知道每一个细节——**of every horror perpetrated in the century.** → 本世纪每一桩恐怖案件的细节。
10. **Plays the violin well.** 小提琴拉得很好。
11. **Is an expert singlestick player, boxer, and swordsman.** 精通棍术、拳击和剑术。
12. **Has a good practical knowledge of British law.** 对英国法律有良好的实用知识。

---

**When I had got so far in my list** 写到这里，

**I threw it into the fire in despair.** 我绝望地把那张单子扔进了火里。

**"If I can only find what the fellow** "除非我能弄清这家伙到底在追求什么—
**is driving at** → —

**by reconciling all these accomplishments,** 通过什么方式？→ 通过把他所有这些才能统一起来，

**and discovering a calling which needs them all,"** → 找到一个需要它们全部的职业，"

**I said to myself,** 我对自己说，

**"I may as well give up the attempt at once."** "否则我还是趁早放弃吧。"

---

**I see that I have alluded above to** 我发现上面我提到了他的小提琴才能。
**his powers upon the violin.** →

**These were very remarkable,** 这方面确实很出色，

**but as eccentric as all his other accomplishments.** 【转折】但跟他所有其他本领一样古怪。

**That he could play pieces,** 他能演奏曲子——
**and difficult pieces,** → 而且是高难度的曲子—
**I knew well,** → —这我很清楚，

**because at my request** 【原因】因为在我的要求下，

**he has played me some of Mendelssohn's Lieder,** 他给我演奏过门德尔松的一些《无词歌》和其他我喜欢的曲目。
**and other favourites.** →

**When left to himself, however,** 【转折】但在他自己独处的时候，

**he would seldom produce any music** 他很少会去弹什么正经曲子，

**or attempt any recognized air.** → 或演奏什么公认的旋律。

**Leaning back in his arm-chair of an evening,** [分词-句首状语] 傍晚时分，往扶手椅里一靠 → 在这种状态下——

**he would close his eyes** 他会闭上眼睛，

**and scrape carelessly at the fiddle** → 漫不经心地在小提琴上拉来拉去，

**which was thrown across his knee.** [定从-句尾补充] 小提琴搁在他膝盖上。

**Sometimes the chords were sonorous and melancholy.** 有时候那些和弦低沉而忧郁。

**Occasionally they were fantastic and cheerful.** 有时候又奇异而欢快。

**Clearly they reflected the thoughts which possessed him,** 显然它们反映了占据他心头的思绪，

**but whether the music aided those thoughts,** 【选项A】至于那音乐是在辅助他的思考，

**or whether the playing was simply the result** 【选项B】还是拉琴纯粹是出于一时兴起—
**of a whim or fancy** → —

**was more than I could determine.** 我就无从判断了。

**I might have rebelled against these exasperating solos** 【假设情况】我恐怕早就要反抗这些令人抓狂的独奏了，

**had it not been that he usually terminated them** 【实际情况】要不是他通常会结束它们——

**by playing in quick succession** 通过什么方式结束？→ 通过连续演奏，

**a whole series of my favourite airs** 演奏什么？→ 一整串我最喜欢的曲子，

**as a slight compensation for the trial upon my patience.** 作为什么？→ 作为对我耐心的小小补偿。

---

**During the first week or so** 头一两个星期，

**we had no callers,** 没有人来拜访，

**and I had begun to think** → 我开始觉得

**that my companion was** →
**as friendless a man** →
**as I was myself.** → 我的同伴跟我一样是个没有朋友的人。

**Presently, however,** 【转折】但很快，

**I found that he had many acquaintances,** 我发现他的相识还真不少，

**and those in the most different classes of society.** → 而且来自社会上最不同的阶层。

**There was one little sallow rat-faced, dark-eyed fellow** 有一个矮小的、面色蜡黄、鼠脸、黑眼睛的家伙，

**who was introduced to me as Mr. Lestrade,** [定从-句尾补充] 被介绍给我说叫雷斯垂德先生，

**and who came three** [并列 who] 而且一个星期来了三四次。
**or four times in a single week.** →

**One morning a young girl called,** 一天早上来了个年轻姑娘，

**fashionably dressed,** [分词-后置修饰] 衣着时髦的，

**and stayed for half an hour or more.** → 待了半个多小时。

**The same afternoon brought a grey-headed, seedy visitor,** 同一天下午又来了个头发灰白、衣衫寒酸的访客，

**looking like a Jew pedlar,** [分词-后置修饰] 看上去像个犹太小贩，

**who appeared to me to be much excited,** [定从-句尾补充] 神情很是激动，

**and who was closely followed by a slip-shod elderly woman.** [并列 who] 紧随其后又来了一位穿着邋遢的上了年纪的妇人。

**On another occasion** 还有一次，

**an old white-haired gentleman had an interview with my companion;** 一位白发老绅士跟我的同伴面谈；

**and on another** 又有一次，

**a railway porter in his velveteen uniform.** 来的是个穿着灯芯绒制服的铁路搬运工。

**When any of these nondescript individuals put in an appearance,** 【情境】每当这些形形色色的人物出现时，

**Sherlock Holmes used to beg** →
**for the use of the sitting-room,** → 歇洛克·福尔摩斯就会请求借用起居室，

**and I would retire to my bed-room.** → 而我就退到自己的卧室去。

**He always apologized to me** 他总是向我道歉，

**for putting me to this inconvenience.** 为什么道歉？→ 为给我造成的不便。

**"I have to use this room** "我得把这间屋子当办公场所用，
**as a place of business," he said,** → "他说，

**"and these people are my clients."** "这些人是我的客户。"

**Again I had an opportunity of asking him** 又一次，
**a point blank question,** → 我有了机会直截了当地问他，

**and again my delicacy prevented me** 【转折】但又一次，我的教养阻止了我，

**from forcing another man to confide in me.** 阻止我做什么？→ 强迫别人对我推心置腹。

**I imagined at the time** 当时我以为

**that he had some strong reason** 他有某种强烈的理由不愿提及此事，
**for not alluding to it,** →

**but he soon dispelled the idea** 【转折】但他很快打消了我的这个想法，

**by coming round to the subject of his own accord.** 通过什么方式？→ 通过自己主动把话题转到了上面。

---

**It was upon the 4th of March,** 那是三月四日——

**as I have good reason to remember,** 这个日子我有充分的理由记得——

**that I rose somewhat earlier than usual,** 我那天起得比平时早了些，

**and found that Sherlock Holmes had not** → 发现歇洛克·福尔摩斯还没有吃完早餐。
**yet finished his breakfast.** →

**The landlady had become so accustomed to my late habits** 房东太太已经习惯了我晚起的毛病，

**that my place had not been laid** 以至于我的位子还没有摆好，

**nor my coffee prepared.** → 咖啡也没有准备。

**With the unreasonable petulance of mankind** 带着人类常有的那种不讲理的小脾气，

**I rang the bell** 我按了铃，

**and gave a curt intimation that I was ready.** → 简短地通知说我准备好了。

**Then I picked up a magazine from the table** 然后我从桌上拿起一本杂志，

**and attempted to while away the time with it,** → 试图翻翻消磨时间，

**while my companion munched silently at his toast.** 【情境】这时候我的同伴正默默地嚼着吐司。

**One of the articles had a pencil mark** 有一篇文章的标题处有铅笔划的记号，
**at the heading,** →

**and I naturally began to run my eye through it.** → 我自然而然地开始浏览起来。

---

**Its somewhat ambitious title was "The Book of Life,"** 那篇文章的标题颇有些野心，叫做《生命之书》，

**and it attempted to show** → 试图说明——

**how much an observant man might learn** 一个善于观察的人能够学到多少东西，

**by an accurate and systematic examination** 通过什么方式？→ 通过精确而系统的考察，

**of all that came in his way.** 考察什么？→ 考察他所遇到的一切。

**It struck me as being a remarkable mixture** 我觉得它是一种奇妙的混合，

**of shrewdness and of absurdity.** 什么的混合？→ 精明与荒谬的混合。

**The reasoning was close and intense,** 推理环环相扣，非常缜密，

**but the deductions appeared to me to be** 【转折】但得出的结论在我看来却牵强而夸大。
**far-fetched and exaggerated.** →

**The writer claimed** 作者声称——

**by a momentary expression,** 通过一个瞬间的表情，

**a twitch of a muscle** → 一次肌肉的抽动，

**or a glance of an eye,** → 或一个眼神，

**to fathom a man's inmost thoughts.** 就能洞悉一个人内心最深处的想法。

**Deceit, according to him, was an impossibility** 他认为，欺骗是不可能的——

**in the case of one trained to observation and analysis.** 对谁来说不可能？→ 对于一个受过观察和分析训练的人来说。

**His conclusions were as infallible** 他的结论就像——一样无懈可击，

**as so many propositions of Euclid.** 像什么一样？→ 像欧几里得的命题一样。

**So startling would his results appear to the uninitiated** 对于外行人来说，他的结论一定是令人震惊的，

**that until they learned the processes** 以至于在他们了解那些过程之前——

**by which he had arrived at them** [介词-后置修饰] 什么样的过程？→ 他得出结论所经历的过程，

**they might well consider him as a necromancer.** 他们完全有理由把他看成一个巫师。

---

**"From a drop of water," said the writer,** "从一滴水，"作者写道，

**"a logician could infer the possibility** "一个逻辑学家可以推断出——的可能性，

**of an Atlantic or a Niagara** 什么的可能性？→ 大西洋或尼亚加拉瀑布的，

**without having seen or heard of one or the other.** 在什么条件下？→ 不必亲眼见过或听说过其中任何一个。

**So all life is a great chain,** 同样，一切生命就是一条大链条，

**the nature of which is known** [定从-句尾补充] 整条链条的性质就可以知道了——

**whenever we are shown a single link of it.** 【情境】只要给我们看到其中一个环节。

**Like all other arts,** 和所有其他技艺一样，

**the Science of Deduction and Analysis is one** 演绎和分析的科学是一门——

**which can only be acquired by long and patient study** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的科学？→ 只有通过漫长而耐心的研究才能掌握的那种，

**nor, is life long enough** → 而且人的一生还不够长，

**to allow any mortal to attain the highest** 不够长到什么程度？
**possible perfection in it.** → 不足以让任何凡人在这方面达到最高的完美境界。

**Before turning to those moral** →
**and mental aspects of the matter** → 在转向这门学问中那些道德和心理层面之前—

**which present the greatest difficulties,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的层面？→ 最具挑战性的那些，

**let the enquirer begin by mastering more elementary problems.** 研究者不妨先从掌握更基础的问题开始。

**Let him, on meeting a fellow-mortal,** 当他遇到一个人的时候，

**learn at a glance to distinguish the history** 让他学会一眼就辨认出此人的经历，
**of the man,** →

**and the trade or profession to which he belongs.** → 以及他从事的行业或职业。

**Puerile as such an exercise may seem,** 【让步】这种练习看似幼稚，

**it sharpens the faculties of observation,** 【主张】但它能磨砺观察力，

**and teaches one** → 教会人该看什么、
**where to look** → 该找什么。
**and what to look for.** →

**By a man's finger nails,** 通过一个人的指甲，

**by his coat-sleeve,** → 衣袖，

**by his boot,** → 靴子，

**by his trouser knees,** → 膝盖处的裤子，

**by the callosities of his forefinger and thumb,** → 食指和拇指上的老茧，

**by his expression,** → 表情，

**by his shirt cuffs** → 衬衫袖口——

**—by each of these things a man's calling** 通过这些东西中的每一样，
**is plainly revealed.** → 一个人的职业就会一目了然。

**That all united should fail to enlighten the competent enquirer** 把所有这些线索加在一起，仍然无法让一个称职的研究者作出判断——

**in any case is almost inconceivable."** 这几乎是不可想象的。"

---

**"What ineffable twaddle!" I cried,** "简直是一派胡言！"我叫道，

**slapping the magazine down on the table,** [分词-句末伴随] 把杂志拍到桌子上，

**"I never read such rubbish in my life."** "我这辈子都没看过这么荒唐的东西。"

---

**"What is it?" asked Sherlock Holmes.** "什么东西？"歇洛克·福尔摩斯问。

---

**"Why, this article," I said,** "就是这篇文章啊，"我说，

**pointing at it with my egg spoon** [分词-句末伴随] 用蛋匙指着它，

**as I sat down to my breakfast.** 【情境】我坐下来吃早餐时。

**"I see that you have read it** "我看你读过了，

**since you have marked it.** 【原因】因为你在上面做了记号。

**I don't deny that it is smartly written.** 我不否认它写得还算巧妙。

**It irritates me though.** 【转折】但它让我很恼火。

**It is evidently the theory of some arm-chair lounger** 这显然是某个安乐椅空想家的理论，

**who evolves all these neat little paradoxes** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的空想家？→ 炮制出这些精巧的小悖论来的那种，

**in the seclusion of his own study.** 在哪炮制？→ 躲在自己书房里。

**It is not practical.** 完全不切实际。

**I should like to see him clapped down** 我倒想看看他被丢下去——

**in a third class carriage on the Underground,** 丢到哪？→ 丢到地铁三等车厢里，

**and asked to give the trades of all his fellow-travellers.** → 让他说出每一位同行旅客的职业。

**I would lay a thousand to one against him."** 我敢以一千比一打赌他说不出来。"

---

**"You would lose your money,"** "你会输掉你的钱的，"

**Sherlock Holmes remarked calmly.** 歇洛克·福尔摩斯平静地说。

**"As for the article, I wrote it myself."** "至于那篇文章，是我自己写的。"

---

**"You!"** "你！"

---

**"Yes, I have a turn both** "是的，
**for observation and for deduction.** → 我在观察和演绎两方面都有天赋。

**The theories which I have expressed there,** 我在那篇文章中表达的那些理论，

**and which appear to you to be so chimerical** [并列 which] 在你看来不切实际的那些，

**are really extremely practical** 实际上却极其实用——

**—so practical that I depend upon them** 实用到什么程度？
**for my bread and cheese."** → 我就是靠它们吃饭的。"

---

**"And how?" I asked involuntarily.** "怎么说？"我不由自主地问道。

---

**"Well, I have a trade of my own.** "嗯，我有一门自己的行当。

**I suppose I am the only one in the world.** 我想我大概是世界上独一份。

**I'm a consulting detective,** 我是一个咨询侦探——

**if you can understand what that is.** 如果你能理解这是什么的话。

**Here in London** 在伦敦，

**we have lots of Government detectives** 我们有很多官方侦探，

**and lots of private ones.** → 也有很多私家侦探。

**When these fellows are at fault** 【情境】当这些人走投无路的时候，

**they come to me,** 他们就来找我，

**and I manage to put them on the right scent.** → 我帮他们找到正确的线索。

**They lay all the evidence before me,** 他们把所有证据摆在我面前，

**and I am generally able,** → 我通常能够——

**by the help of my knowledge of the** 靠着什么？
**history of crime,** → 靠着我对犯罪史的了解——

**to set them straight.** 帮他们理清头绪。

**There is a strong family resemblance about misdeeds,** 犯罪行为之间有很强的家族相似性，

**and if you have all the details of** 【条件】如果你对一千桩案子了如指掌的话，
**a thousand at your finger ends,** →

**it is odd** 【结果】遇到第一千零一桩理不出头绪的话，
**if you can't unravel the thousand and first.** → 那才叫奇怪。

**Lestrade is a well-known detective.** 雷斯垂德是个很有名的侦探。

**He got himself into a fog recently over** 他最近办一桩伪造案弄得一头雾水，
**a forgery case,** →

**and that was what brought him here."** → 所以才来找我。"

---

**"And these other people?"** "那其他那些人呢？"

---

**"They are mostly sent on by private inquiry agencies.** "大多是私家调查所介绍来的。

**They are all people** 他们都是一些人，

**who are in trouble about something,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的人？→ 遇到了什么麻烦的，

**and want a little enlightening.** → 想要人指点迷津的。

**I listen to their story,** 我听他们说故事，

**they listen to my comments,** → 他们听我的评判，

**and then I pocket my fee."** → 然后我收我的费用。"

---

**"But do you mean to say," I said,** "可是你的意思是，"我说，

**"that without leaving your room** "你不出门

**you can unravel some knot** 就能解开那些谜团——

**which other men can make nothing of,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的谜团？→ 别人怎么也弄不清的那种，

**although they have seen every detail for themselves?"** 【让步】虽然他们亲眼看过所有细节？"

---

**"Quite so.** "正是如此。

**I have a kind of intuition that way.** 我在这方面有一种直觉。

**Now and again a case turns up** 偶尔也会碰到案子，

**which is a little more complex.** [定从-句尾补充] 比较复杂的那种。

**Then I have to bustle about** 那时候我就得亲自出去跑跑，

**and see things with my own eyes.** → 亲眼看看。

**You see I have a lot of special knowledge** 你看，我有大量的专业知识，

**which I apply to the problem,** [定从-句尾补充] 我把这些知识用来处理问题，

**and which facilitates matters wonderfully.** [并列 which] 而且这些知识大大帮助了办事。

**Those rules of deduction** 那些演绎法则——

**laid down in that article** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的法则？→ 那篇文章中列出的，

**which aroused your scorn,** [定从-句中插入] 所谓那篇文章，就是被你嗤之以鼻的那篇——

← 回来接谓语 →

**are invaluable to me in practical work.** 对我的实际工作来说是无价之宝。

**Observation with me is second nature.** 观察对我来说已经是第二天性了。

**You appeared to be surprised** 你好像很吃惊——

**when I told you, on our first meeting,** 【情境】当我在第一次见面时告诉你——

**that you had come from Afghanistan."** 你从阿富汗回来的。"

---

**"You were told, no doubt."** "有人告诉你的吧。"

---

**"Nothing of the sort.** "绝对不是。

**I _knew_ you came from Afghanistan.** 我是*推断出来*的。

**From long habit** 出于长期的习惯，

**the train of thoughts ran so swiftly through my mind,** 思维链在我脑中飞速运转，

**that I arrived at the conclusion** 以至于我得出了结论，

**without being conscious of intermediate steps.** 自己都没有意识到中间经历了哪些步骤。

**There were such steps, however.** 不过那些步骤确实是存在的。

**The train of reasoning ran,** 推理的过程是这样的：

**'Here is a gentleman of a medical type,** '眼前这位先生有着医务人员的气质，

**but with the air of a military man.** 【转折】但又带着军人的风度。

**Clearly an army doctor, then.** 显然是个军医。

**He has just come from the tropics,** 他刚从热带回来，

**for his face is dark,** 【原因】因为他脸色很黑，

**and that is not the natural tint of his skin,** → 【转折】但那不是他皮肤天生的颜色——

**for his wrists are fair.** 【原因】因为他的手腕是白的。

**He has undergone hardship and sickness,** 他经历了艰苦和疾病——

**as his haggard face says clearly.** 他憔悴的面容清楚地说明了这一点。

**His left arm has been injured.** 他的左臂受过伤。

**He holds it in a stiff and unnatural manner.** 他举着它的姿态很僵硬、不自然。

**Where in the tropics could an English army doctor** 在热带地区，一个英国军医

**have seen much hardship** 在什么地方可能经历了这么多艰苦，

**and got his arm wounded?** → 而且胳膊还受了伤？

**Clearly in Afghanistan.'** 显然是在阿富汗。'

**The whole train of thought did not occupy a second.** 整个思维过程不到一秒钟。

**I then remarked that you came from Afghanistan,** 然后我就说你从阿富汗回来，

**and you were astonished."** → 你大为吃惊。"

---

**"It is simple enough** "你一解释就简单了，
**as you explain it," I said, smiling.** → "我微笑着说。

**"You remind me of Edgar Allen Poe's Dupin.** "你让我想起了爱伦·坡笔下的杜宾。

**I had no idea** 我都不知道

**that such individuals did exist outside of stories."** 这种人在小说以外也存在。"

---

**Sherlock Holmes rose and lit his pipe.** 歇洛克·福尔摩斯站起来点上了烟斗。

**"No doubt you think that you are complimenting me** "你把我比作杜宾，无疑觉得是在恭维我，"

**in comparing me to Dupin," he observed.** 他说。

**"Now, in my opinion,** 【转折】"但依我看，

**Dupin was a very inferior fellow.** 杜宾是个非常低劣的家伙。

**That trick of his** 他那套把戏——

**of breaking in on his friends' thoughts** 什么把戏？→ 打断朋友思路的把戏，

**with an apropos remark** 用什么打断？→ 用一句切中要害的话，

**after a quarter of an hour's silence** 在什么之后？→ 在沉默了一刻钟之后——

**is really very showy and superficial.** 实在是华而不实、矫揉造作。

**He had some analytical genius, no doubt;** 他有一些分析才能，没错；

**but he was by no means such a phenomenon** 【转折】但他绝不是那种了不起的人物——

**as Poe appeared to imagine."** 像坡想象的那样了不起。"

---

**"Have you read Gaboriau's works?" I asked.** "你读过加博里奥的作品吗？"我问。

**"Does Lecoq come up to your idea of a detective?"** "勒考克符合你心目中侦探的标准吗？"

---

**Sherlock Holmes sniffed sardonically.** 歇洛克·福尔摩斯不屑地哼了一声。

**"Lecoq was a miserable bungler," he said,** "勒考克是个可悲的蹩脚货，
**in an angry voice;** → "他愤愤地说，

**"he had only one thing to recommend him,** "他唯一值得称道的——

**and that was his energy.** 就是他的精力旺盛。

**That book made me positively ill.** 那本书简直让我恶心。

**The question was how to identify an unknown prisoner.** 问题是如何确认一个身份不明的囚犯。

**I could have done it in twenty-four hours.** 我用二十四小时就能办到。

**Lecoq took six months or so.** 勒考克花了大约六个月。

**It might be made a text-book for detectives** 那本书简直可以当教材——

**to teach them what to avoid."** 教侦探们什么事不该做。"

---

**I felt rather indignant** 我感到相当不满，

**at having two characters whom I had admired** 因为什么？→ 因为我所欣赏的两个人物

**treated in this cavalier style.** 被如此轻慢地对待。

**I walked over to the window,** 我走到窗前，

**and stood looking out into the busy street.** → 望着窗外熙熙攘攘的街道。

**"This fellow may be very clever," I said to myself,** "这家伙也许确实很聪明，"我心想，

**"but he is certainly very conceited."** "但他确实非常自负。"

---

**"There are no crimes** "如今没有什么犯罪，
**and no criminals in these days," he said, querulously.** → 也没有什么罪犯了，"他不满地说。

**"What is the use of having brains in our profession.** "在我们这一行，有脑子又有什么用呢。

**I know well that I have it in me** 我清楚地知道我有能力

**to make my name famous.** 让自己名扬天下。

**No man lives or has ever lived** 从来没有一个人——活着的或已故的——

**who has brought the same amount of study** [定从-句尾补充] 把如此多的
**and of natural talent** → 研究和天赋

**to the detection of crime which I have done.** 投入到侦破犯罪中去，像我一样。

**And what is the result?** 结果呢？

**There is no crime to detect,** 没有什么案子好侦查，

**or, at most, some bungling villainy** → 就算有，也不过是些笨拙的犯罪，

**with a motive so transparent** [with-描述特点] 带着什么样的动机？→ 动机明摆着的，

**that even a Scotland Yard official can see through it."** 明到什么程度？→ 连苏格兰场的人都能看穿。"

---

**I was still annoyed at his bumptious style of conversation.** 他这种自大的谈话方式仍然让我很恼火。

**I thought it best to change the topic.** 我觉得最好换个话题。

---

**"I wonder what that fellow is looking for?" I asked,** "我在想那个人在找什么？"我问道，

**pointing to a stalwart, plainly-dressed individual** [分词-句末伴随] 指着一个身材壮实、衣着朴素的人，

**who was walking slowly down the other side** [定从-句尾补充] 正沿着街对面慢慢走着，
**of the street,** →

**looking anxiously at the numbers.** [分词-句末伴随] 焦急地看着门牌号码。

**He had a large blue envelope in his hand,** 他手里拿着一个蓝色大信封，

**and was evidently the bearer of a message.** → 显然是来送信的。

---

**"You mean the retired sergeant of Marines," said Sherlock Holmes.** "你是说那个退役的海军陆战队军士，"歇洛克·福尔摩斯说。

---

**"Brag and bounce!" thought I to myself.** "吹牛大王！"我心想。

**"He knows that I cannot verify his guess."** "他知道我没法验证他的猜测。"

---

**The thought had hardly passed through my mind** 这念头刚刚在脑中一闪，

**when the man whom we were watching** 【转折】我们注视的那个人

**caught sight of the number on our door,** 就看到了我们门上的号码，

**and ran rapidly across the roadway.** → 迅速穿过马路跑了过来。

**We heard a loud knock,** 我们听到一声响亮的敲门声，

**a deep voice below,** → 楼下传来一个低沉的嗓音，

**and heavy steps ascending the stair.** → 然后是沉重的脚步声上了楼。

---

**"For Mr. Sherlock Holmes," he said,** "找歇洛克·福尔摩斯先生的，"他说，

**stepping into the room** [分词-句末伴随] 走进房间，

**and handing my friend the letter.** → 把信递给了我的朋友。

---

**Here was an opportunity of taking the conceit** 这下可是个好机会，
**out of him.** → 让我灭灭他的傲气。

**He little thought of this** 他做出那个随口一蒙时，可没料到这个。

**when he made that random shot.** 【情境】当他做出那个随口一蒙时。

**"May I ask,** "小伙子，请问，
**my lad," I said,** → "我用最温和的语气说，
**in the blandest voice,** →

**"what your trade may be?"** "你是做什么的？"

---

**"Commissionaire, sir," he said, gruffly.** "跑腿的，先生，"他粗声粗气地回答。

**"Uniform away for repairs."** "制服拿去修了。"

---

**"And you were?" I asked,** "那你以前呢？"我问道，

**with a slightly malicious glance at my companion.** [with-描述状态] 带着什么神情？→ 带着一丝得意地瞥了我的同伴一眼。

---

**"A sergeant, sir, Royal Marine Light Infantry, sir.** "军士，先生，皇家海军陆战队轻步兵团，先生。

**No answer? Right, sir."** 不用回信？好的，先生。"

---

**He clicked his heels together,** 他两脚跟一碰，

**raised his hand in a salute,** → 举手敬了个礼，

**and was gone.** → 就走了。

---

### 第三章 劳里斯顿花园街的疑案
### CHAPTER III. THE LAURISTON GARDENS MYSTERY

---

**I confess that I was considerably startled** 我承认我相当吃惊，

**by this fresh proof** 被什么吃惊？→ 被这个新的证据，

**of the practical nature of my companion's theories.** 什么的证据？→ 我同伴的理论确实有实用价值的证据。

**My respect for his powers of analysis increased wondrously.** 我对他分析能力的敬意大大增加了。

**There still remained some lurking suspicion in my mind, however,** 【转折】不过我心里仍然残存着一丝隐隐的怀疑，

**that the whole thing was a pre-arranged episode,** 怀疑什么？→ 怀疑整件事是事先安排好的，

**intended to dazzle me,** [分词-后置修饰] 目的是什么？→ 是为了让我目眩的，

**though what earthly object he could have in** 【让步】虽然他骗我到底能有什么目的，
**taking me in** →

**was past my comprehension.** 已经超出了我的理解力。

**When I looked at him** 【情境】当我看向他时，

**he had finished reading the note,** 他已经读完了那张条子，

**and his eyes had assumed the vacant, lack-lustre expression** → 眼中呈现出一种空洞而黯淡的神情，

**which showed mental abstraction.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的神情？→ 显示出他正在出神的那种。

---

**"How in the world did you deduce that?" I asked.** "你到底是怎么推断出来的？"我问。

---

**"Deduce what?" said he, petulantly.** "推断什么？"他不耐烦地说。

---

**"Why, that he was a retired sergeant of Marines."** "就是他是退役的海军陆战队军士这件事啊。"

---

**"I have no time for trifles," he answered, brusquely;** "我没时间管这种小事，"他生硬地回答；

**then with a smile,** 然后笑了笑，

**"Excuse my rudeness.** "原谅我的粗鲁。

**You broke the thread of my thoughts;** 你打断了我的思路；

**but perhaps it is as well.** 不过也许这样也好。

**So you actually were not able to see** 那么你确实没有看出来——

**that that man was a sergeant of Marines?"** 那个人是海军陆战队的军士？"

---

**"No, indeed."** "确实没有。"

---

**"It was easier to know it** "知道这件事倒是容易——

**than to explain why I knew it.** 【对比】比起要解释我是怎么知道的，反而容易多了。

**If you were asked to prove** 【条件】如果有人要你证明

**that two and two made four,** 二加二等于四，

**you might find some difficulty,** 你可能也会觉得有困难，

**and yet you are quite sure of the fact.** 【转折】但你完全确信这个事实。

**Even across the street** 即使隔着一条街，

**I could see a great blue anchor** 我也能看到一个大大的蓝色锚，

**tattooed on the back of the fellow's hand.** [分词-后置修饰] 纹在哪？→ 纹在那家伙的手背上。

**That smacked of the sea.** 这一看就跟海有关。

**He had a military carriage, however,** 【转折】不过，他有着军人的举止，

**and regulation side whiskers.** → 和标准的鬓角。

**There we have the marine.** 这就是海军陆战队了。

**He was a man with some amount of self-importance** 他是一个有些自负的人，

**and a certain air of command.** → 带着一种指挥者的气派。

**You must have observed the way** 你一定注意到了——

**in which he held his head and swung his cane.** 他昂头和挥手杖的样子。

**A steady, respectable, middle-aged man, too,** 而且一看就是个稳重、体面的中年人，

**on the face of him** 从他脸上就能看出来——

**—all facts which led me to believe** 所有这些事实加在一起，让我相信

**that he had been a sergeant."** 他曾经是一名军士。"

---

**"Wonderful!" I ejaculated.** "太精彩了！"我叫道。

---

**"Commonplace," said Holmes,** "稀松平常，"福尔摩斯说，

**though I thought from his expression** 【让步→主张推测】不过我从他的表情判断，

**that he was pleased at my evident surprise and admiration.** 他对我明显的惊讶和钦佩感到很高兴。

**"I said just now that there were no criminals.** "我刚才还说没有什么罪犯了。

**It appears that I am wrong** 看来我错了——

**—look at this!"** 看看这个！"

**He threw me over the note** 他把那张条子扔给了我，

**which the commissionaire had brought.** [定从-句尾补充] 就是那个跑腿的送来的。

---

**"Why," I cried,** "天哪，"我叫道，

**as I cast my eye over it,** 【情境】当我扫了一眼时，

**"this is terrible!"** "这太可怕了！"

---

**"It does seem to be a little out** "看起来确实有些不同寻常，
**of the common," he remarked, calmly.** → "他平静地说。

**"Would you mind reading it to me aloud?"** "你介意大声读给我听吗？"

---

**This is the letter which I read to him—** 以下就是我读给他听的那封信——

**"MY DEAR MR. SHERLOCK HOLMES,—** "亲爱的歇洛克·福尔摩斯先生——

**"There has been a bad business during the night** "昨晚发生了一桩坏事，

**at 3, Lauriston Gardens,** 在哪？→ 在劳里斯顿花园街3号，

**off the Brixton Road.** 在哪一带？→ 布里克斯顿路旁边。

**Our man on the beat saw a light there** 我们的巡警看到那里有灯光，

**about two in the morning,** 在什么时候？→ 大约凌晨两点，

**and as the house was an empty one,** 【原因】由于那栋房子是空的，

**suspected that something was amiss.** 怀疑出了什么事。

**He found the door open,** 他发现门是开着的，

**and in the front room,** → 在前面的房间里——

**which is bare of furniture,** [定从-句中插入] 所谓这个房间，是没有家具的。← 回来 →

**discovered the body of a gentleman,** 发现了一具男子的尸体。

**well dressed,** [分词-后置修饰] 衣着讲究的，

**and having cards in his pocket** → 口袋里有名片，

**bearing the name of 'Enoch J. Drebber, Cleveland, Ohio, U.S.A.'** [分词-后置修饰] 名片上写着什么？→ '伊诺克·J·德雷伯，美国俄亥俄州克利夫兰'。

**There had been no robbery,** 没有被抢劫的迹象，

**nor is there any evidence** → 【转折】也没有任何证据，

**as to how the man met his death.** 关于什么？→ 关于此人是如何死的。

**There are marks of blood in the room,** 房间里有血迹。

**but there is no wound upon his person.** 【转折】但他身上没有伤口。

**We are at a loss** 我们完全不知道

**as to how he came into the empty house;** 不知道什么？→ 他是怎么进入这栋空房子的；

**indeed, the whole affair is a puzzler.** 说实话，整件事是个谜。

**If you can come round to the house** 【条件】如果你能来这栋房子一趟，

**any time before twelve,** 在十二点之前任何时候，

**you will find me there.** 你会找到我在那里。

**I have left everything _in statu quo_** 我把一切都保持了原状，

**until I hear from you.** 直到收到你的消息。

**If you are unable to come** 【条件】如果你不能来的话，

**I shall give you fuller details,** 【结果】我会给你提供更详细的情况，

**and would esteem it a great kindness** → 而且如果你能赐教，

**if you would favour me with your opinion.** 我将不胜感激。

**Yours faithfully, TOBIAS GREGSON."** 忠实的，托拜厄斯·格雷格森。"

---

**"Gregson is the smartest of the Scotland Yarders,"** "格雷格森是苏格兰场里最聪明的，
**my friend remarked;** → "我的朋友说，

**"he and Lestrade are the pick of a bad lot.** "他和雷斯垂德算是矬子里拔将军了。

**They are both quick and energetic,** 他们俩都很敏捷、精力充沛，

**but conventional—shockingly so.** 【转折】但都很守旧——而且守旧得吓人。

**They have their knives into one another, too.** 他们俩还互相看不顺眼。

**They are as jealous as a pair of professional beauties.** 他们争风吃醋的程度，就像一对职业美人。

**There will be some fun over this case** 如果他们俩都被派去查这个案子，

**if they are both put upon the scent."** 那可有好戏看了。"

---

**I was amazed at the calm way** 我惊讶于——

**in which he rippled on.** 他那种若无其事侃侃而谈的方式。

**"Surely there is not a moment to be** "一分钟都不能耽搁了吧，
**lost," I cried,** → "我叫道，

**"shall I go and order you a cab?"** "要不要我去帮你叫辆马车？"

---

**"I'm not sure about whether I shall go.** "我还不确定要不要去。

**I am the most incurably lazy devil** 我是世上最无可救药的懒鬼——

**that ever stood in shoe leather** [定从-句尾补充] 穿过鞋的人里最懒的那种——

**—that is, when the fit is on me,** 我是说，当我犯懒的时候，

**for I can be spry enough at times."** 【转折】因为有时候我也能挺麻利的。"

---

**"Why, it is just such a chance** "可这正是一个机会啊——

**as you have been longing for."** 你一直渴望的那种机会。"

---

**"My dear fellow, what does it matter to me.** "老伙计，这跟我有什么关系。

**Supposing I unravel the whole matter,** 【假设情况】假设我把整件事解开了，

**you may be sure** 【实际结果】你可以确信——

**that Gregson, Lestrade, and Co. will pocket all the credit.** 格雷格森、雷斯垂德他们会把所有功劳揽走。

**That comes of being an unofficial personage."** 谁让我不是官方人员呢。"

---

**"But he begs you to help him."** "可是他恳求你帮忙啊。"

---

**"Yes. He knows that I am his superior,** "是的。他知道我比他强，

**and acknowledges it to me;** → 也在我面前承认；

**but he would cut his tongue out** 【转折】但他宁可割了自己的舌头，

**before he would own it to any third person.** 也不会在第三个人面前承认。

**However, we may as well go and have a look.** 【转折】不过，去看看也无妨。

**I shall work it out on my own hook.** 我会靠自己把它解开。

**I may have a laugh at them** 也许我能笑话他们一番，

**if I have nothing else.** 就算别的什么都没有。

**Come on!"** 走吧！"

---

**He hustled on his overcoat,** 他急忙穿上大衣，

**and bustled about in a way** → 忙活起来——

**that showed that an energetic fit had superseded** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的忙活法？
**the apathetic one.** → 说明一阵充沛的干劲已经取代了刚才的无精打采。

---

**"Get your hat," he said.** "拿上你的帽子，"他说。

---

**"You wish me to come?"** "你要我一起去？"

---

**"Yes, if you have nothing better to do."** "是的，如果你没有更好的事要做的话。"

**A minute later we were both in a hansom,** 一分钟后我们俩都坐在一辆双轮马车里了，

**driving furiously for the Brixton Road.** 疯狂地朝布里克斯顿路驶去。

---

**It was a foggy, cloudy morning,** 那是一个有雾的、多云的早晨，

**and a dun-coloured veil hung over the house-tops,** → 一层灰褐色的薄纱笼罩在屋顶上，

**looking like the reflection of the mud-coloured streets beneath.** [分词-句末伴随] 看起来像什么？→ 像是下面泥色街道的倒影。

**My companion was in the best of spirits,** 我的同伴心情极好，

**and prattled away about Cremona fiddles,** → 喋喋不休地聊着克雷莫纳小提琴，

**and the difference between a Stradivarius and an Amati.** → 以及斯特拉迪瓦里和阿马蒂之间的区别。

**As for myself, I was silent,** 至于我，我沉默着，

**for the dull weather and the melancholy business** 【原因】因为阴沉的天气和我们正在处理的忧郁事务——

**upon which we were engaged,** [介词-后置修饰] 什么样的事务？→ 我们正在处理的，

**depressed my spirits.** 让我的心情很低落。

---

**"You don't seem to give much thought to** "你好像没怎么考虑手头的事情，
**the matter in hand," I said at last,** → "我终于说道，

**interrupting Holmes' musical disquisition.** [分词-句末伴随] 打断了福尔摩斯关于音乐的长篇大论。

---

**"No data yet," he answered.** "还没有数据呢，"他回答。

**"It is a capital mistake to theorize** "在你掌握所有证据之前就开始推理，

**before you have all the evidence.** 那是一个大错。

**It biases the judgment."** 这会让判断产生偏见。"

---

**"You will have your data soon," I remarked,** "你很快就能拿到数据了，"我说，

**pointing with my finger;** [分词-句末伴随] 用手指着，

**"this is the Brixton Road,** "这就是布里克斯顿路，

**and that is the house,** → 那就是那栋房子，

**if I am not very much mistaken."** 如果我没看错的话。"

---

**"So it is. Stop, driver, stop!"** "没错。停车，车夫，停车！"

**We were still a hundred yards or so from it,** 我们离那里还有大约一百码，

**but he insisted upon our alighting,** 【转折】但他坚持要我们下车，

**and we finished our journey upon foot.** → 剩下的路我们步行走完。

---

**Number 3, Lauriston Gardens wore an ill-omened and minatory look.** 劳里斯顿花园街3号有一种不祥而威胁的外观。

**It was one of four** 它是四栋房子中的一栋，

**which stood back some little way from the street,** [定从-句尾补充] 这四栋房子从街道稍稍退后了一些，

**two being occupied and two empty.** 两栋有人住，两栋空着。

**The latter looked out with three tiers of** 空着的那两栋朝外望去，
**vacant melancholy windows,** → 是三层空洞而忧郁的窗户，

**which were blank and dreary,** [定从-句尾补充] 这些窗户阴暗凄凉，

**save that here and there** 除了这里那里——

**a "To Let" card had developed like a** 一块"招租"牌子像白内障一样长在了模糊的玻璃窗上。
**cataract upon the bleared panes.** →

**A small garden** 一个小花园

**sprinkled over with a scattered eruption of sickly plants** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的花园？→ 零星散布着几株病恹恹的植物，

**separated each of these houses from the street,** ← 回来 → 把每栋房子和街道隔开，

**and was traversed by a narrow pathway,** → 中间有一条窄小的人行道穿过，

**yellowish in colour,** 颜色泛黄，

**and consisting apparently of a mixture of clay** → 看起来是黏土和碎石的混合物。
**and of gravel.** →

**The whole place was very sloppy** 整个地方非常泥泞，

**from the rain which had fallen through the night.** 【原因】因为什么？→ 因为夜里一直在下雨。

**The garden was bounded by a three-foot brick wall** 花园的边界是一道三英尺高的砖墙，

**with a fringe of wood rails upon the top,** [with-描述特点] 墙顶上什么样？→ 上面有一排木栏杆，

**and against this wall was leaning a stalwart police constable,** → 一个身材壮实的警察靠在这面墙上，

**surrounded by a small knot of loafers,** [分词-后置修饰] 被什么围着？→ 被一小群闲人围着，

**who craned their necks and strained their eyes** [定从-句尾补充] 这些闲人伸长脖子、瞪大眼睛，

**in the vain hope of catching some glimpse** 怀着什么希望？→ 怀着徒劳的希望，
**of the proceedings within.** → 想瞥见里面正在发生的事情。

---

**I had imagined** 我本以为

**that Sherlock Holmes would at once have hurried** 歇洛克·福尔摩斯会马上冲进房子，
**into the house** →

**and plunged into a study of the mystery.** → 一头扎进对这个谜案的研究中。

**Nothing appeared to be further from his intention.** 【转折】但他似乎完全没有这个打算。

**With an air of nonchalance** 带着一种漫不经心的态度——

**which, under the circumstances,** [定从-句中插入] 什么样的态度？→ 在当时的情况下，
**seemed to me to border upon affectation,** → 在我看来简直近乎做作。← 回来 →

**he lounged up and down the pavement,** 他在人行道上悠闲地来回踱步，

**and gazed vacantly at the ground,** → 茫然地望着地面、
**the sky, the opposite houses** → 天空、
**and the line of railings.** → 对面的房子和栏杆。

**Having finished his scrutiny,** [分词-句首状语] 完成了这番审视之后 →

**he proceeded slowly down the path,** 他慢慢沿着小路走去——

**or rather down the fringe of grass** 确切地说，
**which flanked the path,** → 是沿着小路旁边的草地边缘走，

**keeping his eyes riveted upon the ground.** [分词-句末伴随] 目光紧盯着地面。

**Twice he stopped,** 他停了两次，

**and once I saw him smile,** → 有一次我看见他笑了，

**and heard him utter an exclamation of satisfaction.** → 还听到他发出满意的叫声。

**There were many marks of footsteps upon the** 潮湿的黏土上有许多脚印，
**wet clayey soil,** →

**but since the police had been coming** 【原因】但由于警察在上面走来走去，
**and going over it,** →

**I was unable to see** 我看不出来——

**how my companion could hope to learn anything from it.** 我的同伴怎么可能指望从中学到什么。

**Still I had had such extraordinary evidence** 【转折】不过我已经见识了——

**of the quickness of his perceptive faculties,** 什么的证据？→ 他的感知力之敏锐而非凡证据，

**that I had no doubt** 以至于我毫不怀疑——

**that he could see a great deal** 他能看到许多对我来说隐藏着的东西。
**which was hidden from me.** →

---

**At the door of the house** 在房子门口，

**we were met by a tall, white-faced, flaxen-haired man,** 迎接我们的是一个高个子、面色苍白、淡黄头发的人，

**with a notebook in his hand,** [with-描述特点] 手里拿着什么？→ 一个笔记本，

**who rushed forward** [定从-句尾补充] 他冲上前来，

**and wrung my companion's hand with effusion.** → 热情地紧握我同伴的手。

**"It is indeed kind of you to come," he said,** "你能来真是太好了，"他说，

**"I have had everything left untouched."** "我把一切都保持了原样。"

---

**"Except that!" my friend answered,** "除了那个！"我的朋友回答，

**pointing at the pathway.** [分词-句末伴随] 指着小路。

**"If a herd of buffaloes had passed along** 【假设情况】就算一群野牛从这里走过，

**there could not be a greater mess.** 也不可能比现在更乱了。

**No doubt, however, you had drawn your own conclusions, Gregson,** 【转折】不过，格雷格森，你想必在之前就已经得出自己的结论了，

**before you permitted this."** 在你允许这种情况发生之前。"

---

**"I have had so much to do inside the house,"** "我在屋里有太多事要做了，"

**the detective said evasively.** 侦探含糊地说。

**"My colleague, Mr. Lestrade, is here.** "我的同事雷斯垂德先生在这里。

**I had relied upon him to look after this."** 我原本指望他来管这事的。"

---

**Holmes glanced at me** 福尔摩斯瞥了我一眼，

**and raised his eyebrows sardonically.** → 讥讽地挑了挑眉毛。

**"With two such men** →
**as yourself and Lestrade upon the ground,** → "有你和雷斯垂德这样的两位在现场，

**there will not be much** 第三方大概也发现不了什么了，
**for a third party to find out," he said.** → "他说。

---

**Gregson rubbed his hands in a self-satisfied way.** 格雷格森自鸣得意地搓了搓手。

**"I think we have done all** "我想我们已经做了所有能做的，
**that can be done," he answered;** → "他回答；

**"it's a queer case though,** "不过这确实是个古怪的案子，

**and I knew your taste for such things."** → 而我知道你对这类事情的兴趣。"

---

**"You did not come here in a cab?"** "你不是坐马车来的吧？
**asked Sherlock Holmes.** → "歇洛克·福尔摩斯问。

**"No, sir."** "不是的，先生。"

**"Nor Lestrade?"** "雷斯垂德也不是？"

**"No, sir."** "不是的，先生。"

---

**"Then let us go and look at the room."** "那我们去看看那个房间吧。"

**With which inconsequent remark** 说了这句莫名其妙的话之后，

**he strode on into the house,** 他大步走进了房子，

**followed by Gregson,** [分词-句末伴随] 后面跟着格雷格森，

**whose features expressed his astonishment.** [定从-句尾补充] 他脸上的表情流露出惊讶。

---

**A short passage, bare planked and dusty,** 一条短短的走廊——光秃秃的木板地面，满是灰尘——

**led to the kitchen and offices.** 通往厨房和各个附属房间。

**Two doors opened out of it to the** 走廊左右各开着一扇门。
**left and to the right.** →

**One of these had obviously been closed for many weeks.** 其中一扇显然已经关了好几个星期了。

**The other belonged to the dining-room,** 另一扇属于餐厅，

**which was the apartment** [定从-句尾补充] 所谓这间餐厅，就是——

**in which the mysterious affair had occurred.** 神秘事件发生的那个房间。

**Holmes walked in,** 福尔摩斯走了进去，

**and I followed him** → 我跟在他后面，

**with that subdued feeling at my heart** [with-描述状态] 带着什么感觉？→ 带着那种沉重的感觉——

**which the presence of death inspires.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的感觉？→ 死亡的存在所激发的那种。

---

**It was a large square room,** 这是一间方方正正的大房间，

**looking all the larger from the absence of all furniture.** [分词-句末伴随] 由于完全没有家具，显得更加空旷。

**A vulgar flaring paper adorned the walls,** 墙上贴着一种花哨俗气的壁纸，

**but it was blotched in places with mildew,** 【转折】但有些地方已经被霉斑沾污了，

**and here and there great strips had become** → 这里那里，
**detached and hung down,** → 大片的壁纸已经脱落下垂，

**exposing the yellow plaster beneath.** [分词-句末伴随] 露出了什么？→ 下面发黄的石膏。

**Opposite the door was a showy fireplace,** 门对面是一个醒目的壁炉，

**surmounted by a mantelpiece of imitation white marble.** [分词-后置修饰] 上面有什么？→ 有一个仿白色大理石的壁炉架。

**On one corner of this was stuck the** 壁炉架的一角插着一截红蜡烛头。
**stump of a red wax candle.** →

**The solitary window was so dirty** 那扇孤零零的窗户非常脏，

**that the light was hazy and uncertain,** 以至于光线朦胧而不确定，

**giving a dull grey tinge to everything,** [分词-句末伴随] 使一切都蒙上了一层灰暗的色调，

**which was intensified by the thick layer of dust** [定从-句尾补充] 这种灰暗还被什么加剧？→ 被厚厚的一层灰尘，

**which coated the whole apartment.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的灰尘？→ 覆盖整个房间的。

---

**All these details I observed afterwards.** 这些细节都是后来我才注意到的。

**At present my attention was centred upon the** 此刻我的注意力集中在一个唯一的、
**single grim motionless figure** → 阴森的、一动不动的人形上，

**which lay stretched upon the boards,** [定从-句尾补充] 这个人形平躺在地板上，

**with vacant sightless eyes staring up at the discoloured ceiling.** [with-描述状态] 什么状态？→ 空洞无神的眼睛凝视着变色的天花板。

**It was that of a man** 那是一个男人——

**about forty-three or forty-four years of age,** 大约四十三四岁，

**middle-sized, broad shouldered,** 中等身材，肩膀宽阔，

**with crisp curling black hair,** [with-描述特点] 带着什么？→ 一头卷曲的黑发，

**and a short stubbly beard.** → 留着短短的胡茬。

**He was dressed in a heavy broadcloth frock** 他穿着一件厚重的呢绒大礼服外套和马甲，
**coat and waistcoat,** →

**with light-coloured trousers,** [with-描述特点] 还有浅色的裤子，

**and immaculate collar and cuffs.** → 以及整洁无瑕的衣领和袖口。

**A top hat, well brushed and trim,** 一顶高礼帽——刷得很干净、很整齐——

**was placed upon the floor beside him.** 放在他身旁的地板上。

**His hands were clenched** 他的双手紧握，

**and his arms thrown abroad,** → 双臂张开，

**while his lower limbs were interlocked** → 他的双腿交缠在一起——

**as though his death struggle had been a grievous one.** 仿佛他经历了一场痛苦的垂死挣扎。

**On his rigid face there stood an expression of horror,** 他僵硬的脸上呈现出一种恐惧的表情，

**and as it seemed to me, of hatred,** → 在我看来还有仇恨的表情，

**such as I have never seen upon human features.** 这种表情我从未在人类的面孔上见过。

**This malignant and terrible contortion,** 这种恶毒而可怕的扭曲——

**combined with the low forehead, blunt nose, and prognathous jaw** [分词-后置修饰] 与什么结合在一起？→ 与低矮的额头、钝圆的鼻子和前突的下颌——

**gave the dead man a singularly simious and ape-like appearance,** ← 回来 → 使这个死者呈现出一种异常猿猴般的外貌，

**which was increased by his writhing, unnatural posture.** [定从-句尾补充] 这种外貌还被什么加剧了？→ 被他扭曲的、不自然的姿势。

**I have seen death in many forms,** 我见过各种形式的死亡，

**but never has it appeared to me in** 【转折】但从来没有以更可怕的面貌出现在我面前，
**a more fearsome aspect** →

**than in that dark grimy apartment,** 比起什么？→ 比起在那间阴暗肮脏的房间里——

**which looked out upon one of the main** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的房间？
**arteries of suburban London.** → 面朝伦敦郊区主要大道之一的。

---

**Lestrade, lean and ferret-like as ever,** 雷斯垂德——一如既往地消瘦，像只雪貂——

**was standing by the doorway,** 站在门口，

**and greeted my companion and myself.** → 跟我的同伴和我打了招呼。

---

**"This case will make a stir, sir," he remarked.** "这个案子会轰动的，先生，"他说。

**"It beats anything I have seen,** "我见过的所有案子里它是最厉害的，

**and I am no chicken."** → 而我也不是新手了。"

---

**"There is no clue?" said Gregson.** "没有线索吗？"格雷格森说。

**"None at all," chimed in Lestrade.** "一点也没有，"雷斯垂德附和道。

---

**Sherlock Holmes approached the body,** 歇洛克·福尔摩斯走近尸体，

**and, kneeling down, examined it intently.** → 跪下来，仔细地检查。

**"You are sure that there is no wound?" he asked,** "你确定没有伤口吗？"他问，

**pointing to numerous gouts and splashes of blood** [分词-句末伴随] 指着大量的血迹和血点，

**which lay all round.** [定从-句尾补充] 散落在周围。

---

**"Positive!" cried both detectives.** "确定无疑！"两位侦探同时叫道。

---

**"Then, of course, this blood belongs to a second individual** "那么，当然，这些血属于第二个人——

**—presumably the murderer,** 很可能就是凶手，

**if murder has been committed.** 【条件】如果确实发生了谋杀的话。→ 

**It reminds me of the circumstances** 这让我想起了那些情况——

**attendant on the death of Van Jansen,** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的情况？→ 与范·扬森之死相关的，

**in Utrecht, in the year '34.** 在哪？→ 在乌特勒支，一八三四年。

**Do you remember the case, Gregson?"** 格雷格森，你记得这个案子吗？"

---

**"No, sir."** "不记得，先生。"

---

**"Read it up—you really should.** "去查查看——你真的应该看看。

**There is nothing new under the sun.** 太阳底下无新事。

**It has all been done before."** 所有的事情以前都发生过了。"

---

**As he spoke,** 他说着，

**his nimble fingers were flying here, there, and everywhere,** 他灵活的手指在这里、那里、到处飞舞，

**feeling, pressing, unbuttoning, examining,** [分词-句末伴随] 触摸着、按压着、解开扣子、检查着，

**while his eyes wore the same far-away expression** 【情境】同时他的眼中带着那种遥远的表情——

**which I have already remarked upon.** [定从-句尾补充] 就是我之前已经提到过的那种。

**So swiftly was the examination made,** 检查进行得如此迅速，

**that one would hardly have guessed** 以至于你几乎猜不到——

**the minuteness with which it was conducted.** 这次检查是以多么细致入微的方式进行的。

**Finally, he sniffed the dead man's lips,** 最后，他嗅了嗅死者的嘴唇，

**and then glanced at the soles of his** → 然后看了看他漆皮皮靴的鞋底。
**patent leather boots.** →

---

**"He has not been moved at all?" he asked.** "他完全没有被移动过吗？"他问。

**"No more than was necessary** →
**for the purposes of our examination."** → "只在我们检查需要的范围内动过。

**"You can take him to the mortuary now," he said.** "现在可以把他送到停尸房去了，"他说。

**"There is nothing more to be learned."** "已经没什么可学的了。"

---

**Gregson had a stretcher and four men at hand.** 格雷格森手边有一副担架和四个人。

**At his call they entered the room,** 一声招呼，他们走进房间，

**and the stranger was lifted and carried out.** → 那个陌生人被抬起来运了出去。

**As they raised him,** 【情境】当他们抬起他的时候，

**a ring tinkled down and rolled across the floor.** 一枚戒指叮当一声掉下来，滚过地板。

**Lestrade grabbed it up** 雷斯垂德一把捡起来，

**and stared at it with mystified eyes.** → 困惑不解地盯着它看。

---

**"There's been a woman here," he cried.** "有个女人来过，"他叫道。

**"It's a woman's wedding-ring."** "这是一枚女人的结婚戒指。"

---

**He held it out,** 他说着，
**as he spoke,** → 把它摊在手掌上。
**upon the palm of his hand.** →

**We all gathered round him and gazed at it.** 我们都围了过来看。

**There could be no doubt** 毫无疑问——

**that that circlet of plain gold** 那个素金的圆环

**had once adorned the finger of a bride.** 曾经戴在一位新娘的手指上。

---

**"This complicates matters," said Gregson.** "这使事情复杂化了，"格雷格森说。

**"Heaven knows, they were complicated enough before."** "天知道，以前就已经够复杂的了。"

---

**"You're sure it doesn't simplify them?" observed Holmes.** "你确定它没有使事情简化吗？"福尔摩斯说。

**"There's nothing to be learned by staring at it.** "盯着它看什么也学不到。

**What did you find in his pockets?"** 你在他口袋里发现了什么？"

---

**"We have it all here," said Gregson,** "都在这里了，"格雷格森说，

**pointing to a litter of objects upon one** [分词-句末伴随] 指着楼梯底部台阶上的一堆物品。
**of the bottom steps of the stairs.** →

**"A gold watch, No. 97163, by Barraud, of London.** "一只金表，编号97163，伦敦巴罗德制造。

**Gold Albert chain, very heavy and solid.** 金色阿尔伯特表链，很重很结实。

**Gold ring, with masonic device.** 金戒指，上面有共济会标志。

**Gold pin—bull-dog's head, with rubies as eyes.** 金别针——牛头犬头造型，用红宝石做眼睛。

**Russian leather card-case,** 俄国皮名片夹，

**with cards of Enoch J. Drebber of Cleveland,** 里面有克利夫兰的伊诺克·J·德雷伯的名片，

**corresponding with the E. J. D. upon the linen.** 与衬衫上的 E.J.D. 缩写相符。

**No purse, but loose money to the extent** 没有钱包，但有散钱，
**of seven pounds thirteen.** → 总共七英镑十三先令。

**Pocket edition of Boccaccio's _Decameron_,** 袖珍版薄伽丘的《十日谈》，

**with name of Joseph Stangerson upon the fly-leaf.** 扉页上写着约瑟夫·斯坦格森的名字。

**Two letters** 两封信——

**—one addressed to E. J. Drebber** 一封写给 E.J. 德雷伯，

**and one to Joseph Stangerson."** → 一封写给约瑟夫·斯坦格森。"

---

**"At what address?"** "写的什么地址？"

---

**"American Exchange, Strand** "河滨大道的美国交易所——

**—to be left till called for.** 留存待取。

**They are both from the Guion Steamship Company,** 两封都来自吉昂轮船公司，

**and refer to the sailing of their boats from Liverpool.** → 内容是关于他们从利物浦出发的船期。

**It is clear that this unfortunate man** 很明显，这个不幸的人

**was about to return to New York."** 正准备返回纽约。"

---

**"Have you made any inquiries as to this man, Stangerson?"** "你调查过这个人——斯坦格森吗？"

---

**"I did it at once, sir," said Gregson.** "我马上就做了，先生，"格雷格森说。

**"I have had advertisements sent to all the newspapers,** "我已经把广告发到了所有报纸上，

**and one of my men has gone to** → 我的一个手下也去了美国交易所，
**the American Exchange,** →

**but he has not returned yet."** 【转折】但还没回来。"

---

**"Have you sent to Cleveland?"** "你有没有发电报到克利夫兰？"

**"We telegraphed this morning."** "今早发了。"

**"How did you word your inquiries?"** "你们怎么措辞的？"

---

**"We simply detailed the circumstances,** "我们只是详述了情况，

**and said that we should be glad of any information** → 说我们欢迎任何信息——

**which could help us."** [定从-句尾补充] 能帮到我们的。"

---

**"You did not ask for particulars on any point** "你没有就任何你觉得关键的要点

**which appeared to you to be crucial?"** [定从-句尾补充] 问具体的情况？"

---

**"I asked about Stangerson."** "我问了斯坦格森的事。"

---

**"Nothing else?** "没别的了？

**Is there no circumstance** 难道没有什么情况

**on which this whole case appears to hinge?** [介词-前置修饰] 整个案子似乎就系于其上的？
