**and was dashing in** → 飞奔进来——

**as she had done many a time before,** 就像她以前做过许多次的那样——

**with all the fearlessness of youth,** [with-描述状态] 带着什么？→ 带着年轻人特有的无所畏惧——

**thinking only of her task** [分词-句末伴随] 心里想着什么？→ 只想着她的差事，
**and how it was to be performed.** → 以及该怎么完成它。

**The travel-stained adventurers gazed after her in astonishment,** 风尘仆仆的冒险者们惊讶地目送着她——

**and even the unemotional Indians,** → 甚至连冷漠的印第安人——

**journeying in with their pelties,** [分词-后置修饰] 带着什么进城的？→ 带着毛皮进城的——

**relaxed their accustomed stoicism** ← 回来接谓语 → 也放下了他们惯常的冷淡——

**as they marvelled at the beauty of the pale-faced maiden.** 【情境·当】当他们惊叹于这位面色白皙的少女的美貌时。

---

**She had reached the outskirts of the city** 她已经到达城郊——

**when she found the road blocked** 【情境·这时】发现路被堵住了——

**by a great drove of cattle,** 被什么堵的？→ 被一大群牲口——

**driven by a half-dozen wild-looking herdsmen from the plains.** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的牲口？→ 由六七个看起来野蛮的平原牧人赶着的那群。

**In her impatience** 在她的不耐烦中——

**she endeavoured to pass this obstacle** 她试图越过这道障碍——

**by pushing her horse into what appeared to** 怎么越过？
**be a gap.** → 把马挤进一个看上去像是缺口的地方。

**Scarcely had she got fairly into it, however,** 【情境·转折·倒装强调】可她几乎刚刚钻进去——

**before the beasts closed in behind her,** 【情境·紧跟着】牲口就从身后合拢了——

**and she found herself completely imbedded** → 她发现自己完全被包裹在——

**in the moving stream of fierce-eyed, long-horned bullocks.** 什么里面？→ 那群眼神凶悍、长角公牛组成的移动洪流里。

**Accustomed as she was to deal with cattle,** 【让步】虽然她惯于应对牲畜——

**she was not alarmed at her situation,** 【主张】她并不因此处境而惊慌——

**but took advantage of every opportunity** 【转折】而是抓住一切机会——

**to urge her horse on** 努力做什么？→ 催马前行——

**in the hopes of pushing her way through the cavalcade.** 【目的】为了什么？→ 为了从这群牲口中挤出一条路。

**Unfortunately** 不幸的是——

**the horns of one of the creatures,** 其中一头的角——

**either by accident or design,** [插入修饰] 不管是不是故意——

**came in violent contact with the flank of the mustang,** ← 回来接谓语 → 猛烈地撞上了那匹野马的侧腹——

**and excited it to madness.** → 把它激得发狂了。

**In an instant** 就在一瞬间——

**it reared up upon its hind legs** 它后腿直立——

**with a snort of rage,** [with-描述状态] 带着什么？→ 带着一声愤怒的鼻息——

**and pranced and tossed** → 踢腾着、甩头——

**in a way** 以一种方式——

**that would have unseated any but a most skilful rider.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的方式？→ 任何一个不够熟练的骑手都会被甩下去的那种。

**The situation was full of peril.** 形势充满了危险。

**Every plunge of the excited horse** 那匹激动的马每一次猛冲——

**brought it against the horns again,** 都让它再次撞上牛角——

**and goaded it to fresh madness.** → 刺激它愈加狂怒。

**It was all that the girl could do** 姑娘已经尽了全力——

**to keep herself in the saddle,** 尽力做什么？→ 维持在马背上——

**yet a slip would mean** 【转折·假设】但一旦失手就意味着——

**a terrible death under the hoofs of the** 什么死法？
**unwieldy and terrified animals.** → 死在那些笨拙而受惊的牲口蹄下的惨死。

**Unaccustomed to sudden emergencies,** [分词-句首状语] 不习惯突如其来的危急——

**her head began to swim,** 她开始头晕目眩——

**and her grip upon the bridle to relax.** → 握着缰绳的手也开始松弛。

**Choked by the rising cloud of dust** [分词-句首状语] 被升腾的尘雾呛着——

**and by the steam from the struggling creatures,** → 还被那些挣扎牲口散发的热气熏着——

**she might have abandoned her efforts in despair,** 她几乎要绝望地放弃——

**but for a kindly voice at her elbow** 【转折·虚拟】要不是她耳边传来一个亲切的声音——

**which assured her of assistance.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么声音？→ 让她放心会有人帮她的那个。

**At the same moment** 就在同一时刻——

**a sinewy brown hand caught the frightened horse** 一只筋腱结实的棕色大手抓住了那匹受惊的马的缰绳—
**by the curb,** → —

**and forcing a way through the drove,** [分词-句末伴随] → 从牛群中强行挤出一条路——

**soon brought her to the outskirts.** → 很快就把她带到了外围。

---

**"You're not hurt, I hope, miss," said her preserver, respectfully.** "我希望你没受伤，小姐，"她的救命恩人恭敬地说。

---

**She looked up at his dark, fierce face,** 她抬起头看着他那张黝黑、英武的脸——

**and laughed saucily.** → 俏皮地笑了。

**"I'm awful frightened," she said, naively;** "我可吓坏了，"她天真地说；

**"whoever would have thought** "谁能想到——

**that Poncho would have been so scared** 想到什么？→ 庞乔会被——

**by a lot of cows?"** 一群牛吓成这样？"

---

**"Thank God you kept your seat," the other said earnestly.** "感谢上帝你没被甩下去，"另一人认真地说。

**He was a tall, savage-looking young fellow,** 他是一个高挑、样子凶悍的年轻人——

**mounted on a powerful roan horse,** [分词-后置修饰] 骑着什么？→ 骑着一匹强壮的红鬃马——

**and clad in the rough dress of a hunter,** → 穿着猎人的粗犷装束——

**with a long rifle slung over his shoulders.** [with-描述特点] 带着什么？→ 背上挎着一把长步枪。

**"I guess you are the daughter of John** "我猜你是约翰·费瑞尔的女儿，
**Ferrier," he remarked,** → "他说——

**"I saw you ride down from his house.** "我看见你从他家骑马下来。

**When you see him,** 【情境·当】你见到他的时候——

**ask him if he remembers the Jefferson Hopes** 问问他是否记得圣路易斯的杰弗逊·霍普家。
**of St. Louis.** →

**If he's the same Ferrier,** 【条件·心悬着】如果是同一个费瑞尔——

**my father and he were pretty thick."** 【结果落地】我父亲和他当年很要好。"

---

**"Hadn't you better come and ask yourself?" she asked, demurely.** "你自己来问不是更好吗？"她文静地问道。

---

**The young fellow seemed pleased at the suggestion,** 那年轻人对这个建议似乎很满意——

**and his dark eyes sparkled with pleasure.** → 他那双黑眼睛闪着愉悦的光芒。

**"I'll do so," he said,** "我会去的，"他说——

**"we've been in the mountains for two months,** "我们在山里待了两个月——

**and are not over and above in visiting condition.** → 现在的状态并不是很适合去串门。

**He must take us as he finds us."** 他只能照我们现在的样子接受了。"

---

**"He has a good deal to thank you for,** "他非常感激你——

**and so have I," she answered,** → 我也是，"她回答——

**"he's awful fond of me.** "他非常疼我。

**If those cows had jumped on me** 【条件·心悬着】要是那些牛踩到我——

**he'd have never got over it."** 【结果落地】他永远都不会好的。"

---

**"Neither would I," said her companion.** "我也是，"她的同伴说。

---

**"You! Well, I don't see** "你！我不明白——

**that it would make much matter to you, anyhow.** 这对你有什么重要的，反正。

**You ain't even a friend of ours."** 你甚至都不是我们的朋友。"

---

**The young hunter's dark face** 那年轻猎人黝黑的脸——

**grew so gloomy over this remark** 因为这句话变得那么阴沉——【心悬着：so ... that】

**that Lucy Ferrier laughed aloud.** 【兑现】阴沉到什么程度？→ 以至于露西·费瑞尔大声笑了起来。

---

**"There, I didn't mean that," she said;** "哎，我不是那个意思，"她说；

**"of course, you are a friend now.** "当然了，你现在是朋友了。

**You must come and see us.** 你必须来看我们。

**Now I must push along,** 我现在得赶路了——

**or father won't trust me with his business any more.** 【结果·不然】不然父亲就再也不放心让我跑腿了。

**Good-bye!"** 再见！"

---

**"Good-bye," he answered,** "再见，"他答道——

**raising his broad sombrero,** [分词-句末伴随] 摘起他那顶宽边毡帽——

**and bending over her little hand.** → 低头吻她的小手。

**She wheeled her mustang round,** 她把野马转了个头——

**gave it a cut with her riding-whip,** → 用马鞭抽了一下——

**and darted away down the broad road** → 飞奔而去，沿着那条宽阔的路——

**in a rolling cloud of dust.** 卷起一团尘雾。

---

**Young Jefferson Hope rode on with his companions,** 年轻的杰弗逊·霍普和同伴们继续骑行——

**gloomy and taciturn.** [形容词-后置修饰] 什么样子？→ 阴郁而沉默。

**He and they had been among the Nevada Mountains** 他和他们一直在内华达山脉里——

**prospecting for silver,** [分词-后置修饰] 干什么？→ 勘探银矿——

**and were returning to Salt Lake City** → 正返回盐湖城——

**in the hope of raising capital enough** [介词-目的] 为了什么？→ 为了筹集足够的资金——

**to work some lodes which they had discovered.** 做什么？→ 开采他们发现的几条矿脉。

**He had been** →
**as keen as any of them upon the business** → 他对这件事曾跟他们任何一个一样热情—

**until this sudden incident** 【转折·直到】直到这个突然的事件——

**had drawn his thoughts into another channel.** → 把他的思绪引入了另一条轨道。

**The sight of the fair young girl,** 看到这个白皙的年轻女孩——

**as frank and wholesome as the Sierra breezes,** 像内华达山风一样坦率、清新的那种——

**had stirred his volcanic, untamed heart** → 搅动了他那颗如火山般炽热、不驯服的心——

**to its very depths.** 搅动到什么程度？→ 搅到了最深处。

**When she had vanished from his sight,** 【情境·当】当她从他视野里消失时——

**he realized that a crisis had come in his life,** 他意识到生命中的一个转折点来了——

**and that neither silver speculations nor any other questions** → 而无论是银矿投机，还是任何其他问题——

**could ever be of such importance to him** → 对他来说都不可能有那么重要——

**as this new and all-absorbing one.** 【对比】跟什么比？→ 跟这个新的、令人全神贯注的问题相比。

**The love which had sprung up in his heart** 在他心里迸发出的爱——

**was not the sudden, changeable fancy of a boy,** 不是少年那种一时冲动、多变的迷恋——

**but rather the wild, fierce passion** 【转折·而是】而是那种狂野、炽烈的激情——

**of a man of strong will and imperious temper.** 什么样的人的激情？→ 一个意志坚强、性格霸道的男人的。

**He had been accustomed to succeed in all** 他习惯于在他着手的一切事上成功。
**that he undertook.** →

**He swore in his heart** 他在心里发誓——

**that he would not fail in this** 发什么誓？→ 这次他不会失败——

**if human effort and human perseverance** 【条件·心悬着】如果人的努力和人的坚持——

**could render him successful.** 【结果·兑现】能让他成功的话。

---

**He called on John Ferrier that night,** 那天晚上他就去拜访了约翰·费瑞尔——

**and many times again,** → 此后又去了许多次——

**until his face was a familiar one at the farm-house.** 【情境·直到】直到他的脸成了农场小屋里熟悉的面孔。

**John, cooped up in the valley,** [分词-句中插入] 约翰被关在谷地里——

**and absorbed in his work,** → 全神贯注于自己的工作——

**had had little chance of learning the news** ← 回来接谓语 → 几乎没有机会了解外面世界的消息—
**of the outside world** → —

**during the last twelve years.** 在过去十二年里。

**All this Jefferson Hope was able to tell him,** 这一切杰弗逊·霍普都能告诉他——

**and in a style** → 而且用一种方式——

**which interested Lucy as well as her father.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的方式？→ 让露西和她父亲都感兴趣的那种。

**He had been a pioneer in California,** 他曾是加利福尼亚的先驱——

**and could narrate many a strange tale** → 能讲述许多奇异故事——

**of fortunes made and fortunes lost** [分词-后置修饰] 什么故事？→ 关于财富的建立与消亡——

**in those wild, halcyon days.** 在哪个年代？→ 在那些狂野、美好的岁月里。

**He had been a scout too, and a trapper,** 他也曾是斥候、陷阱猎人——

**a silver explorer, and a ranchman.** → 银矿探勘者和牧场主。

**Wherever stirring adventures were to be had,** 【情境·条件】无论哪里有惊险刺激——

**Jefferson Hope had been there in search of them.** 杰弗逊·霍普就会去寻找它们。

**He soon became a favourite with the old farmer,** 他很快成了老农场主的心腹人——

**who spoke eloquently of his virtues.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的农场主？→ 滔滔不绝地夸赞他的美德的那位。

**On such occasions, Lucy was silent,** 每逢这样的场合，露西总是沉默的——

**but her blushing cheek and her bright, happy eyes** 【转折】但她那红扑扑的脸颊和明亮、快乐的眼睛——

**showed only too clearly** → 再清楚不过地说明了——

**that her young heart was no longer her own.** 说明什么？→ 她那颗年轻的心已经不再属于自己。

**Her honest father may not have observed these symptoms,** 她诚实的父亲也许没有注意到这些征兆——

**but they were assuredly not thrown away** 【转折】但这些征兆肯定没有白费——

**upon the man** 没有白费在谁那儿？→ 那个人那里——

**who had won her affections.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的人？→ 已经赢得了她芳心的那个。

---

**It was a summer evening** 那是一个夏日傍晚——

**when he came galloping down the road** 【情境】他策马飞奔而来——

**and pulled up at the gate.** → 在大门前勒住了马。

**She was at the doorway,** 她在门口——

**and came down to meet him.** → 走下来迎他。

**He threw the bridle over the fence** 他把缰绳搭在篱笆上——

**and strode up the pathway.** → 大步走上小径。

---

**"I am off, Lucy," he said,** "我要走了，露西，"他说——

**taking her two hands in his,** [分词-句末伴随] 握着她的双手——

**and gazing tenderly down into her face;** → 柔情地低头看着她的脸；

**"I won't ask you to come with me now,** "我现在不会请你随我走——

**but will you be ready to come** → 但等我回来时——

**when I am here again?"** 你愿意做好准备随我走吗？"

---

**"And when will that be?" she asked,** "那是什么时候？"她问——

**blushing and laughing.** [分词-句末伴随] 脸红着、笑着。

---

**"A couple of months at the outside.** "最多两个月。

**I will come and claim you then, my darling.** 那时我会来接你，我的心肝。

**There's no one who can stand between us."** 没有人能站在我们之间。"

---

**"And how about father?" she asked.** "那父亲怎么说？"她问。

---

**"He has given his consent,** "他已经同意了——

**provided we get these mines working all right.** 【条件·心悬着】前提是我们把这些矿开采顺利。

**I have no fear on that head."** 【主张】在这一点上我毫不担心。"

---

**"Oh, well;** "哦，那好——

**of course,** 当然——

**if you and father have arranged it all,** 【条件·心悬着】如果你和父亲都安排好了——

**there's no more to be said," she whispered,** 【结果落地】那也没什么好说的了，"她低声说——

**with her cheek against his broad breast.** [with-描述状态] 脸颊贴着他宽阔的胸膛。

---

**"Thank God!" he said, hoarsely,** "谢天谢地！"他声音沙哑地说——

**stooping and kissing her.** [分词-句末伴随] 俯身吻了她。

**"It is settled, then.** "那就说定了。

**The longer I stay,** 【条件·心悬着】我待得越长——

**the harder it will be to go.** 【结果落地】就越难离开。

**They are waiting for me at the cañon.** 他们在峡谷那里等我。

**Good-bye, my own darling—good-bye.** 再见，我的心肝——再见。

**In two months you shall see me."** 两个月内你就会见到我。"

---

**He tore himself from her as he spoke,** 说着，他从她身边撕裂般地离开——

**and, flinging himself upon his horse,** [分词-句末伴随] → 纵身跃上马——

**galloped furiously away,** → 狂奔而去——

**never even looking round,** → 连头都没回——

**as though afraid** 【比喻·假设】好像担心——

**that his resolution might fail him** 担心什么？→ 他的决心会动摇——

**if he took one glance at what he was leaving.** 【条件·心悬着】如果他回头看一眼他所留下的一切的话。

**She stood at the gate,** 她站在大门口——

**gazing after him** [分词-句末伴随] 目送着他——

**until he vanished from her sight.** 【情境·直到】直到他从她视野中消失。

**Then she walked back into the house,** 然后她走回了屋里——

**the happiest girl in all Utah.** [同位语·省略] 什么样的心情？→ 整个犹他最幸福的女孩。

---


---

### 第三章 约翰·费瑞尔与先知的对话
### CHAPTER III. JOHN FERRIER TALKS WITH THE PROPHET.

---

**Three weeks had passed** 三周过去了——

**since Jefferson Hope** 【情境】什么时候过去的三周？
**and his comrades had departed from Salt Lake City.** → 自从杰弗逊·霍普和他的同伴们离开盐湖城以来。

**John Ferrier's heart was sore within him** 约翰·费瑞尔的心里隐隐作痛——

**when he thought of the young man's return,** 【情境】什么时候痛？→ 每当他想到那年轻人回来之时——

**and of the impending loss of his adopted child.** → 以及即将失去他那养女之时。

**Yet her bright and happy face** 【让步·心悬着】然而，她那明亮快乐的脸——【心里在等"但……"的转折】

**reconciled him to the arrangement** 【主张落地】使他慢慢接受了这个安排——

**more than any argument could have done.** 比任何说辞所能做到的都更有效。

---

**He had always determined,** 他始终坚定地认为——

**deep down in his resolute heart,** [插入修饰-逗号隔开] 在哪里坚定？→ 在他那坚定的内心深处——

**that nothing would ever induce him** ← 回来接 → 世上没有什么能让他——

**to allow his daughter to wed a Mormon.** 允许他女儿嫁给一个摩门教徒。

**Such a marriage he regarded** 这样的婚姻，在他看来——

**as no marriage at all,** → 根本算不上婚姻——

**but as a shame and a disgrace.** 【转折】而是一种羞耻和耻辱。

---

**Whatever he might think of the Mormon doctrines,** 【让步·心悬着】不管他对摩门教义怎么看——【等"在这一点上……"】

**upon that one point he was inflexible.** 【主张落地】在这一点上，他是绝不妥协的。

**He had to seal his mouth on the subject, however,** 【转折】然而，关于这件事他不得不守口如瓶——

**for to express an unorthodox opinion** 【原因】为什么？→ 因为发表异端观点——

**was a dangerous matter in those days** → 在那个年代是一件危险的事——

**in the Land of the Saints.** 在哪里危险？→ 在圣徒之国。

---

**Yes, a dangerous matter** 是的，一件危险的事——

**—so dangerous** 【心悬着：so 开出口袋，等"以至于……"】危险到如此程度——

**that even the most saintly dared only whisper** 【口袋兑现】危险到什么程度？→ 以至于就算是最虔诚的信徒也只敢低声耳语——

**their religious opinions with bated breath,** 低声说什么？→ 他们的宗教见解，说时还屏着呼吸——

**lest something which fell from their lips** 【原因·担忧】生怕什么？→ 生怕从他们嘴里说出去的什么话——

**might be misconstrued,** → 会被误解——

**and bring down a swift retribution upon them.** → 进而给他们招来迅雷不及掩耳的报复。

---

**The victims of persecution had now turned persecutors** 受迫害的人们如今已经自己成了迫害者—
**on their own account,** → —

**and persecutors of the most terrible description.** → 而且是最可怕的那种迫害者。

**Not the Inquisition of Seville,** 塞维利亚的宗教裁判所——

**nor the German Vehmgericht,** → 德意志的私设法庭——

**nor the Secret Societies of Italy,** → 意大利的秘密社团——

**were ever able to put** ← 回来接谓语 → 都从未能够开动——

**a more formidable machinery in motion** 一部更可怕的机器——

**than that which cast a cloud over the** 【对比】比那笼罩在犹他州上空的那部机器更可怕的。
**State of Utah.** →

---

**Its invisibility, and the mystery which was attached to it,** 它的无形，以及那附着其上的神秘感——

**made this organization doubly terrible.** → 让这个组织加倍地可怕。

**It appeared to be omniscient and omnipotent,** 它看起来无所不知、无所不能——

**and yet was neither seen nor heard.** 【让步·心悬着】然而却既看不见也听不到。【主张落地】

---

**The man who held out against the Church** 那些敢于抵抗教会的人——

**vanished away,** → 就消失了——

**and none knew** → 而没有人知道——

**whither he had gone** 知道什么？→ 他去了哪里——

**or what had befallen him.** → 或者遭遇了什么。

**His wife and his children awaited him at home,** 他的妻子和孩子们在家里等着他——

**but no father ever returned** 【转折】但从没有哪个父亲回来过——

**to tell them** 回来干什么？→ 告诉他们——

**how he had fared at the hands of** 他在那些秘密裁判者手下是怎么个遭遇。
**his secret judges.** →

---

**A rash word** 一句冲动的话，
**or a hasty act was followed by annihilation,** → 就是毁灭——

**and yet none knew** 【让步·心悬着】然而没有人知道——【等"到底是什么……"】

**what the nature might be** 知道什么？→ 这究竟是什么性质——

**of this terrible power** → 这股可怕的力量——

**which was suspended over them.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的力量？→ 高悬在他们头顶的那种。

**No wonder that men went about in fear and trembling,** 难怪人们走路都战战兢兢——

**and that even in the heart of the wilderness** → 以至于就算在荒野的腹地——

**they dared not whisper the doubts** → 他们也不敢低声说出那些疑惑——

**which oppressed them.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么疑惑？→ 那些压迫着他们的疑惑。

---

**At first this vague and terrible power** 起初，这股模糊而可怕的力量——

**was exercised only upon the recalcitrants** 只施加在那些顽固分子身上——

**who, having embraced the Mormon faith,** [定从-句中插入] 什么样的顽固分子？→ 那些曾经皈依摩门信仰、[分词-句中插入]

**wished afterwards to pervert or to abandon it.** ← 回来接定从谓语 → 后来却想改宗或脱教的人。

---

**Soon, however, it took a wider range.** 【转折】然而很快，它波及的范围扩大了。

**The supply of adult women was running short,** 成年女性的供应越来越短缺——

**and polygamy without a female population on which to draw** → 而多妻制若没有可以征召的女性人口——

**was a barren doctrine indeed.** → 确实不过是一纸空文。

---

**Strange rumours began to be bandied about** 奇怪的谣言开始四处流传——

**—rumours of murdered immigrants and rifled camps** [同位语] 什么谣言？→ 关于被杀的移民、被洗劫的营地——

**in regions where Indians had never been seen.** [定从-句尾补充] 在哪里发生的？→ 在印第安人从未出没的地区。

**Fresh women appeared in the harems of the Elders** 新来的女人出现在长老们的后宫——

**—women who pined and wept,** [同位语-定从] 什么样的女人？→ 那些日渐消瘦、以泪洗面的女人——

**and bore upon their faces** → 而且脸上带着——

**the traces of an unextinguishable horror.** 带着什么？→ 一种无法消灭的恐惧的痕迹。

---

**Belated wanderers upon the mountains** 在山中误了行程的旅人——

**spoke of gangs of armed men, masked, stealthy, and noiseless,** 讲述起一队队蒙面的、鬼鬼祟祟的、悄无声息的武装男人——

**who flitted by them in the darkness.** [定从-句尾补充] 这些人在干什么？→ 在黑暗中从他们身旁一闪而过。

**These tales and rumours took substance and shape,** 这些传说和谣言逐渐变得有血有肉、有形可据——

**and were corroborated and re-corroborated,** → 一再被印证、反复被佐证——

**until they resolved themselves into a definite name.** 【情境·直到】直到最终凝结成了一个确切的名字。

**To this day, in the lonely ranches of the West,** 时至今日，在西部那些偏僻的牧场里——

**the name of the Danite Band, or the Avenging Angels,** 丹尼特帮，又称"复仇天使"这个名字——

**is a sinister and an ill-omened one.** → 仍是一个令人不寒而栗、充满凶兆的名字。

---

**Fuller knowledge of the organization** 对这个组织了解得越深——

**which produced such terrible results** [定从-句尾补充] 什么组织？→ 制造出如此可怕后果的那个组织——

**served to increase rather than to lessen** ← 回来接谓语 → 反而只会加深，而非减轻——

**the horror which it inspired in the minds of men.** 它在人们心中激起的那种恐惧。

---

**None knew who belonged to this ruthless society.** 没有人知道谁是这个冷酷社团的成员。

**The names of the participators** 参与者的名字——

**in the deeds of blood** 在哪些行动中参与的？
**and violence done under the name of religion** → 那些以宗教名义实施的血腥暴力行动——

**were kept profoundly secret.** → 被严密地保守着秘密。

---

**The very friend** 就是你那个最亲密的朋友——

**to whom you communicated your misgivings** [定从-句中插入] 什么朋友？→ 你向他倾诉过对先知和他使命的疑虑的那个朋友——

**as to the Prophet and his mission,** → 关于先知和他的使命的疑虑——

**might be one of those** ← 回来接谓语 → 可能就是其中的一员——

**who would come forth at night with fire and sword** [定从-句尾补充] 哪些人？→ 那些会在夜里提着火把、拿着刀剑出现——

**to exact a terrible reparation.** 来干什么？→ 来索取可怕的赔偿的人。

**Hence every man feared his neighbour,** 因此每个人都开始害怕自己的邻居——

**and none spoke of the things** → 没有人谈论那些事情——

**which were nearest his heart.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么事情？→ 那些最贴近他内心的事。

---

**One fine morning,** 一个晴朗的早晨，
**John Ferrier was about to set out to his wheatfields,** → 约翰·费瑞尔正准备出发去他的麦田——

**when he heard the click of the latch,** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，他听见门闩咔嗒一声——

**and, looking through the window,** → 朝窗外一看——

**saw a stout, sandy-haired, middle-aged man** → 看见一个粗壮的、沙黄色头发的、中年男人——

**coming up the pathway.** [分词-后置修饰] 这个人在干什么？→ 正沿着小路走来。

---

**His heart leapt to his mouth,** 他的心跳到了嗓子眼——

**for this was none other than the great** 【原因】为什么？→ 因为来者不是别人，
**Brigham Young himself.** → 正是大名鼎鼎的布莱恩·杨本人。

**Full of trepidation** [分词-句首状语] 他是什么状态？→ 满心惊惶——

**—for he knew** 【原因】为什么惊惶？→ 因为他心里清楚——

**that such a visit boded him little good—** 这样的拜访对他不会有什么好兆头——

**Ferrier ran to the door to greet the Mormon chief.** ← 回来接主句 → 费瑞尔跑到门口去迎接这位摩门教领袖。

**The latter, however, received his salutations coldly,** 【转折】然而，那人冷冷地接受了他的问候——

**and followed him with a stern face into the sitting-room.** → 一脸严肃地跟着他走进了客厅。

---

**"Brother Ferrier," he said,** "费瑞尔兄弟，"他说——

**taking a seat,** [分词-句末伴随] → 同时落座——

**and eyeing the farmer keenly** → 并且锐利地打量着这个农夫——

**from under his light-coloured eyelashes,** 从哪里打量？→ 从他那浅色睫毛的下方——

**"the true believers have been good friends to you.** "真正的信徒一直是你的好朋友。

**We picked you up** →
**when you were starving in the desert,** → 我们在你饥寒交迫地倒在沙漠里时救起了你—

**we shared our food with you,** → 我们与你分享了我们的食物——

**led you safe to the Chosen Valley,** → 带你安全抵达了应许之谷——

**gave you a goodly share of land,** → 给了你一大片土地——

**and allowed you to wax rich under our protection.** → 并允许你在我们的庇护下渐渐富裕起来。

**Is not this so?"** 难道不是这样吗？"

---

**"It is so," answered John Ferrier.** "是这样，"约翰·费瑞尔回答道。

---

**"In return for all this we asked but one condition:** "而作为这一切的回报，我们只要求了一个条件：

**that was, that you should embrace the true faith,** 那就是，你要皈依真正的信仰——

**and conform in every way to its usages.** → 并在各方面遵从其习规。

**This you promised to do,** 这一点你曾承诺会做到——

**and this, if common report says truly,** 【条件·心悬着】而这一点，如果坊间的说法是真的——【等"你就……"】

**you have neglected."** 【结果落地】你就没有做到。"

---

**"And how have I neglected it?" asked Ferrier,** "我哪里没有做到？"费瑞尔问道——

**throwing out his hands in expostulation.** [分词-句末伴随] → 同时双手一摊，作出申辩的姿势。

**"Have I not given to the common fund?** "我没有向公共基金捐款吗？

**Have I not attended at the Temple?** 我没有去圣殿礼拜吗？

**Have I not——?"** 我没有——？"

---

**"Where are your wives?" asked Young, looking round him.** "你的妻子们在哪里？"杨问道，环顾四周。

**"Call them in, that I may greet them."** "叫她们进来，让我向她们问候。"

---

**"It is true that I have not married," Ferrier answered.** "我确实没有成婚，"费瑞尔回答。

**"But women were few,** "但女人少——

**and there were many who had better claims than I.** → 而且有很多人比我更有资格。

**I was not a lonely man:** 我并不孤单：

**I had my daughter to attend to my wants."** 我有女儿照料我的日常。"

---

**"It is of** "正是关于那个女儿我想和你谈，
**that daughter that I would speak to you,"** → "摩门教领袖说道。
**said the leader of the Mormons.** →

**"She has grown to be the flower of Utah,** "她已经出落成了犹他的花朵——

**and has found favour in the eyes of many** → 并且在许多人眼中已经大受青睐——

**who are high in the land."** [定从-句尾补充] 哪些人？→ 那些在这片土地上位高权重的人。

---

**John Ferrier groaned internally.** 约翰·费瑞尔在心里暗自叹了口气。

---

**"There are stories of her** "关于她有一些传言——

**which I would fain disbelieve** [定从-句中插入] 什么传言？→ 我倒是很想不相信的那种传言——

**—stories that she is sealed to some Gentile.** [同位语] 具体是什么传言？→ 说她已经私许了某个异教徒。

**This must be the gossip of idle tongues.** 这一定是闲人嚼舌根。

**What is the thirteenth rule in the code** 圣洁的约瑟·史密斯法典第十三条说的是什么？
**of the sainted Joseph Smith?** →

**'Let every maiden of the true faith marry** '让每一位真正信仰的少女嫁给一位选民；
**one of the elect;** →

**for if she wed a Gentile,** 【条件·心悬着】因为如果她嫁给一个异教徒——【等"就……"】

**she commits a grievous sin.'** 【结果落地】她就犯了重罪。'

**This being so,** [分词-句首状语·独立主格] 既然如此——

**it is impossible** → 就不可能——

**that you, who profess the holy creed,** [定从-句中插入] 谁不可能？→ 你，作为一个自称信仰圣洁教义的人——

**should suffer your daughter to violate it."** ← 回来接 → 会允许你的女儿去违背它。"

---

**John Ferrier made no answer,** 约翰·费瑞尔没有回答——

**but he played nervously with his riding-whip.** 【转折】只是紧张地摆弄着他的马鞭。

---

**"Upon this one point your whole faith shall be tested** "就在这一点上，你整个人的信仰将会受到考验——

**—so it has been decided in the Sacred** [插入说明] 谁决定的？
**Council of Four.** → 这是神圣四人委员会的决定。

**The girl is young,** 女孩还年轻——

**and we would not have her wed grey hairs,** → 我们不想让她嫁给白发苍苍的老人——

**neither would we deprive her of all choice.** → 也不想剥夺她所有的选择权。

---

**We Elders have many heifers,** 我们长老们有许多母牛——

**but our children must also be provided.** 【转折】但我们的子女也必须有所安排。

**Stangerson has a son, and Drebber has a son,** 斯坦格森有个儿子，德雷伯也有个儿子——

**and either of them would gladly welcome your** → 他们俩都会很乐意迎娶你的女儿。
**daughter to their house.** →

**Let her choose between them.** 让她在二者之间做出选择。

**They are young and rich, and of the true faith.** 他们年轻富有，而且信仰正统。

**What say you to that?"** 你对此有何看法？"

---

**Ferrier remained silent** 费瑞尔皱着眉头沉默了片刻。
**for some little time with his brows knitted.** →

---

**"You will give us time," he said at last.** "你们会给我们时间的，"他终于开口说道。

**"My daughter is very young** "我的女儿还很年轻——

**—she is scarce of an age to marry."** → 她还不到可以成婚的年纪。"

---

**"She shall have a month to choose," said** "她有一个月的时间来做决定，
**Young, rising from his seat.** → "杨说着从座位上起身。

**"At the end of** "到时候她要给出她的答复。
**that time she shall give her answer."** → "

---

**He was passing through the door,** 他正要走出门——

**when he turned, with flushed face and flashing eyes.** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时他转过身来，满脸通红，双目炯炯。

**"It were better for you, John Ferrier," he thundered,** "约翰·费瑞尔，对你来说，"他怒喝道——

**"that you and she were now lying blanched** "你和她现在躺在塞拉布兰科山上做两具白骨—
**skeletons upon the Sierra Blanco,** → —

**than that you should put your weak wills** 【对比·让步】也好过——【等"比……更好"的对比结构落地】你们用你们那软弱的意志去抗衡——

**against the orders of the Holy Four!"** 对抗什么？→ 神圣四人委员会的命令！"

---

**With a threatening gesture of his hand,** [状语前置] 以怎样的姿态离开？→ 做出一个威胁性的手势——

**he turned from the door,** → 他从门口转身离去——

**and Ferrier heard his heavy step** → 费瑞尔听见他沉重的脚步声——

**scrunching along the shingly path.** [分词-后置修饰] 脚步声怎样？→ 踩着碎石小路嘎吱作响，渐渐远去。

---

**He was still sitting with his elbows upon his knees,** 他还坐在那里，双肘搭在膝上——

**considering how he should broach the matter to his daughter** [分词-句末伴随] 在想什么？→ 思索着该如何向女儿开口谈这件事——

**when a soft hand was laid upon his,** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，一只柔软的手搭上了他的手——

**and looking up,** → 他抬起头来——

**he saw her standing beside him.** → 看见她就站在他身旁。

**One glance at her pale, frightened face** 只消看一眼她那苍白、惊恐的脸——

**showed him that she had heard what had passed.** → 他便知道她已经听到了刚才发生的一切。

---

**"I could not help it," she said,** "我没办法，
**in answer to his look.** → "她回应着他的目光说道。

**"His voice rang through the house.** "他的声音响彻了整个屋子。

**Oh, father, father, what shall we do?"** 哦，父亲，父亲，我们该怎么办？"

---

**"Don't you scare yourself," he answered,** "别害怕，"他回答道——

**drawing her to him,** [分词-句末伴随] → 将她拉到身边——

**and passing his broad,** → 用他那宽大粗糙的手轻轻爱抚着她栗色的头发。
**rough hand caressingly over her chestnut hair.** →

**"We'll fix it up somehow or another.** "我们总会想出办法的。

**You don't find your fancy kind o' lessening** 你对这小伙子的心意没有减少吧，
**for this chap, do you?"** → 是不是？"

---

**A sob and a squeeze of his hand** 一声哽咽和一下紧握他手，
**was her only answer.** → 是她唯一的回答。

---

**"No; of course not.** "不，当然没有。

**I shouldn't care to hear you say you did.** 我也不希望听到你说你减少了。

**He's a likely lad,** 他是个有出息的小伙子——

**and he's a Christian,** → 而且他是个基督徒——

**which is more than these folk here,** [定从-句尾补充] 基督徒意味着什么？→ 这一点比这里这些人强多了——

**in spite o' all their praying and preaching.** 【让步】尽管他们整天祈祷、说教。

**There's a party starting for Nevada to-morrow,** 明天有一队人出发去内华达——

**and I'll manage to send him a message** → 我会想办法给他捎个信——

**letting him know the hole we are in.** [分词-后置修饰] 捎什么消息？→ 让他知道我们现在的困境。

**If I know anything o' that young man,** 【条件·心悬着】凭我对那年轻人的了解——【等"他就会……"】

**he'll be back here with a speed** 【结果落地】他回来的速度——

**that would whip electro-telegraphs."** 会比电报还快。"

---

**Lucy laughed through her tears at her father's description.** 露西听着父亲的描述，含着泪笑了。

---

**"When he comes, he will advise us for the best.** "他来了，他会给我们最好的建议。

**But it is for you that I am frightened, dear.** 【转折】但我担心的是你，亲爱的。

**One hears—one hears such dreadful stories** 人们听说——人们听说了如此可怕的故事——

**about those who oppose the Prophet:** 关于那些反抗先知的人：

**something terrible always happens to them."** 可怕的事情总会降临到他们身上。"

---

**"But we haven't opposed him yet," her father answered.** "但我们还没有反抗他，"她父亲回答道。

**"It will be time to look out** "等到真的反抗了，
**for squalls when we do.** → 再担心暴风雨也不迟。

**We have a clear month before us;** 我们还有整整一个月；

**at the end of that,** 到那时候，
**I guess we had best shin out of Utah."** → 我估摸着我们最好溜出犹他。"

---

**"Leave Utah!"** "离开犹他！"

---

**"That's about the size of it."** "差不多就是这个意思。"

---

**"But the farm?"** "但是农场呢？"

---

**"We will raise as much as we can in money,** "能换多少钱就换多少钱——

**and let the rest go.** → 其余的就算了。

**To tell the truth, Lucy,** 说实话，露西——

**it isn't the first time I have thought** 这不是我第一次动这个念头了。
**of doing it.** →

**I don't care about knuckling under to any man,** 我不喜欢向任何人低头——

**as these folk do to their darned prophet.** 就像这里的人对那个该死的先知俯首帖耳那样。

**I'm a free-born American,** 我是个生来自由的美国人——

**and it's all new to me.** → 这一套对我来说完全是新鲜玩意。

**Guess I'm too old to learn.** 我估计我太老了，学不来了。

**If he comes browsing about this farm,** 【条件·心悬着】如果他跑来这个农场转悠——【等"他就会……"】

**he might chance to run up against a** 【结果落地】他说不定会撞上一颗霰弹—
**charge of buckshot** → —

**travelling in the opposite direction."** [分词-后置修饰] 什么方向的？→ 从相反方向射来的。"

---

**"But they won't let us leave," his daughter objected.** "但他们不会让我们走的，"他的女儿反驳道。

---

**"Wait till Jefferson comes,** "等杰弗逊来了——

**and we'll soon manage that.** → 我们很快就会解决这个问题。

**In the meantime, don't you fret yourself, my dearie,** 眼下，别发愁了，我的宝贝——

**and don't get your eyes swelled up,** → 也别哭肿了眼睛——

**else he'll be walking into me when he sees you.** 【结果】不然他看见你那副样子会来找我算账的。

**There's nothing to be afeared about,** 没什么好害怕的——

**and there's no danger at all."** → 一点危险都没有。"

---

**John Ferrier uttered these consoling remarks in a** 约翰·费瑞尔用十分自信的语气说出了这些宽慰的话—
**very confident tone,** → —

**but she could not help observing** 【转折】但她忍不住注意到——

**that he paid unusual care to the fastening** 当晚他异常仔细地检查了门的锁闭—
**of the doors that night,** → —

**and that he carefully cleaned and loaded** → 以及他仔细地清理并装好了弹药——

**the rusty old shotgun** 什么枪？→ 那把锈迹斑斑的旧猎枪——

**which hung upon the wall of his bedroom.** [定从-句尾补充] 挂在哪里的？→ 挂在他卧室墙上的那把。

---



---

### 第四章 生死大逃亡
### CHAPTER IV. A FLIGHT FOR LIFE.

---

**On the morning** →
**which followed his interview with the Mormon Prophet,** → 在与摩门先知会面的第二天早上—

**John Ferrier went in to Salt Lake City,** 约翰·费瑞尔进了盐湖城——

**and having found his acquaintance,** [分词-句末伴随] → 找到了他的熟人——

**who was bound for the Nevada Mountains,** [定从-句中插入] 什么样的熟人？→ 那个即将前往内华达山脉的熟人——

**he entrusted him with his message to Jefferson Hope.** ← 回来接 → 将捎给杰弗逊·霍普的口信托付给了他。

**In it he told the young man of** 信里，
**the imminent danger** → 他告诉那年轻人迫在眉睫的危险——

**which threatened them,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么危险？→ 威胁着他们的那种危险——

**and how necessary it was that he should return.** → 以及他回来是多么必要。

**Having done thus he felt easier in his mind,** [分词-句首状语] 做完这些之后，他心里轻松了些——

**and returned home with a lighter heart.** → 带着一颗轻松些的心回了家。

---

**As he approached his farm,** 当他走近农场时——

**he was surprised to see a horse hitched** 他惊讶地发现，
**to each of the posts of the gate.** → 大门的每根柱子上都拴着一匹马。

**Still more surprised was he on entering** 【倒装强调】走进去之后，他更加吃惊——

**to find two young men in possession of his sitting-room.** 吃惊地发现什么？→ 发现两个年轻男人占据了他的客厅。

**One, with a long pale face,** 一个，长着一张细长苍白的脸——

**was leaning back in the rocking-chair,** → 斜靠在摇椅里——

**with his feet cocked up upon the stove.** [with-描述状态] 脚放在哪里？→ 双脚翘在炉子上。

**The other, a bull-necked youth with coarse bloated features,** 另一个，是个粗脖子的年轻人，五官粗糙浮肿——

**was standing in front of the window with** → 双手揣在口袋里，
**his hands in his pocket,** → 站在窗户前——

**whistling a popular hymn.** [分词-句末伴随] 同时在干什么？→ 吹着口哨，是一首流行圣歌。

**Both of them nodded to Ferrier as he entered,** 费瑞尔进来时，两人都朝他点了点头——

**and the one in the rocking-chair commenced the conversation.** → 坐在摇椅里的那个开始说话了。

---

**"Maybe you don't know us," he said.** "也许你不认识我们，"他说。

**"This here is the son of Elder Drebber,** "这位是德雷伯长老的儿子——

**and I'm Joseph Stangerson,** → 而我是约瑟夫·斯坦格森——

**who travelled with you in the desert** [定从-句尾补充] 我是谁？→ 当年在沙漠里与你同行的那个人——

**when the Lord stretched out His hand** 什么时候同行的？→ 当上帝伸出他的手——

**and gathered you into the true fold."** → 将你领入真正的羊群的时候。"

---

**"As He will all the nations in His** "正如他终将以自己的方式收聚所有民族，
**own good time," said the other in a nasal voice;** → "另一个用鼻音说道——

**"He grindeth slowly but exceeding small."** "他的磨盘虽转得慢，却磨得极细。"

---

**John Ferrier bowed coldly.** 约翰·费瑞尔冷冷地点了点头。

**He had guessed who his visitors were.** 他已经猜到来访者是谁了。

---

**"We have come," continued Stangerson,** "我们来这里，"斯坦格森继续说道——

**"at the advice of our fathers** "是在我们父亲的建议下——

**to solicit the hand of your daughter** 来求娶你的女儿——

**for whichever of us may seem good to** 无论我们两个中哪一个，
**you and to her.** → 对你和她来说都合适的那位。

**As I have but four wives** 因为我只有四个妻子——

**and Brother Drebber here has seven,** 而德雷伯兄弟这里有七个——

**it appears to me** 在我看来，
**that my claim is the stronger one."** → 我的主张更有分量。"

---

**"Nay, nay, Brother Stangerson," cried the other;** "不，不，斯坦格森兄弟，"另一个喊道——

**"the question is not how many wives we have,** "问题不在于我们有多少妻子——

**but how many we can keep.** 【转折】而在于我们能养活多少。

**My father has now given over his mills to me,** 我父亲已经把他的磨坊交给我了——

**and I am the richer man."** → 所以我是更富有的那个人。"

---

**"But my prospects are better," said the other, warmly.** "但我的前景更好，"另一个热切地说。

**"When the Lord removes my father,** 【情境】什么时候会更好？→ 等到上帝召走我父亲的时候——

**I shall have his tanning yard and his leather factory.** 我就会得到他的鞣革场和皮革厂。

**Then I am your elder,** 而且我比你年长——

**and am higher in the Church."** → 在教会里地位也更高。"

---

**"It will be** "让姑娘自己来决定，
**for the maiden to decide," rejoined young Drebber,** → "小德雷伯接话道——

**smirking at his own reflection in the glass.** [分词-句末伴随] 同时在干什么？→ 对着镜子里自己的倒影得意地微笑。

**"We will leave it all to her decision."** "我们一切都听她的。"

---

**During this dialogue,** 在这段对话期间，
**John Ferrier had stood fuming in the doorway,** → 约翰·费瑞尔一直气呼呼地站在门口——

**hardly able to keep his riding-whip from the** 几乎控制不住自己，
**backs of his two visitors.** → 不想用马鞭抽那两个访客的背。

---

**"Look here," he said at last, striding up to them,** "听着，"他终于说道，大步走向他们——

**"when my daughter summons you, you can come,** "等我女儿传唤你们的时候，你们再来——

**but until then I don't want to see** 但在那之前，
**your faces again."** → 我不想再见到你们的脸。"

---

**The two young Mormons stared at him in amazement.** 两个年轻的摩门教徒惊愕地盯着他。

**In their eyes this competition between them** 在他们眼里，他们之间的这场竞争——

**for the maiden's hand** 为了什么而竞争？→ 为了这位姑娘的芳心——

**was the highest of honours both to her** → 对她和她父亲来说都是莫大的荣耀。
**and her father.** →

---

**"There are two ways out of the room," cried Ferrier;** "这间屋子有两个出口，"费瑞尔喊道——

**"there is the door, and there is the window.** "一个是门，一个是窗。

**Which do you care to use?"** 你们想用哪个？"

---

**His brown face looked so savage,** 他那张棕色的脸看起来是如此狰狞——

**and his gaunt hands so threatening,** → 他那双消瘦的手如此充满威胁——

**that his visitors sprang to their feet** 【结果】以至于那两位访客腾地站了起来，
**and beat a hurried retreat.** → 慌忙撤退。

**The old farmer followed them to the door.** 老农夫跟着他们追到门口。

---

**"Let me know** "等你们商量好了是哪个，
**when you have settled** → 来告诉我，
**which it is to be," he said, sardonically.** → "他讽刺地说道。

---

**"You shall smart for this!" Stangerson cried, white with rage.** "你会为此付出代价的！"斯坦格森气得脸色发白，大喊道。

**"You have defied the Prophet and the Council of Four.** "你已经公然违抗了先知和四人委员会。

**You shall rue it to the end of your days."** 你将后悔终生。"

---

**"The hand of the Lord shall be heavy** "上帝之手将重重地落在你身上，
**upon you," cried young Drebber;** → "小德雷伯大喊——

**"He will arise and smite you!"** "他将兴起击打你！"

---

**"Then I'll start the smiting," exclaimed Ferrier furiously,** "那我先动手，"费瑞尔怒吼道——

**and would have rushed upstairs for his gun** → 眼看就要冲上楼去拿枪——

**had not Lucy seized him by the arm** 【假设·倒装·条件】要不是露西抓住了他的手臂拦住了他。
**and restrained him.** →

**Before he could escape from her,** 在他能从她手中挣脱之前——

**the clatter of horses' hoofs told him** → 马蹄声告诉了他——

**that they were beyond his reach.** 那两人已经跑远了。

---

**"The young canting rascals!" he exclaimed,** "这两个满口虔诚的小流氓！
**wiping the perspiration from his forehead;** → "他擦着额头的汗大声说道——

**"I would sooner see you in your grave, my girl,** "我宁可看你躺在坟墓里，我的孩子——

**than the wife of either of them."** 也不愿你成为他们任何一个人的妻子。"

---

**"And so should I, father," she answered, with spirit;** "我也是这么想，父亲，"她气宇轩昂地回答——

**"but Jefferson will soon be here."** "但杰弗逊很快就会来的。"

---

**"Yes. It will not be long before he comes.** "是的，他不会等太久就来了。

**The sooner the better,** 越快越好——

**for we do not know what their next** 【原因】因为我们不知道他们下一步会做什么。
**move may be."** → "

---

**It was, indeed,** 确实，
**high time that someone capable of giving advice and help** → 是时候有一个能给予建议和帮助的人——

**should come to the aid of the sturdy** 来援助这位坚强的老农夫和他的养女了。
**old farmer and his adopted daughter.** →

**In the whole history of the settlement** 在整个定居地的历史上——

**there had never been such a case of rank disobedience** ← 回来接 → 从未有过如此公然抗命的先例——

**to the authority of the Elders.** 对什么的抗命？→ 对长老们权威的抗命。

---

**If minor errors were punished so sternly,** 【条件·心悬着】如果连小错都被如此严厉惩罚——【等"那么……"】

**what would be the fate of this arch rebel.** 【结果落地】那这个头号叛逆者的命运将会如何。

**Ferrier knew that his wealth** 费瑞尔明白，
**and position would be of no avail to him.** → 他的财富和地位对他毫无用处。

**Others as well known and as rich as himself** 其他像他一样有名望、有财富的人——

**had been spirited away before now,** → 此前已经神秘失踪了——

**and their goods given over to the Church.** → 他们的财产也被移交给了教会。

---

**He was a brave man,** 他是个勇敢的人——

**but he trembled at the vague, shadowy terrors** 【让步·心悬着】然而他也会在那些模糊、幽灵般的恐惧面前颤抖——【等"但……"】

**which hung over him.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么恐惧？→ 悬在他头顶上的那种恐惧。

**Any known danger he could face with a firm lip,** 任何他知道的危险，他都能面不改色地面对——

**but this suspense was unnerving.** 【转折·主张落地】但这种悬而未决的等待令他心神俱裂。

---

**He concealed his fears from his daughter, however,** 【让步·转折】然而，他向女儿隐瞒了自己的恐惧——

**and affected to make light of the whole matter,** → 并假装对整件事轻描淡写——

**though she, with the keen eye of love,** 【让步·心悬着】尽管她，以爱情那敏锐的眼光——

**saw plainly that he was ill at ease.** 【主张落地】清清楚楚地看出他内心不安。

---

**He expected that he would receive some message** 他预料他会收到杨发来的某种信息或警告—
**or remonstrance from Young** → —

**as to his conduct,** 关于他的行为——

**and he was not mistaken,** → 他的预料没有错——

**though it came in an unlooked-for manner.** 【让步】尽管它来临的方式出乎意料。

---

**Upon rising next morning he found, to his surprise,** 第二天早上起床时，他惊讶地发现——

**a small square of paper pinned on to** 一张小方形纸片别在他床铺的被单上—
**the coverlet of his bed** → —

**just over his chest.** 就在他胸口的正上方。

**On it was printed, in bold straggling letters:—** 上面用粗大潦草的字迹印着：——

**"Twenty-nine days are given you for amendment, and then——"** "给你二十九天改过，然后——"

---

**The dash was more fear-inspiring than any threat** 那个破折号比任何威胁都更令人毛骨悚然。
**could have been.** →

**How this warning came into his room puzzled** 这张警告是怎么进来的，
**John Ferrier sorely,** → 令约翰·费瑞尔深感困惑——

**for his servants slept in an outhouse,** 【原因】因为他的仆人睡在外屋——

**and the doors and windows had all been secured.** → 而且所有的门窗都锁好了。

**He crumpled the paper up** 他将纸揉皱，
**and said nothing to his daughter,** → 没有告诉女儿——

**but the incident struck a chill into his heart.** 【转折】但这件事让他心中一阵寒意。

---

**The twenty-nine days were evidently the balance of the month** 二十九天显然是那个月的剩余天数——

**which Young had promised.** [定从-句尾补充] 谁承诺的月份？→ 杨所承诺的那个月。

**What strength or courage could avail** 什么样的力量或勇气能有用——

**against an enemy armed with such mysterious powers?** 对抗一个拥有如此神秘力量的敌人时？

**The hand which fastened that pin** 那只别上大头针的手——

**might have struck him to the heart,** → 本可以插入他的心脏——

**and he could never have known who had slain him.** → 而他永远不会知道是谁杀了他。

---

**Still more shaken was he next morning.** 【倒装强调】第二天早上，他更加震惊了。

**They had sat down to their breakfast** 他们刚坐下来吃早餐——

**when Lucy with a cry of surprise pointed upwards.** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时露西惊叫一声，朝上面指去。

**In the centre of the ceiling was scrawled,** 在天花板的正中央潦草地写着——

**with a burned stick apparently,** [插入修饰] 用什么写的？→ 显然是用一根烧焦的棍子——

**the number 28.** → 数字28。

**To his daughter it was unintelligible,** 对他女儿来说这毫无意义——

**and he did not enlighten her.** → 他也没有向她解释。

---

**That night he sat up with his gun** 那天晚上他拿着枪坐着，
**and kept watch and ward.** → 彻夜守望。

**He saw and he heard nothing,** 他什么也没看见，什么也没听到——

**and yet in the morning** 【让步·转折】然而到了早上——

**a great 27 had been painted upon the** 一个大大的27已经被涂在了他的门外。
**outside of his door.** →

---

**Thus day followed day;** 就这样，一天接着一天——

**and as sure as morning came** 每当早晨来临——

**he found that his unseen enemies had kept their register,** 他都发现那些看不见的敌人记好了他们的账——

**and had marked up in some conspicuous position** → 并在某个显眼的地方标记了出来——

**how many days were still left to him** 标记了什么？→ 他还剩多少天——

**out of the month of grace.** 在那个宽限月里还剩多少天。

---

**Sometimes the fatal numbers appeared upon the walls,** 有时那些致命的数字出现在墙上——

**sometimes upon the floors,** → 有时在地板上——

**occasionally they were on small placards** → 偶尔则出现在小告示牌上——

**stuck upon the garden gate or the railings.** [分词-后置修饰] 贴在哪里？→ 贴在花园大门或栏杆上。

**With all his vigilance John Ferrier could not discover** 尽管费瑞尔保持了一切警觉，他仍无法发现——

**whence these daily warnings proceeded.** 这些每日警告从何而来。

---

**A horror which was almost superstitious came upon** 看见这些，
**him at the sight of them.** → 一种近乎迷信的恐惧笼罩了他。

**He became haggard and restless,** 他变得憔悴、坐立不安——

**and his eyes had the troubled look** → 他的眼神带着那种惶恐的神情——

**of some hunted creature.** 什么样的神情？→ 某种被追猎的动物那样的神情。

**He had but one hope in life now,** 他眼下只剩一个生的希望——

**and that was** [同位语] 什么希望？
**for the arrival of the young hunter from Nevada.** → 盼着那个内华达来的年轻猎人早日到来。

---

**Twenty had changed to fifteen and fifteen to ten,** 二十变成了十五，十五又变成了十——

**but there was no news of the absentee.** 【转折】但那个缺席之人依然音讯全无。

**One by one the numbers dwindled down,** 数字一个一个地减少——

**and still there came no sign of him.** → 却仍旧没有他的任何消息。

**Whenever a horseman clattered down the road,** 每当有骑马的人踏响路上的石子声——

**or a driver shouted at his team,** → 或者赶车人对牲口吆喝着——

**the old farmer hurried to the gate** 老农夫就赶紧走到大门口——

**thinking that help had arrived at last.** [分词-句末伴随] 心里想着什么？→ 以为救援终于来了。

---

**At last, when he saw five give way to four** 终于，当他看见五变成了四——

**and that again to three,** → 四又变成了三——

**he lost heart, and abandoned all hope of escape.** 他心灰意冷，放弃了所有逃跑的希望。

**Single-handed, and with his limited knowledge of the mountains** 孤身一人，加上他对周围山脉有限的了解——

**which surrounded the settlement,** [定从-句尾补充] 哪些山脉？→ 环绕着定居地的山脉——

**he knew that he was powerless.** → 他知道自己无能为力。

---

**The more-frequented roads were strictly watched and guarded,** 人流较多的道路被严密监视和把守——

**and none could pass along them without an** → 没有委员会的命令，
**order from the Council.** → 任何人都无法通过。

**Turn which way he would,** 无论他往哪个方向转——

**there appeared to be no avoiding the blow** → 似乎都无法躲开那一击——

**which hung over him.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么一击？→ 悬在他头顶的那一击。

**Yet the old man never wavered in his resolution** 【让步·转折】然而老人的决心从未动摇——

**to part with life itself** 什么决心？→ 宁可舍弃生命本身——

**before he consented to what he regarded** 也绝不同意他所认为的会使女儿蒙羞之事。
**as his daughter's dishonour.** →

---

**He was sitting alone one evening pondering deeply** 一天傍晚，他独自坐着，
**over his troubles,** → 深深地思索着自己的困境——

**and searching vainly for some way out of them.** [分词-句末伴随] → 徒劳地寻找着出路。

**That morning had shown the figure 2 upon** 那天早晨，
**the wall of his house,** → 他屋子的墙上出现了数字2——

**and the next day would be the last** → 而第二天就将是那宽限时间的最后一天。
**of the allotted time.** →

**What was to happen then?** 那之后又会发生什么？

**All manner of vague and terrible fancies filled his imagination.** 各种模糊而可怕的幻想充斥着他的脑海。

**And his daughter—what was to become of her** 还有他的女儿——他走后，
**after he was gone?** → 她将会怎样？

**Was there no escape from the invisible network** 难道真的无法逃脱那张无形的网——

**which was drawn all round them.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的网？→ 四面八方将他们团团围住的那张网。

**He sank his head upon the table** 他把头埋进桌上，
**and sobbed at the thought of his own impotence.** → 为自己的无能为力而抽泣。

---

**What was that?** 那是什么？

**In the silence he heard a gentle scratching sound** 在寂静中，他听见了一种轻柔的抓挠声——

**—low, but very distinct in the quiet of the night.** [插入说明] 什么样的声音？→ 低沉，但在夜晚的寂静中非常清晰。

**It came from the door of the house.** 声音从屋子的门那里传来。

**Ferrier crept into the hall and listened intently.** 费瑞尔蹑手蹑脚走进门厅，全神贯注地倾听。

**There was a pause for a few moments,** 停顿了片刻——

**and then the low insidious sound was repeated.** → 然后那阴险的低沉声音再次响起。

**Someone was evidently tapping very gently upon one** 显然，
**of the panels of the door.** → 有人正非常轻柔地叩击着门板之一。

---

**Was it some midnight assassin** 是某个午夜刺客——

**who had come to carry out the murderous** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的刺客？
**orders of the secret tribunal?** → 奉那秘密裁判所杀人命令而来的刺客？

**Or was it some agent** 还是某个特工——

**who was marking up** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的特工？
**that the last day of grace had arrived.** → 来标记宽限时间最后一天已经到来的特工？

**John Ferrier felt that instant death would be better** 约翰·费瑞尔感到，即刻的死亡都好过——

**than the suspense** 这种令他神经颤抖、
**which shook his nerves** → 心寒彻骨的煎熬。
**and chilled his heart.** →

**Springing forward he drew the bolt** [分词-句首状语] 随即，他冲上前去，
**and threw the door open.** → 拉开门闩，将门猛地打开。

---

**Outside all was calm and quiet.** 外面，一切平静安宁。

**The night was fine,** 夜色晴好，
**and the stars were twinkling brightly overhead.** → 星星在头顶闪闪发光。

**The little front garden lay before the farmer's eyes** 那片小小的前院展现在农夫眼前——

**bounded by the fence and gate,** [分词-后置修饰] 被什么围着？→ 被篱笆和大门围着——

**but neither there** 【转折】但无论院子里还是路上，
**nor on the road was any human being** → 都看不到任何人影。
**to be seen.** →

**With a sigh of relief,** 费瑞尔松了口气，
**Ferrier looked to right and to left,** → 向左右两边张望——

**until happening to glance straight down at his own feet** 【情境·直到】直到偶然朝自己脚下一看——

**he saw to his astonishment a man lying** 他惊愕地看见一个男人俯卧在地上—
**flat upon his face upon the ground,** → —

**with arms and legs all asprawl.** [with-描述状态] 四肢怎样？→ 手脚四散伸展着。

---

**So unnerved was he at the sight** 【倒装强调·心悬着】看到这一幕，他是如此地心神俱裂——【so...that 的口袋张开】

**that he leaned up against the wall with** 【口袋兑现】心神俱裂到什么程度？
**his hand to his throat** → 以至于他靠着墙，手捂住喉咙——

**to stifle his inclination to call out.** 来干什么？→ 压制住自己想要叫喊的冲动。

**His first thought was that the prostrate figure** 他第一个念头是，那个趴着的人——

**was that of some wounded or dying man,** → 是某个受伤或垂死的人——

**but as he watched it** 【转折】但当他看着那人——

**he saw it writhe along the ground** 他看见那人扭动着身体沿地面爬进了门厅—
**and into the hall** → —

**with the rapidity and noiselessness of a serpent.** 快得像蛇，静得像蛇。

**Once within the house the man sprang to his feet,** 一旦进了屋，那人腾地站起身来——

**closed the door,** → 关上门——

**and revealed to the astonished farmer** → 并向那惊愕的农夫揭示了——

**the fierce face and resolute expression of Jefferson Hope.** 杰弗逊·霍普那张刚烈、坚毅的面孔。

---

**"Good God!" gasped John Ferrier.** "天哪！"约翰·费瑞尔倒吸一口冷气。

**"How you scared me!** "你把我吓坏了！

**Whatever made you come in like that."** 你为什么要那样进来。"

---

**"Give me food," the other said, hoarsely.** "给我吃的，"另一个沙哑地说。

**"I have had no time** →
**for bite or sup for eight-and-forty hours."** → "我四十八个小时没有时间吃任何东西了。

**He flung himself upon the cold meat and bread** 他扑向那些冷肉和面包——

**which were still lying upon the table from** [定从-句中插入] 什么冷肉和面包？→ 还留在桌上的、
**his host's supper,** → 是主人晚餐剩下的那些——

**and devoured it voraciously.** → 狼吞虎咽地吃了起来。

**"Does Lucy bear up well?" he asked,** "露西还好吗？"他问道——

**when he had satisfied his hunger.** 【情境】什么时候问的？→ 当他填饱肚子之后。

---

**"Yes. She does not know the danger," her father answered.** "好的，她不知道危险，"她父亲回答。

---

**"That is well.** "那很好。

**The house is watched on every side.** 房子四面都有人盯着。

**That is why I crawled my way up to it.** 这就是为什么我爬着过来。

**They may be darned sharp,** 他们可能确实很警觉——

**but they're not quite sharp enough to catch** 【让步·转折】但他们还没精明到能抓住一个瓦肖猎人的程度。
**a Washoe hunter."** → "

---

**John Ferrier felt a different man now** 约翰·费瑞尔感到自己判若两人——

**that he realized that he had a devoted ally.** 当他意识到自己有了一个忠诚的盟友。

**He seized the young man's leathery hand** 他抓住那年轻人皮革般的手，
**and wrung it cordially.** → 热切地握了握。

**"You're a man to be proud of," he said.** "你是个值得骄傲的人，"他说。

**"There are not many who would come** "没有多少人愿意来——

**to share our danger and our troubles."** 与我们同担危难的。"

---

**"You've hit it there, pard," the young hunter answered.** "你说对了，老伙计，"年轻猎人回答。

**"I have a respect for you,** "我敬重你——

**but if you were alone in this business** 【条件·心悬着】但如果这件事只关乎你自己——【等"我就……"】

**I'd think twice** →
**before I put my head into such a hornet's nest.** → 【结果落地】我可要三思才会把脑袋伸进这个马蜂窝。

**It's Lucy that brings me here,** 是露西让我来的——

**and before harm comes on her** 在任何伤害降临到她身上之前——

**I guess there will be one less o'** 我估计犹他的霍普家族会少一个人。
**the Hope family in Utah."** → "

---

**"What are we to do?"** "我们该怎么办？"

---

**"To-morrow is your last day,** "明天是你的最后一天——

**and unless you act to-night you are lost.** 【条件·心悬着】除非你今晚采取行动，否则你就完了。

**I have a mule** →
**and two horses waiting in the Eagle Ravine.** → 我在鹰谷有一头骡子和两匹马在等着。

**How much money have you?"** 你有多少钱？"

---

**"Two thousand dollars in gold, and five in notes."** "两千块黄金，另有五千张钞票。"

---

**"That will do.** "够了。

**I have as much more to add to it.** 我还有同样多的可以加上去。

**We must push for Carson City through the mountains.** 我们必须穿越山脉赶往卡森城。

**You had best wake Lucy.** 你最好去叫醒露西。

**It is as well** 好在仆人们不睡在屋里。
**that the servants do not sleep in the house."** → "

---

**While Ferrier was absent,** 趁费瑞尔不在，
**preparing his daughter** → 忙着让女儿为即将到来的旅程做准备时—
**for the approaching journey,** → —

**Jefferson Hope packed all the eatables** 杰弗逊·霍普把他能找到的所有食物都打包成一个小包裹—
**that he could find into a small parcel,** → —

**and filled a stoneware jar with water,** → 并往一个陶罐里装满了水——

**for he knew by experience** 【原因】因为他凭经验知道山里的水井稀少、
**that the mountain wells were few and far between.** → 相距遥远。

**He had hardly completed his arrangements** 他几乎刚刚完成这些准备——

**before the farmer returned with his daughter all** 老农夫就带着她的女儿回来了，
**dressed and ready for a start.** → 女儿已梳洗打扮好，随时可以出发。

**The greeting between the lovers was warm, but brief,** 两个恋人的重逢热情洋溢，却简短仓促——

**for minutes were precious,** 【原因】因为分分秒秒都弥足珍贵——

**and there was much to be done.** → 还有很多事情要做。

---

**"We must make our start at once," said Jefferson Hope,** "我们必须立即出发，"杰弗逊·霍普说道——

**speaking in a low but resolute voice,** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的声音？→ 声音低沉却坚定——

**like one who realizes the greatness of the peril,** [比喻] 像谁那样？→ 像一个意识到危险之巨大——

**but has steeled his heart to meet it.** 但已经钢铁般坚定了心志去迎接的人。

**"The front and back entrances are watched,** "前后两个出口都有人盯着——

**but with caution we may get away through** 【转折】但只要谨慎，
**the side window** → 我们可以从侧面的窗户溜出去，
**and across the fields.** → 穿过田野。

**Once on the road we are only two** 一旦上了路，
**miles from the Ravine** → 我们离山谷只有两英里——

**where the horses are waiting.** [定从-句尾补充] 哪条山谷？→ 马儿在等着的那条山谷。

**By daybreak we should be half-way through the mountains."** 到天亮之前，我们应该已经穿越了一半的山路。"

---

**"What if we are stopped," asked Ferrier.** "万一我们被拦住了，"费瑞尔问道。

---

**Hope slapped the revolver butt** 霍普拍了拍左轮手枪的枪柄——

**which protruded from the front of his tunic.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么枪柄？→ 从他上衣前面突出来的那个枪柄。

**"If they are too many for us** 【条件·心悬着】"如果他们人太多我们对付不了——【等"我们就……"】

**we shall take two** 【结果落地】我们就带上他们中的两三个一起去，
**or three of them with us," he said** → "他带着一抹凶险的微笑说道。
**with a sinister smile.** →

---

**The lights inside the house had all been extinguished,** 屋内的灯光全都熄灭了——

**and from the darkened window Ferrier peered over the fields** 费瑞尔从幽暗的窗口俯望那些田野——

**which had been his own,** [定从-句中插入] 什么田野？→ 曾经属于他的那些田野——

**and which he was now about to abandon for ever.** → 如今他即将永远抛下的田野。

**He had long nerved himself to the sacrifice, however,** 【让步·转折】然而，他早已做好了牺牲的心理准备——

**and the thought of the honour** → 而且想到女儿的荣誉与幸福—
**and happiness of his daughter** → —

**outweighed any regret at his ruined fortunes.** → 远胜过对自己破败家业的任何遗憾。

---

**All looked so peaceful and happy,** 一切看起来是如此宁静美好——

**the rustling trees and the broad silent stretch of grain-land,** [同位语] 具体是什么？→ 那沙沙作响的树木，那片宽阔、沉寂的麦田——

**that it was difficult to realize** 【口袋兑现】宁静到什么程度？→ 以至于人们难以意识到——

**that the spirit of murder lurked through it all.** 杀机已经潜伏其间。

**Yet the white face** →
**and set expression of the young hunter** → 【让步·转折】然而，年轻猎人那苍白的脸和凝固的表情—

**showed that in his approach to the house** → 表明他在靠近房子的途中——

**he had seen enough to satisfy him upon that head.** 已经看到了足够多让他确信这一点的东西。

---

**Ferrier carried the bag of gold and notes,** 费瑞尔带着那袋金币和钞票——

**Jefferson Hope had the scanty provisions and water,** 杰弗逊·霍普带着少得可怜的食物和水——

**while Lucy had a small bundle** → 露西则带着一个小包裹——

**containing a few of her more valued possessions.** [分词-后置修饰] 装着什么？→ 装着她几件最珍视的物品。

---

**Opening the window very slowly and carefully,** [分词-句首状语] 先做什么？→ 极缓极慢地把窗户推开——

**they waited until a dark cloud had somewhat** 他们等到一片乌云遮蔽了夜色—
**obscured the night,** → —

**and then one by one passed through into** → 然后一个接一个地穿窗进入那片小花园。
**the little garden.** →

**With bated breath and crouching figures** [状语前置] 以什么样的姿态？→ 屏住呼吸、弓着腰——

**they stumbled across it,** → 他们摸黑穿越了花园——

**and gained the shelter of the hedge,** → 抵达了树篱的遮蔽之处——

**which they skirted until they came to the gap** [定从-句尾补充] 然后沿着树篱走——直到走到那个缺口——

**which opened into the cornfields.** [定从-句尾补充] 哪个缺口？→ 通往玉米田的那个缺口。

---

**They had just reached this point** 他们刚刚到达这个地点——

**when the young man seized his two companions** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，那年轻人抓住了他的两个同伴——

**and dragged them down into the shadow,** → 将他们拽进阴影中——

**where they lay silent and trembling.** [定从-句尾补充] 躲在哪里？→ 在那里他们一声不吭、浑身颤抖地趴着。

---

**It was as well** →
**that his prairie training had given Jefferson Hope** →
**the ears of a lynx.** → 幸好他的草原历练赋予了杰弗逊·霍普一双猞猁般灵敏的耳朵。

**He and his friends had hardly crouched down** 他和他的伙伴们刚刚蹲下——

**before the melancholy hooting of a mountain owl** 就听见几码之外传来一声哀愁的山猫头鹰叫声—
**was heard within a few yards of them,** → —

**which was immediately answered by another hoot at** [定从-句尾补充] 什么叫声？
**a small distance.** → 紧接着被不远处另一声呼应的叫声回应的叫声。

**At the same moment a vague shadowy figure** 就在同一时刻，
**emerged from the gap** → 一个模糊的幽影从缺口处现身——

**for which they had been making,** [定从-句中插入] 哪个缺口？→ 他们原本要走的那个缺口——

**and uttered the plaintive signal cry again,** → 再次发出那哀怨的信号叫声——

**on which a second man appeared out of the obscurity.** [定从-句尾补充] 叫声之后呢？→ 应声又一个男人从黑暗中现身。

---

**"To-morrow at midnight," said the first** "明天午夜，
**who appeared to be in authority.** → "那个看起来是头领的男人说道。

**"When the Whip-poor-Will calls three times."** "当夜莺叫三声的时候。"

---

**"It is well," returned the other. "Shall I** "好的，"另一个应道。
**tell Brother Drebber?"** → "我要告诉德雷伯兄弟吗？"

---

**"Pass it on to him,** "传给他，再由他传给其他人。
**and from him to the others. Nine to seven!"** → 九减七！"

---

**"Seven to five!" repeated the other,** "七减五！"另一个重复道——

**and the two figures flitted away in different directions.** → 两个人影向不同方向飘然而去。

**Their concluding words had evidently been some form** 他们最后的话显然是某种暗号和回令。
**of sign and countersign.** →

---

**The instant that their footsteps had died away** 他们的脚步声刚在远处消逝—
**in the distance,** → —

**Jefferson Hope sprang to his feet,** 杰弗逊·霍普立刻跃起——

**and helping his companions through the gap,** [分词-句末伴随] → 帮助他的同伴们穿过缺口——

**led the way across the fields at the** → 以最快的速度带头穿越田野—
**top of his speed,** → —

**supporting and half-carrying the girl** [分词-句末伴随] 同时怎么做？→ 搀扶着、半抱着那个女孩——

**when her strength appeared to fail her.** 【情境】什么时候？→ 每当她的体力看起来要支撑不住的时候。

---

**"Hurry on! hurry on!" he gasped from time to time.** "快走！快走！"他不时喘着气催促道。

**"We are through the line of sentinels.** "我们已经穿过了哨兵的封锁线。

**Everything depends on speed. Hurry on!"** 一切都取决于速度。快走！"

---

**Once on the high road they made rapid progress.** 一上大路，他们的速度就快多了。

**Only once did they meet anyone,** 他们只遇到过一个人——

**and then they managed to slip into a field,** → 而那时他们设法溜进了一片田地——

**and so avoid recognition.** → 从而避开了被认出。

---

**Before reaching the town the hunter branched away** 在到达小镇之前，猎人拐上了一条岔路——

**into a rugged** [定从-句尾补充] 什么岔路？
**and narrow footpath** → 一条通往山脉的崎岖狭窄的小路。
**which led to the mountains.** →

**Two dark jagged peaks loomed above them through the darkness,** 两座黑暗、嶙峋的山峰在黑暗中矗立于他们头顶——

**and the defile which led between them** → 而那条穿行其间的山谷通道——

**was the Eagle Cañon in** → 正是那条马儿在等候他们的鹰谷峡谷。
**which the horses were awaiting them.** →

---

**With unerring instinct Jefferson Hope picked his way** 凭着精准的直觉，杰弗逊·霍普摸索着前进——

**among the great boulders** 穿行在巨大的岩石之间，
**and along the bed of a dried-up watercourse,** → 沿着干涸的河床行进——

**until he came to the retired corner, screened with rocks,** 直到他来到那个被岩石遮蔽的僻静角落——

**where the faithful animals had been picketed.** [定从-句尾补充] 在哪里？→ 那些忠实的动物被拴在那里等候。

**The girl was placed upon the mule,** 女孩被扶上了骡子——

**and old Ferrier upon one of the horses,** → 老费瑞尔骑上其中一匹马，
**with his money-bag,** → 随身带着他的钱袋——

**while Jefferson Hope led the other along the** → 而杰弗逊·霍普则牵着另一匹马，
**precipitous and dangerous path.** → 沿着那条险峻危险的小路前行。

---

**It was a bewildering route** 那是一条令人迷惑的路——

**for anyone who was not accustomed to face** 对于任何不习惯面对自然界最狂野面目的人而言。
**Nature in her wildest moods.** →

**On the one side a great crag towered** 一侧，一块巨大的峭壁高耸千尺乃至更高—
**up a thousand feet or more,** → —

**black, stern, and menacing,** [插入修饰] 什么样的？→ 黝黑、严峻、充满威胁——

**with long basaltic columns upon its rugged surface** [with-描述特点] 表面有什么？→ 在它那崎岖的表面上排列着长长的玄武岩柱——

**like the ribs of some petrified monster.** 像什么？→ 像某只石化了的怪兽的肋骨。

**On the other hand a wild chaos of** 另一侧，
**boulders and debris** → 是一片乱石和碎块堆积的混乱地带——

**made all advance impossible.** → 使任何前进都无从实现。

---

**Between the two ran the irregular track,** 两者之间，一条崎岖不平的小道蜿蜒而过——

**so narrow in places** 有些地方是如此狭窄——

**that they had to travel in Indian file,** 【口袋兑现】狭窄到什么程度？→ 以至于他们不得不排成单行前进——

**and so rough** 而且如此崎岖，
**that only practised riders could have traversed it at all.** → 只有有经验的骑手才能通过。

**Yet in spite of all dangers and difficulties,** 【让步·转折】然而，尽管危险重重、困难丛生——

**the hearts of the fugitives were light within them,** 逃亡者们的心里却是轻盈的——

**for every step increased the distance** 【原因】因为每一步都在增加着距离——

**between them and the terrible despotism from** 他们与那正在逃离的可怕专制统治之间的距离。
**which they were flying.** →

---

**They soon had a proof,** 【转折】然而他们很快就得到了证明—
**however, that they were still within the jurisdiction** → —
**of the Saints.** → 他们仍在圣徒们的管辖范围之内。

**They had reached the very wildest** 他们已经到达了山道最荒凉、
**and most desolate portion of the pass** → 最孤寂的地段——

**when the girl gave a startled cry, and pointed upwards.** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，女孩发出一声惊叫，朝上面指去。

**On a rock which overlooked the track,** 在一块俯瞰小道的岩石上——

**showing out dark and plain against the sky,** [分词-后置修饰] 看起来怎样？→ 在天空的映衬下显得黑暗而分明——

**there stood a solitary sentinel.** ← 回来接谓语 → 孤零零地站着一个哨兵。

**He saw them as soon as they perceived him,** 他看见他们，和他们看见他几乎同时——

**and his military challenge of "Who goes there?"** → 他那军人式的喝问"何人经过？"——

**rang through the silent ravine.** → 响彻了寂静的山谷。

---

**"Travellers for Nevada," said Jefferson Hope,** "前往内华达的旅人，
**with his hand upon the rifle** → "杰弗逊·霍普说道，
**which hung by his saddle.** → 手搭在马鞍旁挂着的步枪上。

---

**They could see the lonely watcher fingering his gun,** 他们能看见那孤独的哨兵摆弄着他的枪——

**and peering down at them** → 俯视着他们——

**as if dissatisfied at their reply.** 好像对他们的回答不满意。

---

**"By whose permission?" he asked.** "谁批准的？"他问道。

---

**"The Holy Four," answered Ferrier.** "神圣四人委员会，"费瑞尔回答。

**His Mormon experiences had taught him** 他的摩门经历教会了他——

**that that was the highest authority to** 那是他所能援引的最高权威。
**which he could refer.** →

---

**"Nine from seven," cried the sentinel.** "九减七！"哨兵喊道。

---

**"Seven from five," returned Jefferson Hope promptly,** "七减五，"杰弗逊·霍普迅速回应道——

**remembering the countersign which he had heard in the garden.** [分词-句末伴随] 他记起了什么？→ 想起了他在花园里听到的那个回令。

---

**"Pass, and the Lord go with you," said** "通过，愿上帝同行，
**the voice from above.** → "上面传来声音。

**Beyond his post the path broadened out,** 过了他的哨位，小路变宽了——

**and the horses were able to break into a trot.** → 马儿得以小跑起来。

**Looking back, they could see the solitary watcher** 回头望去，
**leaning upon his gun,** → 他们能看见那孤独的哨兵靠着他的枪站着——

**and knew that they had passed the outlying** → 并且知道，
**post of the chosen people,** → 他们已经通过了那个选民之地的外围哨所——

**and that freedom lay before them.** → 而自由就在前方。

---



---

### 第五章 复仇天使
### CHAPTER V. THE AVENGING ANGELS.

---

**All night their course lay through intricate defiles** 整整一夜，他们的路途穿行于错综复杂的峡谷之间——

**and over irregular and rock-strewn paths.** → 以及崎岖不平、乱石遍布的小道上。

**More than once they lost their way,** 他们不止一次迷了路——

**but Hope's intimate knowledge of the mountains** 【转折】但霍普对山脉的深厚了解——

**enabled them to regain the track once more.** → 让他们一次次地找回了道路。

---

**When morning broke,** 当晨光破晓——

**a scene of marvellous though savage beauty lay before them.** 一幅奇丽却带着几分野性之美的景象展现在他们眼前。

**In every direction the great snow-capped peaks hemmed them in,** 四面八方，巍峨的雪顶山峰将他们围拢——

**peeping over each other's shoulders to the far horizon.** [分词-后置修饰] 山峰在干什么？→ 彼此从对方肩头探出头来，望向遥远的地平线。

---

**So steep were the rocky banks on either** 【倒装强调·心悬着】两侧的岩壁是如此陡峭——
**side of them,** → 【so...that 的口袋张开】

**that the larch** 【口袋兑现】陡峭到什么程度？
**and the pine seemed to be suspended over their heads,** → 以至于那些落叶松和松树看起来像是悬在他们头顶——

**and to need only a gust of wind** → 只需一阵风，
**to come hurtling down upon them.** → 就会呼啸着砸下来。

**Nor was the fear entirely an illusion,** 这种恐惧也并非全是幻觉——

**for the barren valley was thickly strewn with** 【原因】因为那片荒谷里密密麻麻地散落着树木和巨石—
**trees and boulders** → —

**which had fallen in a similar manner.** [定从-句尾补充] 怎样的树木巨石？→ 以类似方式倒下来的那些。

---

**Even as they passed, a great rock came thundering down** 就在他们经过时，一块巨石轰然滚落——

**with a hoarse rattle** 发出一阵沙哑的隆隆声——

**which woke the echoes in the silent gorges,** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的隆隆声？→ 在寂静的峡谷中激起了回声的——

**and startled the weary horses into a gallop.** → 并把疲惫的马匹惊得扬蹄飞奔。

---

**As the sun rose slowly above the eastern horizon,** 随着太阳从东方地平线上缓缓升起——

**the caps of the great mountains lit up** 那些大山的山顶一座接一座地被点亮—
**one after the other,** → —

**like lamps at a festival,** 像什么？→ 像节日里的一盏盏灯火——

**until they were all ruddy and glowing.** 【情境·直到】直到全都泛起玫瑰色的辉光。

---

**The magnificent spectacle cheered the hearts of the three fugitives** 这壮丽的景象鼓舞了三个逃亡者的心——

**and gave them fresh energy.** → 给了他们新的力气。

**At a wild torrent which swept out of a ravine** 在一道从峡谷中奔涌而出的急流旁——

**they called a halt and watered their horses,** 他们停下来，给马儿饮水——

**while they partook of a hasty breakfast.** → 同时匆匆吃了顿早饭。

---

**Lucy and her father would fain have rested longer,** 露西和她父亲本想多歇息一会儿——

**but Jefferson Hope was inexorable.** 【让步·转折·主张落地】但杰弗逊·霍普铁石心肠，毫不通融。

**"They will be upon our track by this** "他们这时候已经在追踪我们了，
**time," he said.** → "他说。

**"Everything depends upon our speed.** "一切都取决于我们的速度。

**Once safe in Carson we may rest** 一旦安全抵达卡森，
**for the remainder of our lives."** → 我们余生就可以歇息了。"

---

**During the whole of** 那整整一天，
**that day they struggled on through the defiles,** → 他们都在艰难地穿行于峡谷之间——

**and by evening they calculated** 到傍晚，他们估算——

**that they were more than thirty miles from their enemies.** 他们已经距离那些敌人三十多英里了。

**At night-time they chose the base of a beetling crag,** 入夜，他们选了一块突出岩石的底部——

**where the rocks offered some protection from the chill wind,** [定从-句尾补充] 选在哪里？→ 岩石能提供一些遮风的地方——

**and there huddled together for warmth,** → 在那里紧紧缩在一起取暖——

**they enjoyed a few hours' sleep.** → 享受了几小时的睡眠。

---

**Before daybreak, however,** 【转折】然而天亮前他们就起身，
**they were up** → 再次上路了。
**and on their way once more.** →

**They had seen no signs of any pursuers,** 他们没有看到任何追兵的迹象——

**and Jefferson Hope began to think** → 杰弗逊·霍普开始认为——

**that they were fairly out of the reach** 认为什么？→ 他们算是已经脱离了——

**of the terrible organization whose enmity they had incurred.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么组织的掌控？→ 那个他们已惹上的可怕组织的掌控。

**He little knew how far that iron grasp could reach,** 他万万不知道那铁腕的掌控能伸多远——

**or how soon it was to close upon** → 也不知道它会多快地扼住他们，
**them and crush them.** → 将他们粉碎。

---

**About the middle of the second day of their flight** 逃亡第二天的中途——

**their scanty store of provisions began to run out.** 他们那点少得可怜的食物开始告罄。

**This gave the hunter little uneasiness, however,** 【让步·转折】然而这给猎人带来的忧虑并不大——

**for there was game to be had among the mountains,** 【原因】因为山里有猎物可猎——

**and he had frequently** → 而且他以前也常常不得不靠猎枪维持生计。
**before had to depend upon his rifle** →
**for the needs of life.** →

---

**Choosing a sheltered nook,** [分词-句首状语] 先做什么？→ 选了一处隐蔽的角落——

**he piled together a few dried branches** 他堆起几根干树枝，
**and made a blazing fire,** → 生起一堆烈火——

**at which his companions might warm themselves,** [定从-句尾补充] 为了什么？→ 让他的伙伴们可以在旁边取暖——

**for they were now nearly five thousand feet** 【原因】因为他们现在已在海拔将近五千英尺的高处—
**above the sea level,** → —

**and the air was bitter and keen.** → 空气冷冽而刺骨。

---

**Having tethered the horses, and bade Lucy adieu,** [分词-句首状语] 先做什么？→ 拴好马匹，向露西道别之后——

**he threw his gun over his shoulder,** → 他把猎枪往肩上一搭——

**and set out in search of whatever chance** → 出发去寻找任何碰巧能遇到的猎物。
**might throw in his way.** →

**Looking back he saw the old man** [分词-句首状语] 回头一望——
**and the young girl crouching over the blazing fire,** → 他看见老人和年轻女孩蜷缩在火堆旁——

**while the three animals stood motionless in the back-ground.** → 而那三头牲口纹丝不动地站在远处。

**Then the intervening rocks hid them from his view.** 然后，中间的岩石遮住了他们的身影。

---

**He walked for a couple of miles through** 他一个峡谷接一个峡谷地走了好几英里—
**one ravine after another** → —

**without success,** 却毫无所获——

**though from the marks upon the bark of** 【让步】尽管从树皮上的爪痕和其他迹象来看—
**the trees, and other indications,** → —

**he judged that there were numerous bears in the vicinity.** 他判断附近有不少熊。

---

**At last, after two or three hours' fruitless search,** 终于，经过两三个小时毫无结果的搜寻之后——

**he was thinking of turning back in despair,** 他正打算绝望地折返——

**when casting his eyes upwards** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，他向上望去——

**he saw a sight** →
**which sent a thrill of pleasure through his heart.** → 看见了一幕令他心头涌起一阵喜悦的景象。

**On the edge of a jutting pinnacle,** 在一块突出岩尖的边缘上——

**three or four hundred feet above him,** 在他头顶三四百英尺处——

**there stood a creature somewhat resembling a sheep in appearance,** ← 回来接谓语 → 站着一只外形有些像羊的动物——

**but armed with a pair of gigantic horns.** 【转折】但长着一对巨大的角。

**The big-horn—for so it is called—** 大角羊——这便是它的名字——

**was acting, probably, as a guardian over a flock** 大概是在充当羊群的守卫——

**which were invisible to the hunter;** [定从-句尾补充] 什么羊群？→ 猎人看不见的那群羊——

**but fortunately it was heading in the opposite direction,** 【转折】但幸运的是，它正朝反方向望去——

**and had not perceived him.** → 并未发现他。

---

**Lying on his face,** [分词-句首状语] 他怎么做的？→ 趴在地上——

**he rested his rifle upon a rock,** → 把步枪架在一块岩石上——

**and took a long** → 仔细瞄准了很久，
**and steady aim** → 然后扣下扳机。
**before drawing the trigger.** →

**The animal sprang into the air,** 那动物腾空而起——

**tottered for a moment upon the edge of the precipice,** → 在悬崖边摇晃了一下——

**and then came crashing down into the valley beneath.** → 然后轰然坠入下面的山谷。

---

**The creature was too unwieldy to lift,** 这动物太笨重，无法抬起——

**so the hunter contented himself** 【结果】所以猎人就满足于——

**with cutting away one haunch and part of the flank.** 只割下一条后腿和部分腹侧肉。

**With this trophy over his shoulder,** [状语前置] 带着什么出发？→ 扛着这份战利品——

**he hastened to retrace his steps,** → 他急忙原路返回——

**for the evening was already drawing in.** 【原因】因为傍晚已经来临。

---

**He had hardly started, however,** 【让步·转折】然而他刚出发没多久——

**before he realized the difficulty which faced him.** → 就意识到了摆在他面前的困难。

**In his eagerness he had wandered far past** 因为急于追猎，他走得太远，
**the ravines which were known to him,** → 早已越过了他熟悉的那些峡谷——

**and it was no easy matter to pick** → 要找出他来时走过的路并不容易。
**out the path** →
**which he had taken.** →

**The valley in** 他所在的山谷分叉再分叉，
**which he found himself divided** → 分成了许多支谷——
**and sub-divided into many gorges,** →

**which were so like each other** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的支谷？→ 彼此如此相像——

**that it was impossible to distinguish one from the other.** 【结果】以至于根本无从分辨。

---

**He followed one for a mile or more** 他沿着其中一条走了一英里多——

**until he came to a mountain torrent** 【情境·直到】直到遇见一道山中急流——

**which he was sure that he had never seen before.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么急流？→ 他确信自己从未见过的那道急流。

**Convinced that he had taken the wrong turn,** [分词-句首状语] 确认了什么之后？→ 确认自己走错了路之后——

**he tried another, but with the same result.** 他试了另一条，却得到同样的结果。

---

**Night was coming on rapidly,** 夜色迅速降临——

**and it was almost dark** → 天几乎全黑了——

**before he at last found himself in a** 才终于走进了一条他熟悉的峡谷。
**defile which was familiar to him.** →

**Even then it was no easy matter to** 即便如此，
**keep to the right track,** → 要保持在正确的路上也非易事——

**for the moon had not yet risen,** 【原因】因为月亮还未升起——

**and the high cliffs on either side made** → 两侧高耸的峭壁让黑暗更加深沉。
**the obscurity more profound.** →

---

**Weighed down with his burden, and weary from his exertions,** [分词-句首状语] 他是什么状态？→ 被猎物的重量压着，被体力消耗折磨着——

**he stumbled along,** 他跌跌撞撞地前行——

**keeping up his heart by the reflection** [分词-句末伴随] 靠什么支撑？→ 靠着这个念想撑着心气——

**that every step brought him nearer to Lucy,** 什么念想？→ 每一步都让他离露西更近——

**and that he carried with him enough** → 以及他身上带的食物足够——

**to ensure them food for the remainder of their journey.** 保证他们完成剩余旅程的口粮。

---

**He had now come to the mouth of** 他现在已来到那条峡谷的入口—
**the very defile** → —

**in which he had left them.** [定从-句尾补充] 哪条峡谷？→ 他留下他们的那条峡谷。

**Even in the darkness he could recognize the** 即便在黑暗中，
**outline of the cliffs** → 他也能认出那些悬崖的轮廓——

**which bounded it.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么悬崖？→ 围绕着这条峡谷的那些悬崖。

**They must, he reflected, be awaiting him anxiously,** 他心想，他们一定在焦急地等着他——

**for he had been absent nearly five hours.** 【原因】因为他已经离开将近五个小时了。

---

**In the gladness of his heart** 内心充满欣喜——

**he put his hands to his mouth** 他用双手围成喇叭口——

**and made the glen re-echo to a loud** 让山谷里回响起一声响亮的呼喊，
**halloo as a signal** → 作为他即将到来的信号。
**that he was coming.** →

**He paused and listened for an answer.** 他停下来，侧耳倾听回应。

**None came save his own cry,** 什么都没有，只有他自己的呼喊声——

**which clattered up the dreary silent ravines,** 在那片寂静荒凉的峡谷中回响——

**and was borne back to his ears in countless repetitions.** → 一遍又一遍地传回他的耳中。

---

**Again he shouted, even louder than before,** 他再次呼喊，比之前更大声——

**and again no whisper came back** → 依然没有任何回音传来——

**from the friends** →
**whom he had left such a short time ago.** → 从那些他才离开没多久的伙伴那里。

**A vague, nameless dread came over him,** 一种模糊的、无以名状的恐惧笼罩了他——

**and he hurried onwards frantically,** → 他疯狂地向前冲去——

**dropping the precious food in his agitation.** [分词-句末伴随] 同时怎样？→ 在慌乱中丢弃了那些珍贵的食物。

---

**When he turned the corner,** 当他转过弯角——

**he came full in sight of the spot** 他正好看到了那个曾经生过火的地点。
**where the fire had been lit.** →

**There was still a glowing pile of wood ashes there,** 那里还有一堆燃着余烬的木灰——

**but it had evidently not been tended since his departure.** 【转折】但显然自他离开后就没人照管过了。

**The same dead silence still reigned all round.** 同样的死寂依然笼罩四周。

---

**With his fears all changed to convictions,** [状语前置] 带着什么心情？→ 带着已由恐惧变成确信的心情——

**he hurried on.** → 他继续向前奔去。

**There was no living creature near the remains** 火堆余烬旁没有任何活物：
**of the fire:** →

**animals, man, maiden, all were gone.** 牲口、老人、少女，全都不见了。

**It was only too clear** 这再清楚不过——

**that some sudden** →
**and terrible disaster had occurred during his absence** → 在他不在的这段时间里发生了某种突如其来的可怕灾难—

**—a disaster which had embraced them all,** [同位语-定从] 什么灾难？→ 一场波及了所有人的灾难——

**and yet had left no traces behind it.** → 却没有留下任何痕迹的灾难。

---

**Bewildered and stunned by this blow,** [分词-句首状语] 他是什么状态？→ 被这打击搞得茫然失措、目瞪口呆——

**Jefferson Hope felt his head spin round,** 杰弗逊·霍普感到脑袋一阵眩晕——

**and had to lean upon his rifle to** → 不得不倚靠着步枪，
**save himself from falling.** → 才没有倒下。

**He was essentially a man of action, however,** 【让步·转折】然而，他从根本上是一个行动派——

**and speedily recovered from his temporary impotence.** → 很快就从一时的无助中缓了过来。

---

**Seizing a half-consumed piece of wood from the smouldering fire,** [分词-句首状语] 先做什么？→ 从阴燃的火堆中抓起一根半截的木柴——

**he blew it into a flame,** → 他将它吹出火焰——

**and proceeded with its help to examine the little camp.** → 借着火光开始检查那小小的营地。

**The ground was all stamped down by the** 地面被马蹄踩得乱成一片—
**feet of horses,** → —

**showing that a large party of mounted men** [分词-后置修饰] 说明了什么？
**had overtaken the fugitives,** → 说明一大队骑马的人追上了逃亡者——

**and the direction of their tracks proved** → 而他们蹄印的方向证明——

**that they had afterwards turned back to Salt Lake City.** 他们随后折返了盐湖城。

---

**Had they carried back both of his companions with them?** 他们把他的两个同伴都带走了吗？

**Jefferson Hope had almost persuaded himself** 杰弗逊·霍普几乎已经说服自己，
**that they must have done so,** → 他们一定是那样做的——

**when his eye fell upon an object** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，他的目光落在了一个东西上——

**which made every nerve of his body tingle within him.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么东西？→ 让他全身每一根神经都刺痛起来的那个东西。

**A little way on one side of the camp** 就在营地一旁不远处——

**was a low-lying heap of reddish soil,** ← 回来接谓语 → 有一堆低矮的红色土丘——

**which had assuredly not been there before.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么土丘？→ 之前这里肯定没有的那堆土丘。

---

**There was no mistaking it** 那无疑就是一座新挖的坟墓，
**for anything but a newly-dug grave.** → 不可能是别的。

**As the young hunter approached it,** 当年轻猎人走近时——

**he perceived that a stick had been planted on it,** 他发现上面插着一根木棍——

**with a sheet of paper stuck in the** [with-描述状态] 木棍上有什么？
**cleft fork of it.** → 在分叉处夹着一张纸。

**The inscription upon the paper was brief,** 纸上的文字简短，
**but to the point:** → 却直截了当：

---

> **JOHN FERRIER,**
>
> **FORMERLY OF SALT LAKE CITY,**
>
> **Died August 4th, 1860.**
>
> 约翰·费瑞尔，
>
> 前盐湖城居民，
>
> 卒于1860年8月4日。

---

**The sturdy old man,** 那个他才刚刚离开不久的结实老人，
**whom he had left** → 就这样走了——
**so short a time before,** →
**was gone, then,** →

**and this was all his epitaph.** → 而这，便是他全部的墓志铭。

**Jefferson Hope looked wildly round** 杰弗逊·霍普茫然地四处张望——

**to see if there was a second grave,** 寻找是否有第二座坟——

**but there was no sign of one.** 却没有任何迹象。

**Lucy had been carried back by their terrible pursuers** 露西被那些可怕的追兵带了回去——

**to fulfil her original destiny,** 去实现她最初的命运——

**by becoming one of the harem of the Elder's son.** 成为某位长老之子后宫中的一员。

---

**As the young fellow realized the certainty of her fate,** 当这年轻人意识到她命运的确定无疑——

**and his own powerlessness to prevent it,** → 以及自己无力阻止这一切——

**he wished that he,** →
**too, was lying with the old farmer in** →
**his last silent resting-place.** → 他真希望自己也能躺在那老农夫那最后的静谧安息之所里。

---

**Again, however, his active spirit shook off the lethargy** 【转折】然而，他那活跃的精神再次甩掉了那种麻木——

**which springs from despair.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么麻木？→ 从绝望中滋生的那种麻木。

**If there was nothing else left to him,** 【条件·心悬着】如果什么都没剩下了——【等"那他至少可以……"】

**he could at least devote his life to revenge.** 【结果落地】他至少还可以将余生献给复仇。

---

**With indomitable patience and perseverance,** [状语前置] 霍普是什么样的人？→ 有着不屈不挠的耐心和毅力——

**Jefferson Hope possessed also a power of sustained vindictiveness,** 杰弗逊·霍普还拥有一种持久的复仇意志——

**which he may have learned from the Indians** [定从-句尾补充] 从哪里学到的？
**amongst whom he had lived.** → 也许是从他生活过的那些印第安人那里学到的。

**As he stood by the desolate fire,** 当他站在那片荒凉的余烬旁——

**he felt that the only one thing** 他感到，唯一一件事——

**which could assuage his grief** [定从-句中插入] 什么事？→ 能平息他悲痛的那件事——

**would be thorough and complete retribution,** ← 回来接 → 就是彻底、完全的清算——

**brought by his own hand upon his enemies.** [分词-后置修饰] 什么样的清算？→ 由他亲手施加于仇敌的那种清算。

---

**His strong will** 他决意，
**and untiring energy should,** → 他坚强的意志和不知疲倦的精力，
**he determined, be devoted to that one end.** → 将全部献给这一个目标。

**With a grim, white face,** [状语前置] 带着什么表情？→ 带着一张铁青、苍白的脸——

**he retraced his steps to** → 他原路折返，
**where he had dropped the food,** → 找到了他丢弃食物的地方——

**and having stirred up the smouldering fire,** [分词-句末伴随] → 拨旺了那堆阴燃的火——

**he cooked enough to last him for a few days.** → 烹制了足够他撑几天的食物。

**This he made up into a bundle,** 他把这些食物打成一个包裹——

**and, tired as he was,** → 然后，尽管疲惫不堪，
**he set himself to walk back through the mountains** → 他还是迈步踏上了穿越山脉的归途——

**upon the track of the avenging angels.** 沿着那些复仇天使留下的踪迹前行。

---

**For five days he toiled footsore** 五天里，他脚掌磨烂、
**and weary through the defiles** → 精疲力竭地穿行于峡谷之间——

**which he had already traversed on horseback.** [定从-句尾补充] 哪些峡谷？→ 他骑马走过的那些峡谷。

**At night he flung himself down among the rocks,** 夜里，他把自己扔倒在岩石间——

**and snatched a few hours of sleep;** → 打上几个小时的盹儿——

**but before daybreak he was always well on his way.** 【转折】但天亮之前，他早已重新上路。

---

**On the sixth day, he reached the Eagle Cañon,** 第六天，他到达了鹰谷峡谷——

**from which they had commenced their ill-fated flight.** [定从-句尾补充] 哪里的峡谷？→ 他们那次命运多舛的逃亡就是从那里开始的。

**Thence he could look down upon the home** 从那里，
**of the saints.** → 他能俯瞰圣徒们的家园。

**Worn and exhausted,** [分词-句首状语] 他是什么状态？→ 憔悴而疲惫——

**he leaned upon his rifle** → 他倚着步枪，
**and shook his gaunt hand fiercely** → 愤然挥动着他那瘦削的手——

**at the silent widespread city beneath him.** 朝着他脚下那片沉默、广袤的城市。

---

**As he looked at it,** 当他凝视着那座城市——

**he observed that there were flags in some** 他注意到一些主要街道上挂着旗帜—
**of the principal streets,** → —

**and other signs of festivity.** → 以及其他节日的迹象。

**He was still speculating as to what this might mean** 他正在猜测这意味着什么——

**when he heard the clatter of horse's hoofs,** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，他听见了马蹄声——

**and saw a mounted man riding towards him.** → 并看见一个骑马的人朝他骑来。

**As he approached,** 走近时，
**he recognized him** → 他认出此人是一个叫考伯的摩门教徒—
**as a Mormon named Cowper,** → —

**to whom he had rendered services at different times.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的人？→ 他曾在不同时候帮助过的那个人。

**He therefore accosted him when he got up to him,** 因此，对方靠近时他便主动搭话——

**with the object of finding out what Lucy** 目的是打听露西·费瑞尔的命运。
**Ferrier's fate had been.** →

---

**"I am Jefferson Hope," he said. "You remember me."** "我是杰弗逊·霍普，"他说。"你还记得我。"

---

**The Mormon looked at him with undisguised astonishment** 摩门教徒毫不掩饰地惊讶地看着他——

**—indeed, it was difficult to recognize** 确实，很难认出——

**in this tattered,** 从这个衣衫褴褛、蓬头垢面、
**unkempt wanderer, with ghastly white face** → 脸色惨白、
**and fierce, wild eyes,** → 目光凶狠而野性的流浪者身上——

**the spruce young hunter of former days.** 当年那个整洁干练的年轻猎人。

**Having, however, at last, satisfied himself as to his identity,** [分词-句首状语] 终于确认了他的身份之后——

**the man's surprise changed to consternation.** 那人的惊讶变成了惊恐。

---

**"You are mad to come here," he cried.** "你来这里是疯了，"他叫道。

**"It is as much** "被人看见和你说话，
**as my own life is worth to be** → 我自己的命也搭进去了。
**seen talking with you.** →

**There is a warrant against you from the Holy Four** 神圣四人委员会发出了对你的通缉令——

**for assisting the Ferriers away."** 罪名是协助费瑞尔一家出逃。"

---

**"I don't fear them, or their warrant," Hope said, earnestly.** "我不怕他们，也不怕他们的通缉令，"霍普郑重地说。

**"You must know something of this matter, Cowper.** "你一定知道这件事的来龙去脉，考伯。

**I conjure you by everything you hold dear** 我求你，以你所珍视的一切起誓，
**to answer a few questions.** → 回答我几个问题。

**We have always been friends.** 我们一直是朋友。

**For God's sake, don't refuse to answer me."** 看在上帝的份上，不要拒绝回答我。"

---

**"What is it?" the Mormon asked uneasily. "Be quick.** "什么事？"摩门教徒不安地问。"快说。

**The very rocks have ears and the trees eyes."** 这里的石头都长着耳朵，树木都长着眼睛。"

---

**"What has become of Lucy Ferrier?"** "露西·费瑞尔怎么样了？"

---

**"She was married yesterday to young Drebber.** "她昨天嫁给了小德雷伯。

**Hold up, man,** 撑着点，撑着点，
**hold up, you have no life left in you."** → 你快没气了。"

---

**"Don't mind me," said Hope faintly.** "别管我，"霍普有气无力地说。

**He was white to the very lips,** 他白到了嘴唇——

**and had sunk down on the stone against** 已经瘫坐在他依靠着的那块石头上。
**which he had been leaning.** →

**"Married, you say?"** "你说，已经嫁了？"

---

**"Married yesterday—that's what those flags are** "昨天嫁的——
**for on the Endowment House.** → 那就是天恩堂上那些旗帜的缘由。

**There was some words between young Drebber and young Stangerson** 小德雷伯和小斯坦格森之间有过一番争论——

**as to which was to have her.** 争谁能娶到她。

**They'd both been in the party that followed them,** 他们两个都在追踪队伍里——

**and Stangerson had shot her father,** → 斯坦格森杀了她父亲——

**which seemed to give him the best claim;** → 这似乎给了他最有力的主张——

**but when they argued it out in council,** 【转折】但当他们在会议上辩论清楚之后——

**Drebber's party was the stronger,** → 德雷伯一方更强——

**so the Prophet gave her over to him.** 【结果】所以先知把她交给了他。

**No one won't have her very long though,** 不过也没人能长时间拥有她——

**for I saw death in her face yesterday.** 【原因】因为昨天我在她脸上看见了死亡。

**She is more like a ghost than a woman.** 她与其说是个女人，不如说是个鬼。

**Are you off, then?"** 那你要走了？"

---

**"Yes, I am off," said Jefferson Hope,** "是的，我要走了，"杰弗逊·霍普说，
**who had risen from his seat.** → 他已从石头上站起来。

**His face might have been chiselled out of marble,** 他的脸仿佛用大理石雕刻而成——

**so hard and set was its expression,** 是如此地坚硬、凝固——

**while its eyes glowed with a baleful light.** 而那双眼睛里燃烧着一种凶险的光芒。

---

**"Where are you going?"** "你去哪里？"

---

**"Never mind," he answered;** "没关系，"他回答——

**and, slinging his weapon over his shoulder,** [分词-句末伴随] → 把武器挎在肩上——

**strode off down the gorge** → 大步走下峡谷——

**and so away into the heart of the mountains** → 就这样走入山脉的腹地——

**to the haunts of the wild beasts.** 走向野兽出没之所。

**Amongst them all there was none** 在那些野兽之中，
**so fierce and** → 没有一个比他更凶猛、
**so dangerous as himself.** → 更危险。

---

**The prediction of the Mormon was only too well fulfilled.** 那个摩门教徒的预言被应验得太彻底了。

**Whether it was the terrible death of her father** 不管是她父亲那骇人的死——

**or the effects of the hateful marriage into** → 还是被逼迫进入那可憎婚姻的影响—
**which she had been forced,** → —

**poor Lucy never held up her head again,** ← 回来接 → 可怜的露西再也没有抬起过头——

**but pined away and died within a month.** → 而是日渐消沉，一个月内便去世了。

---

**Her sottish husband,** 她那个酒鬼丈夫——

**who had married her principally** [定从-句中插入] 什么丈夫？
**for the sake of John Ferrier's property,** → 娶她主要是为了约翰·费瑞尔财产的那个人——

**did not affect any great grief at his bereavement;** ← 回来接 → 对丧妻之事并未表现出什么深重的悲痛——
