**but his other wives mourned over her,** 【转折】但他的其他妻子们为她哭泣——

**and sat up with her the night before the burial,** → 并在下葬前的夜晚守着她——

**as is the Mormon custom.** 正如摩门的风俗。

---

**They were grouped round the bier in the** 清晨时分，
**early hours of the morning,** → 她们围着灵床聚集着——

**when, to their inexpressible fear and astonishment,** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，令她们无以言表的恐惧和惊愕中——

**the door was flung open,** 门被猛地撞开——

**and a savage-looking, weather-beaten man in tattered garments** → 一个面貌凶悍、饱经风霜、身着破烂衣衫的男人——

**strode into the room.** → 大步走进了房间。

**Without a glance or a word to the cowering women,** 对那些瑟缩的女人们不瞅一眼、不吐一字——

**he walked up to the white silent figure** → 他径直走向那具白静的身影——

**which had once contained the pure soul of Lucy Ferrier.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么身影？→ 曾经承载着露西·费瑞尔那纯洁灵魂的身影。

---

**Stooping over her,** [分词-句首状语] 先做什么？→ 俯身下去——

**he pressed his lips reverently to her cold forehead,** → 他虔敬地将嘴唇贴上她冰冷的额头——

**and then, snatching up her hand,** [分词-句末伴随] → 然后，抓起她的手——

**he took the wedding-ring from her finger.** → 将婚戒从她的手指上取下来。

**"She shall not be buried in** "她不该戴着这个入土，
**that," he cried with a fierce snarl,** → "他怒吼道——

**and before an alarm could be raised** → 在有人来得及发出警报之前——

**sprang down the stairs and was gone.** → 他已跳下楼梯，消失无踪。

---

**So strange and so brief was the episode,** 这一幕是如此奇异、如此短暂——

**that the watchers might have found it hard** 守灵的人们或许会觉得难以相信—
**to believe it themselves** → —

**or persuade other people of it,** → 或者很难说服别人相信——

**had it not been for the undeniable fact** 【假设·倒装条件】要不是有一个无可辩驳的事实——

**that the circlet of gold** 那只金环——

**which marked her as having been a bride** [定从-句中插入] 什么金环？→ 标志着她曾为人妇的那只金环——

**had disappeared.** ← 回来接 → 已经不见了。

---

**For some months Jefferson Hope lingered among the mountains,** 此后数月，杰弗逊·霍普流连于山间——

**leading a strange wild life,** [分词-句末伴随] 过着什么样的生活？→ 过着一种奇异而野性的生活——

**and nursing in his heart the fierce desire** → 心里滋养着那股强烈的复仇欲望，
**for vengeance which possessed him.** → 那欲望已完全占据了他。

**Tales were told in the City** 城里流传着故事——

**of the weird figure** →
**which was seen prowling about the suburbs,** → 关于那个被人看见在郊区游荡的神秘身影—

**and which haunted the lonely mountain gorges.** → 以及出没于僻静山谷的身影。

---

**Once a bullet whistled through Stangerson's window** 有一次，一颗子弹从斯坦格森的窗户呼啸而入——

**and flattened itself upon the wall within a** → 打扁在距他不到一英尺的墙上。
**foot of him.** →

**On another occasion, as Drebber passed under a cliff** 还有一次，当德雷伯经过一处峭壁下方时——

**a great boulder crashed down on him,** → 一块巨石轰然砸落——

**and he only escaped a terrible death** → 他才侥幸逃过了一场可怕的死亡——

**by throwing himself upon his face.** [分词-后置修饰] 怎么逃过的？→ 靠着扑倒在地。

---

**The two young Mormons were not long in discovering** 两个年轻的摩门教徒没过多久就发现了——

**the reason of these attempts upon their lives,** 这些对他们生命袭击的原因——

**and led repeated expeditions into the mountains** → 并多次带队进山——

**in the hope of capturing or killing their enemy,** 希望能抓住或杀死他们的敌人——

**but always without success.** 却屡屡无功而返。

---

**Then they adopted the precaution of never going** 于是他们开始采取预防措施，从不单独外出，
**out alone or after nightfall,** → 也不在夜幕降临后出门——

**and of having their houses guarded.** → 并让房子有人守卫。

**After a time they were able to relax these measures,** 一段时间后，他们得以放松这些措施——

**for nothing was either heard or seen of their opponent,** 【原因】因为他们的对手既没有任何音讯，也再未出现——

**and they hoped that time had cooled his vindictiveness.** → 他们希望时间已经冷却了他的复仇之火。

---

**Far from doing so,** 恰恰相反——

**it had, if anything, augmented it.** 如果说有什么变化，那只是更炽烈了。

**The hunter's mind was of a hard, unyielding nature,** 这猎人的心性是那种坚硬、不屈的——

**and the predominant idea of revenge** → 而那个主导一切的复仇念头——

**had taken such complete possession of it** 已经完全占据了他的心——

**that there was no room for any other emotion.** 以至于再没有任何其他情感的容身之所。

---

**He was, however, above all things practical.** 【转折】然而，他首先是个务实的人。

**He soon realized that even his iron constitution** 他很快意识到，就连他那铁打的体格——

**could not stand the incessant strain** 也承受不住他不断强加于它的折磨。
**which he was putting upon it.** →

**Exposure and want of wholesome food were wearing him out.** 风餐露宿和缺乏营养的食物正在把他消耗殆尽。

**If he died like a dog among the mountains,** 【条件·心悬着】如果他像条狗一样死在山里——【等"那复仇又从何谈起"】

**what was to become of his revenge then?** 【结果落地】那他的复仇又当如何？

**And yet such a death was sure to** 然而若他继续坚持，
**overtake him if he persisted.** → 这样的死亡必将降临。

---

**He felt that that was to play his enemy's game,** 他感到，那样做是在遂了敌人的心愿——

**so he reluctantly returned to the old Nevada mines,** 【结果】所以他不情愿地返回了内华达的旧矿场——

**there to recruit his health** 在那里恢复健康——

**and to amass money enough** → 并积攒足够的钱——

**to allow him to pursue his object without privation.** 来干什么？→ 让他能在不受物质匮乏之苦的情况下追求他的目标。

---

**His intention had been to be absent a** 他本打算最多离开一年—
**year at the most,** → —

**but a combination of unforeseen circumstances** 【转折】但一系列不可预见的情况——

**prevented his leaving the mines for nearly five.** → 使他在矿场滞留了将近五年。

**At the end of that time, however,** 然而到那段时间结束时——

**his memory of his wrongs and his craving for revenge** 他对所受冤屈的记忆和对复仇的渴望——

**were quite as keen as on that memorable night** → 依然和那个难忘的夜晚一样强烈——

**when he had stood by John Ferrier's grave.** [定从-句尾补充] 哪个夜晚？→ 他站在约翰·费瑞尔坟前的那个夜晚。

---

**Disguised, and under an assumed name,** [分词-句首状语·独立主格] 以什么身份？→ 乔装改扮，以假名——

**he returned to Salt Lake City,** 他回到了盐湖城——

**careless what became of his own life,** [分词-句末伴随] 对什么漠然？→ 全不在乎自己的命运如何——

**as long as he obtained what he knew** 只要他能得到他所认为的正义。
**to be justice.** →

**There he found evil tidings awaiting him.** 在那里，等待他的是噩耗。

---

**There had been a schism among the Chosen** 几个月前，
**People a few months before,** → 选民们中间发生了一次分裂——

**some of the younger members of the Church having rebelled** [分词-独立主格] 具体情况如何？→ 一些教会年轻成员起而反抗——

**against the authority of the Elders,** 反抗什么？→ 长老们的权威——

**and the result had been the secession of** → 其结果是一批不满分子的出走—
**a certain number of the malcontents,** → —

**who had left Utah and become Gentiles.** [定从-句尾补充] 出走的是谁？→ 那些离开犹他、成为异教徒的人。

**Among these had been Drebber and Stangerson;** 其中就有德雷伯和斯坦格森——

**and no one knew whither they had gone.** → 而没有人知道他们去了哪里。

---

**Rumour reported that Drebber had managed to convert** 传言说，
**a large part of his property into money,** → 德雷伯设法将大部分财产变现——

**and that he had departed a wealthy man,** → 并作为一个富人离开了——

**while his companion, Stangerson, was comparatively poor.** → 而他的伙伴斯坦格森则相对贫穷。

**There was no clue at all,** 【转折】然而，关于他们的下落，
**however, as to their whereabouts.** → 却没有任何线索。

---

**Many a man, however vindictive,** 许多人，不管多么怀有复仇之心——

**would have abandoned all thought of revenge** → 在面对这样的困难时都会放弃一切复仇的念头——

**in the face of such a difficulty,** 在这样的困难面前——

**but Jefferson Hope never faltered for a moment.** 【让步·转折·主张落地】但杰弗逊·霍普一刻也未曾动摇。

---

**With the small competence he possessed,** [状语前置] 靠什么？→ 靠着他那点微薄的积蓄——

**eked out by such employment as he could pick up,** [分词-后置修饰] 如何补充？→ 辅以他能找到的零散工作——

**he travelled from town to town through the** 他走遍了美国各地的城镇，
**United States in quest of his enemies.** → 追寻他的仇人。

**Year passed into year,** 年复一年——

**his black hair turned grizzled,** 他的黑发变成了花白——

**but still he wandered on,** 【转折】但他依然继续游荡——

**a human bloodhound,** [同位语] 什么样的游荡者？→ 一个人形猎犬——

**with his mind wholly set upon the one object** [with-描述状态] 心思全在哪里？→ 心思全部凝聚在那一个目标上——

**upon which he had devoted his life.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么目标？→ 他将整个生命都献给的那个目标。

---

**At last his perseverance was rewarded.** 终于，他的坚持得到了回报。

**It was but a glance of a face** 不过是窗户里一张脸的一瞥—
**in a window,** → —

**but that one glance told him** 但那一瞥告诉了他——

**that Cleveland in Ohio possessed the men** 俄亥俄州的克利夫兰市藏着他追寻的那两个人。
**whom he was in pursuit of.** →

**He returned to his miserable lodgings with his** 他回到了他那破败的住所，
**plan of vengeance all arranged.** → 复仇计划已经全部安排妥当。

---

**It chanced, however, that Drebber, looking from his window,** 【转折】然而，碰巧德雷伯从他的窗子朝外望——

**had recognized the vagrant in the street,** 认出了街上的那个流浪者——

**and had read murder in his eyes.** → 并从他眼中读出了杀意。

**He hurried before a justice of the peace,** 他急忙赶去见治安法官——

**accompanied by Stangerson, who had become his private secretary,** [分词-后置修饰] 谁陪同？→ 由已成为他私人秘书的斯坦格森陪同——

**and represented to him** → 向法官表明他们的生命受到威胁—
**that they were in danger of their lives** → —

**from the jealousy and hatred of an old rival.** 来自一个昔日对手的嫉妒和仇恨。

---

**That evening Jefferson Hope was taken into custody,** 当天傍晚，杰弗逊·霍普被捕——

**and not being able to find sureties,** [分词-句中插入] 因为什么被羁押？→ 因为找不到担保人，
**was detained for some weeks.** → 被关押了数周。

**When at last he was liberated,** 当他终于获释时——

**it was only to find that Drebber's house was deserted,** 却发现德雷伯的房子已人去楼空——

**and that he and his secretary had departed for Europe.** → 以及他和他的秘书已经出发去了欧洲。

---

**Again the avenger had been foiled,** 复仇者再一次被挫败了——

**and again his concentrated hatred urged him to** → 而他那集中的仇恨再一次驱使他继续追踪。
**continue the pursuit.** →

**Funds were wanting, however,** 然而，资金告缺——

**and for some time he had to return to work,** → 他不得不重新去工作一段时间——

**saving every dollar for his approaching journey.** [分词-句末伴随] 攒着什么？→ 为即将到来的旅程攒着每一分钱。

---

**At last, having collected enough to keep life in him,** [分词-句首状语] 终于，攒够了维持生计的钱之后——

**he departed for Europe,** 他出发去了欧洲——

**and tracked his enemies from city to city,** → 从一座城市到另一座城市追踪他的仇人——

**working his way in any menial capacity,** [分词-句末伴随] 以什么方式维生？→ 做任何低贱的活计来维持生计——

**but never overtaking the fugitives.** → 却始终追不上那两个在逃之人。

---

**When he reached St. Petersburg they had departed for Paris;** 当他到达圣彼得堡时，他们已经出发去了巴黎——

**and when he followed them there** → 当他追到那里时——

**he learned that they had just set off for Copenhagen.** → 他得知他们刚刚动身去了哥本哈根。

**At the Danish capital he was again a** 在丹麦首都，
**few days late,** → 他又一次晚到了几天——

**for they had journeyed on to London,** 【原因】因为他们已辗转去了伦敦——

**where he at last succeeded in running them to earth.** [定从-句尾补充] 在伦敦怎样？→ 在那里，他终于成功地将他们逼入绝境。

---

**As to what occurred there,** 至于那里发生了什么——

**we cannot do better than quote the old** 我们能做的，
**hunter's own account,** → 莫过于引述那位老猎人自己的陈述——

**as duly recorded in Dr. Watson's Journal,** [分词-后置修饰] 记录在哪里？→ 如实记录在华生医生的日记中——

**to which we are already under such obligations.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么日记？→ 我们已经多亏了的那本日记。

---



---

### 第六章 华生医生回忆录续篇
### CHAPTER VI. A CONTINUATION OF THE REMINISCENCES OF JOHN WATSON, M.D.

---

**Our prisoner's furious resistance** 我们的囚犯那猛烈的抵抗——

**did not apparently indicate any ferocity in his** 表面上并不意味着他对我们怀有任何凶恶之意—
**disposition towards ourselves,** → —

**for on finding himself powerless,** 【原因】因为当他发现自己无力挣脱时——

**he smiled in an affable manner,** → 他以一种和蔼的方式微笑着——

**and expressed his hopes** → 并表示希望——

**that he had not hurt any of us** 他在扭打中没有伤到我们任何人。
**in the scuffle.** →

**"I guess you're going to take me to** "我猜你们是要把我带到警察局，
**the police-station," he remarked to Sherlock Holmes.** → "他对夏洛克·福尔摩斯说道。

**"My cab's at the door.** "我的马车就在门口。

**If you'll loose my legs I'll walk down to it.** 如果你们松开我的腿，我自己走下去。

**I'm not so light to lift** 我可不像从前那么轻了，
**as I used to be."** → 抬起来费劲。"

---

**Gregson and Lestrade exchanged glances** 格雷格森和雷斯垂德交换了个眼神——

**as if they thought this proposition rather a bold one;** 好像觉得这个提议相当大胆——

**but Holmes at once took the prisoner at his word,** 【转折】但福尔摩斯立即信了他的话——

**and loosened the towel** → 解开了我们绑在他脚踝上的毛巾。
**which we had bound round his ankles.** →

**He rose and stretched his legs,** 他站了起来，伸展了一下腿——

**as though to assure himself** →
**that they were free once more.** → 好像在确认它们又能自由活动了。

**I remember that I thought to myself,** 我记得，当我打量他时，
**as I eyed him,** → 我心里想——

**that I had seldom seen a more powerfully built man;** 我很少见过体格如此强健的男人——

**and his dark sunburned face** → 而他那张黝黑、晒得发红的脸——

**bore an expression of determination and energy** → 带着一种坚毅和活力的神情——

**which was as formidable as his personal strength.** 与他的体格一样令人生畏。

---

**"If there's a vacant place** "如果警察局长有空缺的话—
**for a chief of the police,** → —

**I reckon you are the man for it," he said,** 我认为你就是合适的人选，"他说道——

**gazing with undisguised admiration at my fellow-lodger.** [分词-句末伴随] 同时毫不掩饰地钦佩地看着我的同住人。

**"The way you kept on my trail was a caution."** "你追踪我的那种方式，真是让人叹服。"

---

**"You had better come with me," said Holmes** "你们最好跟我来，
**to the two detectives.** → "福尔摩斯对两位侦探说道。

---

**"I can drive you," said Lestrade.** "我来赶车，"雷斯垂德说。

---

**"Good! and Gregson can come inside with me.** "好！格雷格森可以跟我坐里面。

**You too, Doctor,** 你也是，医生——

**you have taken an interest in the case** 你对这个案子感了兴趣，
**and may as well stick to us."** → 不妨跟着我们。"

---

**I assented gladly, and we all descended together.** 我欣然同意，我们一同下楼。

**Our prisoner made no attempt at escape,** 我们的囚犯没有企图逃跑——

**but stepped calmly into the cab which had been his,** 【转折】而是镇定地踏上了原本属于他的那辆马车——

**and we followed him.** → 我们跟了上去。

**Lestrade mounted the box, whipped up the horse,** 雷斯垂德坐上了驾驶座，扬鞭驱马——

**and brought us in a very short time** → 很快就把我们送到了目的地。
**to our destination.** →

---

**We were ushered into a small chamber** 我们被引进一间小屋——

**where a police Inspector noted down our prisoner's name** [定从-句尾补充] 什么小屋？→ 一位警察督察在那里记录下我们囚犯的姓名——

**and the names of the men with** → 以及他被指控谋杀的那些人的姓名。
**whose murder he had been charged.** →

**The official was a white-faced unemotional man,** 那官员是个面色苍白、毫无表情的男人——

**who went through his duties in a dull mechanical way.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的人？→ 以一种枯燥机械的方式履行职责的那种人。

**"The prisoner will be put** "本周内，
**before the magistrates in the course of the** → 犯人将被带上治安法庭，
**week," he said;** → "他说道——

**"in the mean time, Mr. Jefferson Hope,** "在此期间，杰弗逊·霍普先生——

**have you anything that you wish to say?** 你有什么想说的吗？

**I must warn you** 我必须警告你，
**that your words will be taken down,** → 你的话将被记录在案——

**and may be used against you."** → 并可能被用于对你不利。"

---

**"I've got a good deal to say," our** "我有很多话要说，
**prisoner said slowly.** → "我们的囚犯缓缓说道。

**"I want to tell you gentlemen all about it."** "我想把整件事原原本本地告诉你们几位先生。"

---

**"Hadn't you better reserve** "你最好留到审判时再说，
**that for your trial?" asked the Inspector.** → "督察问道。

---

**"I may never be tried," he answered.** "我可能永远等不到审判，"他回答道。

**"You needn't look startled.** "你不必一脸惊愕。

**It isn't suicide I am thinking of.** 我想的不是自杀。

**Are you a Doctor?" He turned his fierce** 你是医生吗？
**dark eyes upon me** → "他说完这最后一句话，
**as he asked this last question.** → 把那双凶狠的黑眼睛转向了我。

---

**"Yes; I am," I answered.** "是的，我是，"我回答道。

---

**"Then put your hand here," he said, with a smile,** "那就把你的手放在这里，"他带着微笑说道——

**motioning with his manacled wrists towards his chest.** [分词-句末伴随] 同时怎样示意？→ 用他那戴着手铐的双腕朝他的胸口示意。

---

**I did so;** 我照做了——

**and became at once conscious of an extraordinary** → 立刻感觉到一种异常的跳动和震动—
**throbbing and commotion** → —

**which was going on inside.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的跳动？→ 在他胸腔里搏动着的那种。

**The walls of his chest seemed to thrill and quiver** 他的胸腔壁似乎在颤动和抖动——

**as a frail building would do inside** 像什么？→ 就像一栋脆弱的建筑内部——

**when some powerful engine was at work.** 当某台强力机器运转时那样。

**In the silence of the room I could** 在屋子的寂静中，
**hear a dull humming and buzzing noise** → 我能听见一种沉闷的嗡嗡声——

**which proceeded from the same source.** [定从-句尾补充] 从哪里来的？→ 从同一个地方传出的。

---

**"Why," I cried, "you have an aortic aneurism!"** "天哪，"我失声道，"你有主动脉瘤！"

---

**"That's what they call it," he said, placidly.** "他们就是这么叫的，"他平静地说。

**"I went to a doctor last week about it,** "上周我去看了医生——

**and he told me** 他告诉我，
**that it is bound to burst** → 它不用多少天就必然会破裂。
**before many days passed.** →

**It has been getting worse for years.** 这病已经恶化好几年了。

**I got it from over-exposure** 我是在盐湖山脉里风餐露宿、
**and under-feeding among the Salt Lake Mountains.** → 忍饥挨饿落下的病根。

**I've done my work now,** 我现在已经完成了我的使命——

**and I don't care how soon I go,** → 我不在乎什么时候走——

**but I should like to leave some account** 【转折】但我希望能留下一些对这件事的说明。
**of the business behind me.** →

**I don't want to be remembered as a common cut-throat."** 我不想被人记住是个普通的杀手。"

---

**The Inspector and the two detectives had a hurried discussion** 督察和两位侦探匆忙地商量了一番——

**as to the advisability of allowing him to** 关于是否应该让他讲述他的故事。
**tell his story.** →

---

**"Do you consider,** "医生，你认为有即时的危险吗？
**Doctor, that there is immediate danger?" the former asked.** → "前者问道。

---

**"Most certainly there is," I answered.** "当然有，"我回答道。

---

**"In that case it is clearly our duty,** "既然如此，为了维护正义，
**in the interests of justice,** → 我们显然有责任——

**to take his statement," said the Inspector.** 听取他的陈述，"督察说道。

**"You are at liberty, sir, to give your account,** "先生，你可以自由地陈述你的情况——

**which I again warn you will be taken down."** 我再次警告你，这将被记录在案。"

---

**"I'll sit down,** "承蒙允许，
**with your leave," the prisoner said,** → 我坐下来说，
**suiting the action to the word.** → "犯人边说边坐了下来。

**"This aneurism of mine makes me easily tired,** "我这个动脉瘤让我很容易疲劳——

**and the tussle we had half an hour** → 而且半小时前那番搏斗也没让情况好转。
**ago has not mended matters.** →

**I'm on the brink of the grave,** 我已经站在坟墓边缘了——

**and I am not likely to lie to you.** → 不太可能向你们撒谎。

**Every word I say is the absolute truth,** 我说的每一个字都是绝对的真相——

**and how you use it is a matter** → 至于你们怎么利用它，
**of no consequence to me."** → 我无所谓。"

---

**With these words, Jefferson Hope leaned back in his chair** 说完这些话，杰弗逊·霍普靠在椅背上——

**and began the following remarkable statement.** → 开始了以下这段非凡的陈述。

**He spoke in a calm and methodical manner,** 他说话冷静而有条理——

**as though the events which he narrated were commonplace enough.** 好像他所讲述的那些事件再普通不过一样。

**I can vouch for the accuracy of the subjoined account,** 我可以为下面这段陈述的准确性作担保——

**for I have had access to Lestrade's note-book,** 【原因】因为我获得了雷斯垂德的笔记本——

**in which the prisoner's words were taken down** [定从-句中插入] 什么笔记本？
**exactly as they were uttered.** → 犯人的话一字不差地被记录在其中的那本笔记本。

---

**"It don't much matter to you why I** "我为什么恨这两个人，
**hated these men," he said;** → 对你们来说无关紧要，"他说——

**"it's enough that they were guilty of the** "只需知道，
**death of two human beings** → 他们对两条人命负有罪责——

**—a father and a daughter—** [同位语] 是谁？→ 一对父女——

**and that they had, therefore, forfeited their own lives.** → 因此，他们也已经失去了自己的生命权利。

**After the lapse of time** →
**that has passed since their crime,** → —

**it was impossible** →
**for me to secure a conviction against them** → 在他们犯罪之后这么多年过去之后—
**in any court.** → 我不可能在任何法庭上获得对他们的定罪。

**I knew of their guilt though,** 然而，我知道他们的罪行——

**and I determined** → 我决定，我要集法官、
**that I should be judge,** → 陪审团、
**jury, and executioner all rolled into one.** → 执行人于一身。

**You'd have done the same,** 你们也会这么做的，
**if you have any manhood in you,** → 如果你们身为男人的话——

**if you had been in my place.** 如果你们处于我的位置。

---

**"That girl that I spoke of** "我说的那个女孩——

**was to have married me twenty years ago.** 本该在二十年前嫁给我。

**She was forced into marrying that same Drebber,** 她被逼着嫁给了那个德雷伯——

**and broke her heart over it.** → 并为此心碎而死。

**I took the marriage ring from her dead finger,** 我从她死去的手指上取下了婚戒——

**and I vowed** → 我发誓，
**that his dying eyes should rest upon that very ring,** → 他临死时的眼睛要看到那枚戒指——

**and that his last thoughts should be of** → 他最后的念头要是那桩让他受到惩罚的罪行。
**the crime for** →
**which he was punished.** →

**I have carried it about with me,** 我一直随身带着它——

**and have followed him and his accomplice over two continents** → 追踪他和他的同谋穿越了两个大洲——

**until I caught them.** 直到我抓住了他们。

**They thought to tire me out,** 他们以为能把我拖垮——

**but they could not do it.** 【转折】但他们做不到。

**If I die to-morrow, as is likely enough,** 【条件·心悬着】如果我明天就死，这很有可能——【等"那我也……"】

**I die knowing** 【结果落地】我死时知道，
**that my work in this world is done,** → 我在这个世上的使命已经完成，
**and well done.** → 而且完成得很好。

**They have perished, and by my hand.** 他们已经死了，死在我的手上。

**There is nothing left** 我已经没有什么可期待的，
**for me to hope for,** → 也没有什么可渴望的了。
**or to desire.** →

---

**"They were rich and I was poor,** "他们富有，我贫穷——

**so that it was no easy matter** 【结果】所以追踪他们对我来说并不容易。
**for me to follow them.** →

**When I got to London my pocket was about empty,** 当我到了伦敦，我的口袋几乎空了——

**and I found** → 我发现我必须找点什么活计维持生计。
**that I must turn my hand to something** →
**for my living.** →

**Driving and riding are as natural to me as walking,** 赶车和骑马对我来说就像走路一样自然——

**so I applied at a cabowner's office,** 【结果】所以我去了一家马车行求职，
**and soon got employment.** → 很快就找到了活儿。

**I was to bring a certain sum a** 我每周要交给老板一定数额的钱—
**week to the owner,** → —

**and whatever was over that I might keep for myself.** → 超出部分就归我自己。

**There was seldom much over,** 超出的部分很少——

**but I managed to scrape along somehow.** 【转折】但我还是勉强维持下来了。

**The hardest job was to learn my way about,** 最难的事是摸清这座城市的路——

**for I reckon** 【原因】因为我认为，
**that of all the mazes** → 在人类设计过的所有迷宫中—
**that ever were contrived,** → —

**this city is the most confusing.** 这座城市是最令人迷惑的。

**I had a map beside me though,** 不过我随身带着地图——

**and when once I had spotted the principal** 等我一旦找准了主要的旅馆和车站—
**hotels and stations,** → —

**I got on pretty well.** → 就大致摸清了门道。

---

**"It was some time** →
**before I found out** → —
**where my two gentlemen were living;** → "过了一段时间我才找到那两位先生住在哪里—

**but I inquired** → 但我一路打听，打听，
**and inquired until at last I dropped across them.** → 终于偶然碰上了他们。

**They were at a boarding-house at Camberwell,** 他们住在河对岸坎伯韦尔的一家寄宿公寓里。
**over on the other side of the river.** →

**When once I found them out** 一旦我找到了他们——

**I knew that I had them at my mercy.** → 我就知道他们已在我的掌握之中。

**I had grown my beard,** 我留了胡须——

**and there was no chance of their recognizing me.** → 他们认出我的可能性为零。

**I would dog them and follow them** 我会紧跟着他们、追踪他们——

**until I saw my opportunity.** 直到我看准了机会。

**I was determined that they should not escape me again.** 我下定决心，他们不会再次逃脱。

---

**"They were very near doing it for all that.** "尽管如此，他们差点就逃脱了。

**Go where they would about London,** 不管他们在伦敦去哪里——

**I was always at their heels.** → 我总是如影随形。

**Sometimes I followed them on my cab,** 有时我驾着马车跟踪他们——

**and sometimes on foot,** → 有时步行跟踪——

**but the former was the best,** 【转折】但前者更好——

**for then they could not get away from me.** 【原因】因为那样他们就无法甩掉我。

**It was only early in the morning** 只有在清晨或深夜，
**or late at night** → 我才能赚到钱——
**that I could earn anything,** →

**so that I began to get behindhand with my employer.** 【结果】所以我开始拖欠老板的钱。

**I did not mind that, however,** 【让步·转折】然而我不在乎这个——

**as long as I could lay my hand** 只要我能抓住我要找的那两个人。
**upon the men I wanted.** →

---

**"They were very cunning, though.** "不过他们非常狡猾。

**They must have thought** →
**that there was some chance of their being followed,** → 他们一定认为被人跟踪是有可能的—

**for they would never go out alone,** 【原因】因为他们从不单独外出，
**and never after nightfall.** → 也从不在夜幕降临后出门。

**During two weeks I drove behind them every day,** 两周来，我每天都跟在他们后面——

**and never once saw them separate.** → 却从未见过他们分开。

**Drebber himself was drunk half the time,** 德雷伯本人有一半时间都在喝醉——

**but Stangerson was not to be caught napping.** 【转折】但斯坦格森可从不打盹。

**I watched them late and early,** 我从早到晚地盯着他们——

**but never saw the ghost of a chance;** → 却始终没看到任何机会的影子——

**but I was not discouraged,** 【转折】但我并不气馁——

**for something told me that the hour had almost come.** 【原因】因为有什么东西告诉我，时机快到了。

**My only fear was** 我唯一的担忧是——

**that this thing in my chest might burst** 我胸腔里这个东西可能会破裂得稍微早了一点—
**a little too soon** → —

**and leave my work undone.** → 从而让我的使命无法完成。

---

**"At last, one evening I was driving up** "终于，一天傍晚，
**and down Torquay Terrace,** → 我在托基台地附近来回驾车——

**as the street was called in which they boarded,** [插入说明] 那条街是什么？→ 也就是他们住宿的那条街——

**when I saw a cab drive up to their door.** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，我看见一辆马车驶到他们门口。

**Presently some luggage was brought out,** 不一会儿，有人把行李搬了出来——

**and after a time Drebber** → 过了一阵，
**and Stangerson followed it,** → 德雷伯和斯坦格森也跟了出来，
**and drove off.** → 坐车离开了。

**I whipped up my horse** 我扬鞭催马，
**and kept within sight of them,** → 一直跟在他们视野范围内——

**feeling very ill at ease,** [分词-句末伴随] 内心感受如何？→ 感到非常不安——

**for I feared** 【原因】因为我担心他们要换地方住了。
**that they were going to shift their quarters.** →

---

**At Euston Station they got out,** 在尤斯顿车站，他们下了车——

**and I left a boy to hold my horse,** → 我把马交给一个男孩看管——

**and followed them on to the platform.** → 跟他们上了站台。

**I heard them ask for the Liverpool train,** 我听见他们问利物浦方向的火车——

**and the guard answer that one had just gone** → 而乘务员回答说刚刚走了一班——

**and there would not be another for some hours.** → 几个小时内不会再有了。

**Stangerson seemed to be put out at that,** 斯坦格森对此似乎颇为不满——

**but Drebber was rather pleased than otherwise.** 【转折】但德雷伯反倒有几分高兴。

---

**I got so close to them in the bustle** 我在人群的嘈杂中靠得很近——

**that I could hear every word that passed between them.** 以至于我能听到他们之间说的每一个字。

**Drebber said that he had a little business** 德雷伯说他有点私事要处理—
**of his own to do,** → —

**and that if the other would wait for him** → 如果对方愿意等他——

**he would soon rejoin him.** → 他很快就回来。

**His companion remonstrated with him,** 他的同伴劝阻了他——

**and reminded him that they had resolved to stick together.** → 提醒他们已经决定要一起行动。

**Drebber answered that the matter was a delicate one,** 德雷伯回答说这件事很敏感——

**and that he must go alone.** → 他必须独自去。

**I could not catch what Stangerson said to that,** 我没听清斯坦格森对此说了什么——

**but the other burst out swearing,** 【转折】但另一个突然破口大骂起来——

**and reminded him** → 提醒他不过是他的雇佣仆人—
**that he was nothing more than his paid servant,** → —

**and that he must not presume to dictate to him.** → 不该妄想对他发号施令。

---

**On that the Secretary gave it up** 于是那秘书就放弃了这件没有指望的事—
**as a bad job,** → —

**and simply bargained with him** → 只是与他商议——

**that if he missed the last train** 【条件·心悬着】如果他错过了最后一班火车——【等"那就……"】

**he should rejoin him at Halliday's Private Hotel;** 【结果落地】他就去哈利戴私人旅馆找他——

**to which Drebber answered** → 对此德雷伯回答说——

**that he would be back on the platform before eleven,** 他会在十一点前回到站台——

**and made his way out of the station.** → 然后走出了车站。

---

**"The moment for** "我等待已久的时机终于来了。
**which I had waited** →
**so long had at last come.** →

**I had my enemies within my power.** 我的仇人已经在我的掌握之中。

**Together they could protect each other,** 在一起时他们可以互相保护——

**but singly they were at my mercy.** 【转折】但单独行动时，他们任我处置。

**I did not act, however, with undue precipitation.** 然而，我没有轻举妄动。

**My plans were already formed.** 我的计划早已制定好了。

---

**There is no satisfaction in vengeance** 复仇没有任何满足感——

**unless the offender has time to realize** 除非冒犯者有时间意识到——

**who it is that strikes him,** 是谁在惩罚他——

**and why retribution has come upon him.** → 以及为什么报应降临到他身上。

**I had my plans arranged** 我安排好了我的计划——

**by which I should have the opportunity** 通过这些计划，我应该能有机会——

**of making the man who had wronged me understand** 让那个曾经伤害我的人明白——

**that his old sin had found him out.** 他昔日的罪孽已经找上了门。

---

**It chanced that some days before** 碰巧几天前——

**a gentleman who had been engaged in looking** 一位在布里克斯顿路看房的绅士—
**over some houses in the Brixton Road** → —

**had dropped the key of one of them** 把其中一所房子的钥匙遗落在了我的马车里。
**in my carriage.** →

**It was claimed that same evening, and returned;** 当天傍晚就有人来认领了，钥匙也还了回去——

**but in the interval I had taken a** 【转折】但在那段时间里，
**moulding of it,** → 我已经翻了个模——

**and had a duplicate constructed.** → 并配了一把复制钥匙。

**By means of this I had access to** 凭借这把钥匙，
**at least one spot in this great city** → 我在这座大城市里至少有一个地方——

**where I could rely upon being free from interruption.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的地方？→ 我可以确信不会受到打扰的地方。

**How to get Drebber to that house** 如何把德雷伯引到那所房子——

**was the difficult problem which I had now to solve.** 是我现在需要解决的难题。

---

**"He walked down the road** "他沿街走去，
**and went into one** → 进了一两家酒馆—
**or two liquor shops,** → —

**staying for nearly half-an-hour in the last of them.** 在最后一家待了将近半小时。

**When he came out he staggered in his walk,** 当他出来时，他走路踉踉跄跄——

**and was evidently pretty well on.** → 显然已经喝得七七八八了。

**There was a hansom just in front of me,** 我前面正好有一辆出租马车——

**and he hailed it.** → 他招手叫了它。

**I followed it so close** 我跟得如此之近——

**that the nose of my horse was within** 以至于我的马鼻子全程都离那辆车的车夫不到一码。
**a yard of his driver the whole way.** →

**We rattled across Waterloo Bridge and through miles of streets,** 我们轰隆隆地越过滑铁卢桥，穿过数英里的街道——

**until, to my astonishment,** 直到，令我吃惊的是，
**we found ourselves back in the Terrace** → 我们发现自己又回到了那条台地街道——

**in which he had boarded.** [定从-句尾补充] 哪条街道？→ 他住宿的那条街道。

**I could not imagine what his intention was** 我想不透他回来的目的—
**in returning there;** → —

**but I went on** 但我继续跟着，
**and pulled up my cab a hundred yards** → 把我的马车停在那所房子百码左右远的地方。
**or so from the house.** →

**He entered it, and his hansom drove away.** 他进了屋，那辆出租马车离去了。

**Give me a glass of water, if you please.** 请给我一杯水。

**My mouth gets dry with the talking."** 说话说得我口渴了。"

---

**I handed him the glass, and he drank it down.** 我递给他那杯水，他一饮而尽。

---

**"That's better," he said.** "好多了，"他说。

**"Well, I waited** "好，我等了一刻钟，
**for a quarter of an hour, or more,** → 或者更久——

**when suddenly there came a noise like people** 突然，
**struggling inside the house.** → 屋子里传来一阵像是人在扭打的声音。

**Next moment the door was flung open** 下一刻，门被猛地打开，
**and two men appeared,** → 两个男人出现了——

**one of whom was Drebber,** 其中一个是德雷伯——

**and the other was a young chap** → 另一个是一个我从未见过的年轻小伙。
**whom I had never seen before.** →

**This fellow had Drebber by the collar,** 这个小伙揪着德雷伯的衣领——

**and when they came to the head of the steps** → 等他们走到台阶顶端——

**he gave him a shove and a kick** → 他猛地推了他一把，再踢了一脚——

**which sent him half across the road.** → 把他送出了半条街。

**'You hound,' he cried, shaking his stick at him;** '你这条狗，'他挥着手杖朝他喊道——

**'I'll teach you to insult an honest girl!'** '我来教教你怎么对一个正派女孩的！'

**He was so hot** 他是如此愤怒——

**that I think he would have thrashed Drebber** 我想他会用棍子揍德雷伯的—
**with his cudgel,** → —

**only that the cur staggered away down the** 只是那条狗以双腿所能承受的最快速度踉跄着跑下了街道。
**road as fast** →
**as his legs would carry him.** →

**He ran as far as the corner,** 他跑到了街角——

**and then, seeing my cab,** → 然后，看见我的马车，
**he hailed me and jumped in.** → 他招手叫住我，跳了进去。

**'Drive me to Halliday's Private Hotel,' said he.** '送我去哈利戴私人旅馆，'他说道。

---

**"When I had him fairly inside my cab,** "当他稳稳地坐进我的马车——

**my heart jumped so with joy** 我的心因为喜悦而猛地一跳——

**that I feared lest at this last moment** 以至于我担心就在这最后关头，
**my aneurism might go wrong.** → 我的动脉瘤会出问题。

**I drove along slowly,** 我慢慢地驾车——

**weighing in my own mind what it was** [分词-句末伴随] 心里在想什么？
**best to do.** → 在心中权衡着最好的做法。

**I might take him right out into the country,** 我可以把他一直带到乡下——

**and there in some deserted lane have my** → 在某条荒僻的小道上与他进行最后的对话。
**last interview with him.** →

**I had almost decided upon this,** 我几乎已经决定这么做了——

**when he solved the problem for me.** 【情境·转折·when】就在这时，他替我解决了这个问题。

**The craze for drink had seized him again,** 对酒的渴望再次抓住了他——

**and he ordered me to pull up outside** → 他命令我停在一家杜松子酒馆门外。
**a gin palace.** →

**He went in,** 他进去了，
**leaving word that I should wait for him.** → 留话让我等他。

**There he remained until closing time,** 他在里面待到打烊——

**and when he came out** → 当他出来时——

**he was so far gone** 他已经烂醉如泥——

**that I knew the game was in my own hands.** → 我知道，局势已经完全掌握在我手中了。

---

**"Don't imagine that I intended to kill him** "不要以为我打算冷血地杀死他。
**in cold blood.** →

**It would only have been rigid justice** 即便那样做也不过是严格意义上的正义—
**if I had done so,** → —

**but I could not bring myself to do it.** 【让步·转折·主张落地】但我无法下得了那个手。

**I had long determined** 我早就决定，
**that he should have a show for his life** → 他应该有一次为自己的命运搏一搏的机会——

**if he chose to take advantage of it.** 如果他选择利用这个机会的话。

---

**Among the many billets** →
**which I have filled in America during my wandering life,** → —

**I was once janitor** → 在我漂泊生涯中在美国做过的许多工作里—
**and sweeper out of the laboratory at York College.** → 我曾经在约克学院做过实验室的看门人和清洁工。

**One day the professor was lecturing on poisons,** 有一天，教授在讲授毒物——

**and he showed his students some alkaloid,** 他向学生们展示了一种生物碱，
**as he called it,** → 他是这么叫的——

**which he had extracted from some South American arrow poison,** [定从-句中插入] 什么生物碱？→ 从某种南美箭毒中提取的——

**and which was** → 强效到连最微量都意味着即刻死亡的那种。
**so powerful that the least grain meant instant death.** →

**I spotted the bottle in which this preparation was kept,** 我找准了装这种制剂的瓶子——

**and when they were all gone,** 等所有人都离开后，
**I helped myself to a little of it.** → 我取了一点儿。

---

**I was a fairly good dispenser,** 我是个相当不错的配药师——

**so I worked this alkaloid into small, soluble pills,** 【结果】所以我把这种生物碱做成了小而易溶的药片——

**and each pill I put in a box** 每颗毒药片，我都配上一颗同样外观但不含毒的药片，
**with a similar pill made without the poison.** → 放在一个盒子里。

**I determined at the time** 我当时就决定——

**that when I had my chance,** 等我有机会时——

**my gentlemen should each have a draw out** 我的那两位先生各自从其中一个盒子里取一颗—
**of one of these boxes,** → —

**while I ate the pill that remained.** 而我吃掉剩下那颗。

**It would be quite** 这会同样致命，
**as deadly, and a good deal less noisy** → 而且安静得多——

**than firing across a handkerchief.** 比隔着手帕开枪要安静得多。

**From that day I had always my pill** 从那天起，
**boxes about with me,** → 我一直随身带着那些药盒——

**and the time had now come** 现在，
**when I was to use them.** → 该用它们的时候到了。

---

**"It was nearer one than twelve,** "时间接近凌晨一点而非十二点——

**and a wild, bleak night,** 是一个狂野、凄寒的夜晚——

**blowing hard and raining in torrents.** [分词-后置修饰] 天气怎样？→ 狂风大作，暴雨倾盆。

**Dismal as it was outside,** 【让步·心悬着】尽管外面如此阴沉——

**I was glad within** 【主张落地】我内心却是欢喜的——

**—so glad that I could have shouted out** 如此欢喜，
**from pure exultation.** → 以至于我几乎要因为纯粹的欢欣而大喊出来。

**If any of you gentlemen have ever pined** 【条件·心悬着】如果你们之中有谁曾渴望过一件事—
**for a thing,** → —

**and longed for it during twenty long years,** → 并且渴望了整整二十年——

**and then suddenly found it within your reach,** → 然后突然发现它触手可及——

**you would understand my feelings.** 【结果落地】你就会明白我的感受。

---

**I lit a cigar,** 我点了一根雪茄，猛吸几口，
**and puffed at it to steady my nerves,** → 试图平稳神经——

**but my hands were trembling,** 但我的双手在颤抖，
**and my temples throbbing with excitement.** → 太阳穴因激动而砰砰跳。

**As I drove,** 驾车时，
**I could see old John Ferrier and sweet Lucy** → 我仿佛看见了老约翰·费瑞尔和温柔的露西——

**looking at me out of the darkness** → 从黑暗中望着我，
**and smiling at me,** → 对我微笑——

**just as plain** →
**as I see you all in this room.** → 就像我现在清清楚楚地看见你们所有人一样真实。

**All the way they were ahead of me,** 一路上，他们都在我前方——

**one on each side of the horse** 一人在马的一侧——

**until I pulled up at the house in** 直到我把车停在布里克斯顿路那所房子前。
**the Brixton Road.** →

---

**"There was not a soul to be seen,** "看不到一个人影，
**nor a sound to be heard,** → 也听不到任何声音——

**except the dripping of the rain.** 除了雨水滴落的声音。

**When I looked in at the window,** 当我从窗子朝里看——

**I found Drebber all huddled together in a drunken sleep.** 我发现德雷伯蜷缩成一团，烂醉酣睡。

**I shook him by the arm,** 我摇了摇他的手臂，
**'It's time to get out,' I said.** → '该下车了，'我说。

---

**"'All right, cabby,' said he.** "'好的，车夫，'他说道。

---

**"I suppose he thought we had come to** "我想他以为我们到了他说的那家旅馆—
**the hotel that he had mentioned,** → —

**for he got out without another word,** 因为他一句话没说就下车了——

**and followed me down the garden.** → 跟着我走进了花园。

**I had to walk beside him to keep him steady,** 我不得不走在他身边扶稳他——

**for he was still a little top-heavy.** 【原因】因为他还有几分醉意，身子不稳。

**When we came to the door, I opened it,** 当我们走到门口，我把门打开——

**and led him into the front room.** → 把他引进了前厅。

**I give you my word** 我向你们保证——

**that all the way,** 整个途中，
**the father and the daughter were walking in** → 那对父女一直走在我们前面。
**front of us.** →

---

**"'It's infernally dark,' said he, stamping about.** "'这里他妈的真黑，'他跺着脚说道。

---

**"'We'll soon have a light,' I said,** "'很快就有光亮了，'我说——

**striking a match** [分词-后置修饰] 怎么有光亮？→ 划着火柴，
**and putting it to a wax candle** → 点燃了我随身带来的一根蜡烛。
**which I had brought with me.** →

**'Now, Enoch Drebber,' I continued,** '现在，伊诺克·德雷伯，'我继续说道——

**turning to him,** [分词-句末伴随] → 转向他，
**and holding the light to my own face,** → 把灯光打在自己脸上——

**'who am I?'** '我是谁？'

---

**"He gazed at me with bleared,** "他用那双朦胧醉眼盯了我片刻—
**drunken eyes for a moment,** → —

**and then I saw a horror spring up in them,** → 然后我看见恐惧在他眼中骤然升起——

**and convulse his whole features,** → 使他整张脸都扭曲起来——

**which showed me that he knew me.** [定从-句尾补充] 说明了什么？→ 说明他认出了我。

**He staggered back with a livid face,** 他面色铁青地向后踉跄——

**and I saw the perspiration break out upon his brow,** → 我看见汗珠从他额头上渗出——

**while his teeth chattered in his head.** → 而他的牙关咯咯作响。

---

**At the sight,** 看到这一幕，
**I leaned my back against the door** → 我靠在门上，放声大笑，
**and laughed loud and long.** → 笑了很久。

**I had always known that vengeance would be sweet,** 我一直知道复仇是甜蜜的——

**but I had never hoped for the contentment of soul** 【转折】但我从未奢望过那种灵魂的满足——

**which now possessed me.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的满足？→ 此刻占据着我的那种满足。

---

**"'You dog!' I said;** "'你这条狗！'我说道——

**'I have hunted you from Salt Lake City** '我从盐湖城追到了圣彼得堡—
**to St. Petersburg,** → —

**and you have always escaped me.** 而你总是从我手中逃脱。

**Now, at last your wanderings have come to an end,** 现在，你的流亡终于走到了尽头——

**for either you** 因为你我之中，
**or I shall never see to-morrow's sun rise.'** → 有一个人明天看不到日出了。'

**He shrunk still further away as I spoke,** 我说话时，他越缩越远——

**and I could see on his face** → 我从他脸上看出，
**that he thought I was mad.** → 他以为我疯了。

**So I was for the time.** 那时候，我确实疯了。

**The pulses in my temples beat like sledge-hammers,** 太阳穴里的脉搏跳得像铁锤——

**and I believe I would have had a** → 我想我本来会有某种发作—
**fit of some sort** → —

**if the blood had not gushed from my** 要不是鼻血涌出，
**nose and relieved me.** → 为我缓解了压力。

---

**"'What do you think of Lucy Ferrier now?' I cried,** "'你现在怎么看待露西·费瑞尔？'我大声说道——

**locking the door, and shaking the key in his face.** [分词-句末伴随] 同时怎样？→ 锁上门，把钥匙在他脸前晃动。

**'Punishment has been slow in coming,** '惩罚来得很慢——

**but it has overtaken you at last.'** 但它终究追上了你。'

**I saw his coward lips tremble as I spoke.** 我说话时，看见他那懦弱的嘴唇在颤抖。

**He would have begged for his life,** 他本想求我饶命——

**but he knew well that it was useless.** 但他心里清楚，那是没有用的。

---

**"'Would you murder me?' he stammered.** "'你要杀我吗？'他结结巴巴地说。

---

**"'There is no murder,' I answered.** "'这不是谋杀，'我回答。

**'Who talks of murdering a mad dog?** '谁会说杀一条疯狗叫谋杀？

**What mercy had you upon my poor darling,** 你对我可怜的心上人有什么怜悯——

**when you dragged her from her slaughtered father,** 当你把她从被杀害的父亲身边拖走——

**and bore her away to your accursed and shameless harem.'** 带她进你那该死的、无耻的后宫的时候。'

---

**"'It was not I who killed her father,' he cried.** "'杀她父亲的不是我，'他叫道。

---

**"'But it was you** "'但是你伤透了她那颗纯洁的心，
**who broke her innocent heart,' I shrieked,** → '我尖声叫道——

**thrusting the box before him.** [分词-句末伴随] → 同时把那个盒子推到他面前。

**'Let the high God judge between us.** '让至高的上帝来评判我们。

**Choose and eat.** 选一颗，吃下去。

**There is death in one and life in the other.** 其中一颗是死，另一颗是生。

**I shall take what you leave.** 你留下的，我来吃。

**Let us see if there is justice upon the earth,** 让我们看看地球上是否存在正义——

**or if we are ruled by chance.'** 还是我们都受命运的摆布。'

---

**"He cowered away with wild cries and prayers for mercy,** "他一边惊叫一边苦苦哀求——

**but I drew my knife** 但我抽出刀，
**and held it to his throat** → 顶住他的喉咙——

**until he had obeyed me.** 直到他服从了我。

**Then I swallowed the other,** 然后我吞下了另一颗——

**and we stood facing one another in silence** → 我们沉默地面对面站着，
**for a minute or more,** → 一分钟，或者更久——

**waiting to see** 等待着，
**which was to live** → 看谁生，
**and which was to die.** → 谁死。

---

**Shall I ever forget the look** 我怎么能忘记他脸上浮现的那个表情—
**which came over his face** → —

**when the first warning pangs told him** 当第一阵预兆的剧痛告诉他，
**that the poison was in his system?** → 毒药已经进入他体内的时候？

**I laughed as I saw it,** 我看见时，大笑起来——

**and held Lucy's marriage ring in front of his eyes.** → 并把露西的婚戒举到他眼前。

**It was but for a moment,** 只是一瞬间——

**for the action of the alkaloid is rapid.** 因为生物碱的作用很迅速。

**A spasm of pain contorted his features;** 一阵痛苦的痉挛扭曲了他的面孔——

**he threw his hands out in front of him,** → 他把双手向前一伸——

**staggered, and then,** → 踉跄了一下，然后，
**with a hoarse cry,** → 发出一声沙哑的叫声，
**fell heavily upon the floor.** → 沉沉地倒在了地板上。

**I turned him over with my foot,** 我用脚把他翻了过来——

**and placed my hand upon his heart.** → 把手放在他的心口。

**There was no movement. He was dead!** 没有任何跳动。他死了！

---

**"The blood had been streaming from my nose,** "血一直从我的鼻子里流出来——

**but I had taken no notice of it.** 但我没有在意。

**I don't know what it was** 我不知道是什么让我想到—
**that put it into my head** → —

**to write upon the wall with it.** 用它在墙上写字。

**Perhaps it was some mischievous idea of setting** 也许是某种恶作剧的念头，
**the police upon a wrong track,** → 想把警察引上歪路——

**for I felt light-hearted and cheerful.** 因为我感到轻松愉快。

**I remembered a German being found in New** 我想起一个德国人在纽约被发现时，
**York with RACHE written up above him,** → 头顶上方写着"RACHE"——

**and it was argued at the time in the newspapers** → 当时报纸上有人论述说——

**that the secret societies must have done it.** 一定是秘密社团干的。

**I guessed that what puzzled the New Yorkers** 我猜想，让纽约人费解的东西，
**would puzzle the Londoners,** → 也会让伦敦人费解——

**so I dipped my finger in my own blood** 【结果】所以我把手指蘸进自己的血里——

**and printed it on a convenient place on the wall.** → 在墙上一个合适的地方印上了那个字。

---

**Then I walked down to my cab** 然后我走回到我的马车——

**and found that there was nobody about,** → 发现四下无人——

**and that the night was still very wild.** → 夜色依然狂野。

**I had driven some distance** 我驾车走了一段路——

**when I put my hand into the pocket** 当我把手伸进口袋——

**in which I usually kept Lucy's ring,** [定从-句中插入] 哪个口袋？→ 我通常放露西戒指的那个口袋——

**and found that it was not there.** ← 回来接 → 发现戒指不在里面了。

---

**I was thunderstruck at this,** 我为此大惊失色——

**for it was the only memento** 【原因】因为那是我唯一留有的关于她的纪念物。
**that I had of her.** →

**Thinking that I might have dropped it** 心想也许是我在——

**when I stooped over Drebber's body,** 俯身查看德雷伯的尸体时——

**I drove back,** 把它掉落了，我驾车返回——

**and leaving my cab in a side street,** [分词-句末伴随] → 把马车停在一条小巷里——

**I went boldly up to the house** → 大胆地走向那所房子——

**—for I was ready to dare anything rather** 因为为了不失去那枚戒指，
**than lose the ring.** → 我什么都愿意冒险。

**When I arrived there,** 当我到达时——

**I walked right into the arms of a** 我正好撞进了一个正在出来的警察的怀里—
**police-officer who was coming out,** → —

**and only managed to disarm his suspicions** → 而且只能靠——

**by pretending to be hopelessly drunk.** 假装烂醉如泥来打消他的怀疑。

---

**"That was how Enoch Drebber came to his end.** "这就是伊诺克·德雷伯走到末路的经过。

**All I had to do then was to** 我接下来要做的，
**do as much for Stangerson,** → 就是对斯坦格森如法炮制——

**and so pay off John Ferrier's debt.** → 以此偿还约翰·费瑞尔的债。

**I knew that he was staying at Halliday's Private Hotel,** 我知道他住在哈利戴私人旅馆——

**and I hung about all day,** → 我在那里徘徊了一整天——

**but he never came out.** 但他始终没有出来。

**I fancy that he suspected something** 我猜他有所察觉——

**when Drebber failed to put in an appearance.** 当德雷伯未能现身的时候。

---

**He was cunning, was Stangerson, and always on his guard.** 斯坦格森狡猾，而且始终保持警惕。

**If he thought he could keep me off** 【条件·心悬着】如果他以为待在室内就能挡住我—
**by staying indoors** → —【等"他就大错特错了"】

**he was very much mistaken.** 【结果落地】他大错特错了。

**I soon found out** →
**which was the window of his bedroom,** → 我很快就查明了他卧室的窗户在哪里—

**and early next morning** → 第二天一早——

**I took advantage of some ladders** 我利用旅馆后巷里搭着的几架梯子—
**which were lying in the lane behind the hotel,** → —

**and so made my way into his room** → 就这样在黎明的薄暮中潜进了他的房间。
**in the grey of the dawn.** →

**I woke him up** 我叫醒他，
**and told him** → 告诉他时候到了—
**that the hour had come** → —

**when he was to answer** →
**for the life he had taken so long before.** → 他要为多年前夺走的那条人命付出代价了。

**I described Drebber's death to him,** 我向他描述了德雷伯的死——

**and I gave him the same choice of** → 并给了他同样的毒药选择。
**the poisoned pills.** →

**Instead of grasping at the chance of safety** 然而他没有抓住那给他的一线生机—
**which that offered him,** → —

**he sprang from his bed and flew at my throat.** → 而是从床上跳起，扑向我的喉咙。

**In self-defence I stabbed him to the heart.** 出于自卫，我刺穿了他的心脏。

**It would have been the same in any case,** 不管怎样，结果都是一样的——

**for Providence would never have allowed his guilty** 因为上天绝不会允许他那有罪的手选到除毒药之外的任何东西。
**hand to pick out anything but the poison.** →

---

**"I have little more to say, and it's as well,** "我没有太多要说的了，这也好——

**for I am about done up.** 因为我已经筋疲力尽。

**I went on cabbing it for a day or so,** 我又赶了一天左右的马车——

**intending to keep at it until I could save enough** 打算继续干下去，直到攒够钱——

**to take me back to America.** 够我回美国。

**I was standing in the yard** 我正站在院子里——

**when a ragged youngster asked** 一个衣衫褴褛的年轻人走来问，
**if there was a cabby there called Jefferson Hope,** → 这里有没有一个叫杰弗逊·霍普的车夫——

**and said that his cab was wanted by** → 说贝克街221B的一位绅士要用他的车。
**a gentleman at 221B, Baker Street.** →

**I went round, suspecting no harm,** 我走了过去，毫无戒心——

**and the next thing I knew,** → 然后我意识到，
**this young man here had the bracelets on my wrists,** → 眼前这个年轻人已经把手铐扣上了我的手腕——

**and as neatly shackled** 铐得之干净利落，
**as ever I saw in my life.** → 是我一生中见过最漂亮的。

**That's the whole of my story, gentlemen.** 这就是我的故事，各位先生。

**You may consider me to be a murderer;** 你们可以认为我是个杀人犯——

**but I hold** 但我认为，
**that I am just** → 我和你们一样，
**as much an officer of justice as you are."** → 同样是正义的执行者。"

---

**So thrilling had the man's narrative been,** 【倒装强调·心悬着】这个人的陈述是如此扣人心弦——

**and his manner was so impressive** → 而他的神态是如此令人动容——

**that we had sat silent and absorbed.** 【结果落地】以至于我们一直沉默地坐着，全神贯注。

**Even the professional detectives,** 就连那两位职业侦探——

**_blasé_ as they were in every detail of crime,** [插入修饰] 他们是什么样的人？→ 尽管他们对罪案的每个细节都早已司空见惯——

**appeared to be keenly interested in the man's story.** ← 回来接 → 也显然对这个人的故事深感兴趣。

**When he finished we sat** 当他讲完，
**for some minutes in a stillness** → 我们在沉默中坐了几分钟——

**which was only broken by the scratching of Lestrade's pencil** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的沉默？→ 只被雷斯垂德铅笔的沙沙声打破的那种沉默——

**as he gave the finishing touches to his shorthand account.** 当他给他的速记笔录做最后的收尾。

---

**"There is only one point on** "只有一点我还想了解得更多一些，
**which I should like a little more information,"** → "夏洛克·福尔摩斯终于说道。
**Sherlock Holmes said at last.** →

**"Who was your accomplice** "是谁来取我登广告的那枚戒指？
**who came for the ring which I advertised?"** → 你的同伙是谁？"

---

**The prisoner winked at my friend jocosely.** 那囚犯调皮地朝我的朋友眨了眨眼。

**"I can tell my own secrets," he said,** "我只能说我自己的秘密，"他说——

**"but I don't get other people into trouble.** "但我不会让别人陷入麻烦。

**I saw your advertisement,** 我看见了你的广告——

**and I thought it might be a plant,** → 我以为这可能是个圈套——

**or it might be the ring which I wanted.** → 或者那可能就是我想要的戒指。

**My friend volunteered to go and see.** 我的朋友自告奋勇去看个究竟。

**I think you'll own he did it smartly."** 我想你承认，他做得很机灵。"

---

**"Not a doubt of that," said Holmes heartily.** "毫无疑问，"福尔摩斯爽朗地说。

---

**"Now, gentlemen," the Inspector remarked gravely,** "好了，各位先生，"督察严肃地说道——

**"the forms of the law must be complied with.** "法律程序必须遵守。

**On Thursday the prisoner will be brought before the magistrates,** 周四，犯人将被带上治安法庭——

**and your attendance will be required.** → 届时需要你们出席。

**Until then I will be responsible for him."** 在那之前，我负责看管他。"

**He rang the bell as he spoke,** 说话间，他按了铃——

**and Jefferson Hope was led off by a** → 杰弗逊·霍普被两名狱卒带走了—
**couple of warders,** → —

**while my friend** → 而我的朋友和我走出了警察局—
**and I made our way out of the Station** → —

**and took a cab back to Baker Street.** → 叫了辆马车回到贝克街。

---



---

### 第七章 结局
### CHAPTER VII. THE CONCLUSION.

---

**We had all been warned to appear** 我们都被告知周四要出席治安法庭—
**before the magistrates upon the Thursday;** → —

**but when the Thursday came there was no** 【让步·转折·主张落地】然而周四到来时，
**occasion for our testimony.** → 我们的证词已没有出庭的必要。

**A higher Judge had taken the matter in hand,** 一位更高的裁判者已经接手了这件事——

**and Jefferson Hope had been summoned before a tribunal** → 而杰弗逊·霍普已经被传唤到了一个法庭——

**where strict justice would be meted out to him.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么法庭？→ 在那里，严厉的正义将向他施行的那个法庭。

**On the very night after his capture the aneurism burst,** 就在他被捕后的那天夜里，动脉瘤破裂了——

**and he was found in the morning stretched** 早上，他被发现躺倒在囚室的地板上—
**upon the floor of the cell,** → —

**with a placid smile upon his face,** [with-描述状态] 脸上什么表情？→ 脸上带着一抹安详的微笑——

**as though he had been able in his dying moments** 好像他在临终之际——

**to look back upon a useful life,** 回望了一生有意义的事业，
**and on work well done.** → 以及一件做得漂亮的工作。

---

**"Gregson and Lestrade will be wild about his** "格雷格森和雷斯垂德听到他的死讯，
**death," Holmes remarked,** → 一定会抓狂的，"福尔摩斯说道——

**as we chatted it over next evening.** 这是我们第二天傍晚闲聊时说的。

**"Where will their grand advertisement be now?"** "他们那大张旗鼓的功绩现在又算什么？"

---

**"I don't see** →
**that they had very much to do with** →
**his capture," I answered.** → "我看不出他们在逮捕他这件事上有什么大功，"我回答道。

---

**"What you do in this world is a** "你在这个世界上做了什么，毫不重要，
**matter of no consequence," returned my companion, bitterly.** → "我的同伴苦涩地回答道。

**"The question is,** "问题是，
**what can you make people believe** → 你能让人们相信你做了什么。
**that you have done.** →

**Never mind," he continued, more brightly, after a pause.** 算了，"他停顿了一下，继续说道，语气开朗了些。

**"I would not have missed the investigation for anything.** "这个案子的调查，我无论如何都不想错过。

**There has been no better case within my recollection.** 在我的记忆中，没有比这更精彩的案子了。

**Simple as it was,** 尽管它简单，
**there were several most instructive points about it."** → 但其中有几个极具教益的地方。"

---

**"Simple!" I ejaculated.** "简单！"我失声叫道。

---

**"Well, really, it can hardly be described** "嗯，说真的，很难用其他词来形容，
**as otherwise," said Sherlock Holmes,** → "夏洛克·福尔摩斯微笑着看着我的惊讶说道。
**smiling at my surprise.** →

**"The proof of its intrinsic simplicity is,** "它本质上简单的证明在于——

**that without any help save a few very ordinary deductions** 不借助任何帮助，只凭几个极普通的推理——

**I was able to lay my hand upon** 我就能在三天内将罪犯绳之以法。
**the criminal within three days."** → "

---

**"That is true," said I.** "那倒是真的，"我说道。

---

**"I have already explained to you** "我已经向你解释过，
**that what is out of the common** → 不寻常的东西——

**is usually a guide rather than a hindrance.** 通常是引导，而非阻碍。

**In solving a problem of this sort,** 在解决这类问题时——

**the grand thing is to be able to reason backwards.** 最重要的是能够逆向推理。

**That is a very useful accomplishment,** 这是一种非常有用的能力，
**and a very easy one,** → 而且很容易掌握——

**but people do not practise it much.** 【转折】但人们很少练习它。

**In the every-day affairs of life it is** 在日常生活中，
**more useful to reason forwards,** → 正向推理更有用——

**and so the other comes to be neglected.** 【结果】因此逆向推理便被忽视了。

**There are fifty** 能综合推理的人，
**who can reason synthetically** → 是能分析推理的人的五十倍。
**for one who can reason analytically."** → "

---

**"I confess," said I,** "我承认，"我说道，
**"that I do not quite follow you."** → "我不太跟得上你。"

---

**"I hardly expected that you would.** "我几乎料到你会这样。

**Let me see if I can make it clearer.** 让我看看能不能说得更清楚些。

**Most people, if you describe a train of** 大多数人，
**events to them,** → 如果你向他们描述一连串事件——

**will tell you what the result would be.** → 会告诉你结果是什么。

**They can put those events together in their minds,** 他们能把那些事件在脑中组合起来——

**and argue from them that something will come to pass.** → 并由此推断出某件事将要发生。

**There are few people, however,** 然而，很少有人——

**who, if you told them a result,** 如果你告诉他们一个结果——

**would be able to evolve from their own inner consciousness** → 能够从自己的内在意识中推演出——

**what the steps were which led up to that result.** 导致那个结果的各个步骤。

**This power is what I mean** 这种能力就是我所说的逆向推理，
**when I talk of reasoning backwards, or analytically."** → 或者说分析推理。"

---

**"I understand," said I.** "我明白了，"我说道。

---

**"Now this was a case in** "这个案子里，
**which you were given the result** → 你被给予了结果——

**and had to find everything else for yourself.** 而你必须自己找出所有其他的东西。

**Now let me endeavour to show you the** 现在让我来尝试向你展示我推理的各个步骤。
**different steps in my reasoning.** →

**To begin at the beginning.** 从头开始。

**I approached the house, as you know, on foot,** 我走路接近那所房子，你知道的——

**and with my mind entirely free from all impressions.** → 而且脑子里完全没有任何先入之见。

---

**I naturally began by examining the roadway,** 我自然先从检查道路开始——

**and there, as I have already explained to you,** → 在那里，正如我已向你解释过的——

**I saw clearly the marks of a cab,** → 我清楚地看见了马车的痕迹——

**which, I ascertained by inquiry,** [定从-句中插入] 什么痕迹？→ 我通过询问确认，
**must have been there during the night.** → 那痕迹一定是夜间留下的。

**I satisfied myself** 我确认那是辆出租马车，
**that it was a cab** → 而非私人马车——
**and not a private carriage** →

**by the narrow gauge of the wheels.** 依据是车轮的窄轨距。

**The ordinary London growler is considerably less wide** 普通的伦敦四轮马车比绅士的双轮马车要窄得多。
**than a gentleman's brougham.** →

---

**"This was the first point gained.** "这是获得的第一个线索。

**I then walked slowly down the garden path,** 然后我沿着花园小径缓缓走去——

**which happened to be composed of a clay** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的小径？→ 恰好由黏土构成、
**soil, peculiarly suitable for taking impressions.** → 特别适合留下印迹的小径。

**No doubt it appeared to you to be** 在你看来，
**a mere trampled line of slush,** → 那无疑只是一条被踩成泥浆的路迹——

**but to my trained eyes every mark upon** 【转折】但在我受过训练的眼睛看来，
**its surface had a meaning.** → 上面的每一个痕迹都有含义。

---

**There is no branch of detective science** 在侦探科学的各个分支中——

**which is so important and so much neglected** 没有哪个分支既如此重要，又如此被忽视——

**as the art of tracing footsteps.** 像追踪脚印这门技艺那样。

**Happily, I have always laid great stress upon it,** 幸运的是，我一直非常重视它——

**and much practice has made it second nature to me.** → 大量的练习使它成了我的第二本能。

---

**I saw the heavy footmarks of the constables,** 我看见了警察们沉重的脚印——

**but I saw also the track of the two men** → 但我也看见了两个男人的踪迹——

**who had first passed through the garden.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的踪迹？→ 最先穿过花园的那两个人的踪迹。

**It was easy to tell** 很容易判断他们比其他人先到—
**that they had been before the others,** → —

**because in places their marks had been entirely obliterated** 因为在某些地方，他们的痕迹已经完全被盖掉了——

**by the others coming upon the top of them.** 被后来者踩在上面所盖掉的。

---

**In this way my second link was formed,** 就这样，我的第二个线索形成了——

**which told me** [定从-句尾补充] 这个线索告诉了我什么？
**that the nocturnal visitors were two in number,** → 夜间来访者共有两人——

**one remarkable for his height** 一个以身高著称——

**(as I calculated from the length of his stride),** [插入说明] 如何计算出来的？→ 根据他的步幅长度推算的——

**and the other fashionably dressed,** → 另一个穿着时髦——

**to judge from the small** →
**and elegant impression left by his boots.** → 从他靴子留下的小而精致的印迹来判断。

---

**"On entering the house this last inference was confirmed.** "进入房子后，最后这个推断得到了证实。

**My well-booted man lay before me.** 那个穿着考究靴子的人就躺在我眼前。

**The tall one,** 那么，那个高个子就是凶手—
**then, had done the murder,** → —
**if murder there was.** → 如果那是谋杀的话。

**There was no wound upon the dead man's person,** 死者身上没有任何伤口——

**but the agitated expression upon his face** 【转折】但他脸上惊惶的神情——

**assured me that he had foreseen his fate** → 让我确信，
**before it came upon him.** → 他在命运降临之前就预见到了它。

**Men who die from heart disease,** 死于心脏病或任何突发自然原因的人—
**or any sudden natural cause,** → —

**never by any chance exhibit agitation upon their features.** 绝不会在脸上呈现出惊惶的表情。

---

**Having sniffed the dead man's lips** [分词-句首状语] 做了什么之后？→ 嗅了嗅死者的嘴唇之后——

**I detected a slightly sour smell,** 我察觉到一丝轻微的酸味——

**and I came to the conclusion** → 我得出结论，
**that he had had poison forced upon him.** → 他是被强迫服下了毒药。

**Again, I argued that it had been forced upon him** 而且，我推断，之所以是强迫——

**from the hatred and fear expressed upon his face.** 是从他脸上表现出的憎恶和恐惧推断出来的。

**By the method of exclusion,** 通过排除法，
**I had arrived at this result,** → 我得出了这个结论——

**for no other hypothesis would meet the facts.** 【原因】因为没有其他假说能符合所有事实。

---

**Do not imagine** →
**that it was a very unheard of idea.** → 不要以为这是什么闻所未闻的想法。

**The forcible administration of poison is by no** 强制投毒在犯罪史上绝非新鲜事。
**means a new thing in criminal annals.** →

**The cases of Dolsky in Odessa,** 敖德萨的多尔斯基案和蒙彼利埃的勒图里耶案—
**and of Leturier in Montpellier,** → —

**will occur at once to any toxicologist.** 任何毒物学家都会立刻想到。

---

**"And now came the great question** "接下来是关于动机的重大问题。
**as to the reason why.** →

**Robbery had not been the object of the murder,** 抢劫不是谋杀的目的——

**for nothing was taken.** 因为什么都没有被拿走。

**Was it politics, then, or was it a woman?** 那是政治，还是一个女人？

**That was the question which confronted me.** 这就是摆在我面前的问题。

**I was inclined from the first to the latter supposition.** 我从一开始就倾向于后者。

---

**Political assassins are only too glad to do** 政治刺客只会迫不及待地完成任务然后逃跑。
**their work and to fly.** →

**This murder had, on the contrary, been done most deliberately,** 这次谋杀，恰恰相反，是经过深思熟虑的——

**and the perpetrator had left his tracks all** → 凶手在整个房间里留下了他的踪迹—
**over the room,** → —

**showing that he had been there all the time.** [分词-后置修饰] 说明了什么？→ 说明他在那里待了很长时间。

**It must have been a private wrong,** 这一定是私人的冤仇，
**and not a political one,** → 而非政治原因——

**which called for such a methodical revenge.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的冤仇？→ 需要如此有条不紊地复仇的那种冤仇。

---

**When the inscription was discovered upon the wall** 当墙上的文字被发现时——

**I was more inclined than ever to my opinion.** 我比以往任何时候都更坚定了我的判断。

**The thing was too evidently a blind.** 那东西太明显是个幌子了。

**When the ring was found, however, it settled the question.** 然而，当戒指被找到时，问题就彻底明了了。

**Clearly the murderer had used it** 显然，凶手用它——

**to remind his victim of some dead or absent woman.** 来提醒他的受害者想起某个已故或不在场的女人。

---

**It was at this point that I asked Gregson** 正是在这个时候，我问格雷格森——

**whether he had enquired in his telegram to Cleveland** 他在发给克利夫兰的电报里是否询问过——

**as to any particular point in Mr. Drebber's former career.** 关于德雷伯先生过去生涯中某个特别的细节。

**He answered, you remember, in the negative.** 他的回答，你还记得，是否定的。

---

**"I then proceeded to make a careful examination** "然后我进行了对那间房间的仔细检查—
**of the room,** → —

**which confirmed me in my opinion** [定从-句尾补充] 检查结果如何？
**as to the murderer's height,** → 这证实了我对凶手身高的判断——

**and furnished me with the additional details** → 并为我提供了额外的细节——

**as to the Trichinopoly cigar** →
**and the length of his nails.** → 关于特里奇诺波利雪茄和他的指甲长度。

**I had already come to the conclusion,** 我已经得出了结论——

**since there were no signs of a struggle,** 既然没有搏斗的迹象——

**that the blood which covered the floor** 地板上那摊血——

**had burst from the murderer's nose in his excitement.** 是凶手在激动时从鼻子里涌出来的。

**I could perceive** 我能看出，
**that the track of blood coincided with the** → 血迹与他的脚印轨迹重合。
**track of his feet.** →

---

**It is seldom** 一个人很少会，
**that any man,** → 除非他血气旺盛—
**unless he is very full-blooded,** → —

**breaks out in this way through emotion,** 因情绪激动而这样流血——

**so I hazarded the opinion** 【结果】所以我大胆推断——

**that the criminal was probably a robust and ruddy-faced man.** 那个罪犯可能是个体格健壮、面色红润的人。

**Events proved that I had judged correctly.** 事实证明我的判断是正确的。

---

**"Having left the house,** [分词-句首状语] 离开那所房子之后——

**I proceeded to do what Gregson had neglected.** 我做了格雷格森忽略了的事。

**I telegraphed to the head of the police at Cleveland,** 我发电报给克利夫兰的警察局长——

**limiting my enquiry to the circumstances connected with** 把我的询问限定在与伊诺克·德雷伯婚姻有关的情况上。
**the marriage of Enoch Drebber.** →

**The answer was conclusive.** 回答是决定性的。

**It told me** 它告诉我，
**that Drebber had already applied** → 德雷伯已经申请过法律保护—
**for the protection of the law** → —

**against an old rival in love, named Jefferson Hope,** 对抗一个叫杰弗逊·霍普的昔日情敌——

**and that this same Hope was at present in Europe.** → 而这个霍普目前在欧洲。

**I knew now** 我现在知道，
**that I held the clue to the mystery** → 我已经握住了这个谜案的线索—
**in my hand,** → —

**and all that remained was to secure the murderer.** → 剩下的只是抓住凶手了。

---

**"I had already determined in my own mind** "我已经在心里认定——

**that the man** →
**who had walked into the house with Drebber,** → 那个和德雷伯一起走进房子的人—

**was none other than the man** 不是别人，
**who had driven the cab.** → 正是那个驾车的人。

**The marks in the road showed me** 路上的痕迹告诉我——

**that the horse had wandered on in a way** → 那匹马一直在游荡——

**which would have been impossible had there been** 这种情况若有人管着它是不可能的。
**anyone in charge of it.** →

**Where, then, could the driver be,** 那么，驾车人在哪里——

**unless he were inside the house?** 除非他在屋子里？

---

**Again, it is absurd to suppose** 此外，假设这种情况也是荒谬的——

**that any sane man would carry out a deliberate crime** 任何神智正常的人会蓄意犯罪——

**under the very eyes,** 在某个第三者的眼皮底下—
**as it were,** → —
**of a third person,** →

**who was sure to betray him.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么样的第三者？→ 必然会出卖他的那种第三者。

**Lastly, supposing one man wished to dog another through London,** 最后，假设一个人想在伦敦一直跟踪另一个人——

**what better means could he adopt** 他能采取什么更好的手段——

**than to turn cabdriver.** 比当个出租马车车夫更好的手段？

**All these considerations led me to the irresistible conclusion** 所有这些考量把我引向了不可抗拒的结论——

**that Jefferson Hope was to be found among** 杰弗逊·霍普就藏在大都市的马车夫中间。
**the jarveys of the Metropolis.** →

---

**"If he had been one there was no** "如果他曾经是一个马车夫，
**reason to believe** → 就没有理由相信他已经停止了。
**that he had ceased to be.** →

**On the contrary, from his point of view,** 相反，从他的角度来看——

**any sudden change would be likely to draw** 任何突然的改变都可能引起对他的注意。
**attention to himself.** →

**He would, probably,** 他很可能，
**for a time at least,** → 至少在一段时间内，
**continue to perform his duties.** → 会继续履行他的职责。

**There was no reason to suppose** 没有理由认为他在使用化名。
**that he was going under an assumed name.** →

**Why should he change his name in a country** 他为什么要在一个国家里改名——

**where no one knew his original one?** 在那里没有人知道他原来的名字？

---

**I therefore organized my Street Arab detective corps,** 因此，我组织了我的街头流浪儿侦探队——

**and sent them systematically to every cab proprietor in London** → 有条不紊地把他们派到伦敦每一个马车行——

**until they ferreted out the man that I wanted.** 直到他们找出了我要找的人。

**How well they succeeded,** 他们成功得多么漂亮——

**and how quickly I took advantage of it,** → 以及我多么迅速地加以利用——

**are still fresh in your recollection.** 你还记忆犹新。

---

**The murder of Stangerson was an incident** 斯坦格森的死是一个完全出乎意料的事件—
**which was entirely unexpected,** → —

**but which could hardly in any case have been prevented.** 但无论如何几乎都无法避免。

**Through it, as you know,** 通过它，你知道，
**I came into possession of the pills,** → 我获得了那些药片——

**the existence of which I had already surmised.** [定从-句尾补充] 什么药片？→ 我已经猜测其存在的那些药片。

**You see the whole thing is a chain** 你看，
**of logical sequences without a break or flaw."** → 整件事是一连串没有断裂或瑕疵的逻辑推断链。"

---

**"It is wonderful!" I cried.** "太精彩了！"我叫道。

**"Your merits should be publicly recognized.** "你的功绩应该得到公开认可。

**You should publish an account of the case.** 你应该发表关于这个案子的说明。

**If you won't, I will for you."** 如果你不愿意，我替你写。"

---

**"You may do what you like, Doctor," he answered.** "你随便，医生，"他回答道。

**"See here!" he continued,** "你看！"他继续说道，
**handing a paper over to me,** → 把一张报纸递给我，
**"look at this!"** → "看看这个！"

---

**It was the _Echo_ for the day,** 那是当天的《回声报》——

**and the paragraph to** →
**which he pointed was devoted to the case in question.** → 他指着的那段文字正是关于这个案子的。

---

**"The public," it said,** "公众，"报纸说道——

**"have lost a sensational treat** "失去了一场轰动性的盛宴——

**through the sudden death of the man Hope,** 由于霍普这个人的突然死亡——

**who was suspected of the murder of Mr.** 他被怀疑谋杀了伊诺克·德雷伯先生和约瑟夫·斯坦格森先生。
**Enoch Drebber and of Mr. Joseph Stangerson.** →

**The details of the case will probably be** 这个案子的细节现在可能永远无从得知了—
**never known now,** → —

**though we are informed upon good authority** 尽管我们从可靠消息来源得知——

**that the crime was the result of an** 这桩犯罪是一段由来已久的浪漫恩怨的结果—
**old standing and romantic feud,** → —

**in which love and Mormonism bore a part.** 其中爱情和摩门教都扮演了角色。

---

**It seems that both the victims belonged,** 看来两位受害者年轻时都曾属于—
**in their younger days,** → —

**to the Latter Day Saints,** 末世圣徒教——

**and Hope, the deceased prisoner,** 而已故囚犯霍普也来自盐湖城。
**hails also from Salt Lake City.** →

**If the case has had no other effect,** 如果这个案子没有产生其他任何影响——

**it, at least, brings out in the most striking manner** 它至少以最引人注目的方式展现出——

**the efficiency of our detective police force,** 我们侦探警察队伍的效率——

**and will serve as a lesson to all foreigners** → 并将作为警示教训送给所有外国人——

**that they will do wisely to settle their** 让他们明白，
**feuds at home,** → 把恩怨在本国解决才是明智之举——

**and not to carry them on to British soil.** → 而不是把它们带到英国的土地上来。

---

**It is an open secret** 这是公开的秘密——

**that the credit of this smart capture belongs entirely** 这次漂亮逮捕的功劳完全属于——

**to the well-known Scotland Yard officials, Messrs. Lestrade and Gregson.** 苏格兰场的知名官员，雷斯垂德和格雷格森两位先生。

**The man was apprehended, it appears,** 那个人被捕，看来是——

**in the rooms of a certain Mr. Sherlock Holmes,** 在某位名叫夏洛克·福尔摩斯的先生的房间里——

**who has himself,** [定从-句中插入] 他是谁？→ 他本人作为业余爱好者，
**as an amateur,** → 在侦探领域展示出了一些才能的那个人——
**shown some talent in the detective line,** →

**and who, with such instructors,** → 在这样的导师熏陶下，
**may hope in time to attain to some** → 也许终有一天能达到他们一定程度的水准。
**degree of their skill.** →

**It is expected** →
**that a testimonial of some sort will be** → —
**presented to the two officers** → 预计将向这两位官员颁发某种嘉奖—

**as a fitting recognition of their services."** 以此作为对他们功绩的合理认可。"

---

**"Didn't I tell you** "我一开始不就说了吗？
**so when we started?" cried Sherlock Holmes with a laugh.** → "夏洛克·福尔摩斯笑着叫道。

**"That's the result of all our Study in** "这就是我们整个'血字的研究'的结果：
**Scarlet: to get them a testimonial!"** → 给他们挣了个嘉奖！"

---

**"Never mind," I answered,** "没关系，"我回答道——

**"I have all the facts in my journal,** "我的日记里记录了所有的事实——

**and the public shall know them.** → 公众将会知晓一切。

**In the meantime you must make yourself contented** 眼下，你必须让自己感到满足——

**by the consciousness of success,** 靠着对成功的自知——

**like the Roman miser—** 就像那个罗马守财奴一样——

---

**"'Populus me sibilat, at mihi plaudo** "'公众朝我嘘声，但我为自己鼓掌——

**Ipse domi simul ac nummos contemplor in arca.'"** 就在自家，当我独自凝视着箱中的钱财。'"

---

---

—— 全书完 ——

*《血字的研究》第二部分·顺译法处理，完。*

---
